INTRODUCTION

Concentration is the first stage of the Suluk — the spiritual journey of the Inayatiyya. The word Suluk means 'to travel' — not an outer pilgrimage, but the soul's journey from the periphery of consciousness to its luminous center. Concentration is the gathering of scattered attention, the training of the sovereign faculty that makes all other inner work possible.

This handbook is organized in three parts, each preserving the voice and teaching arc of a single instructor:

Part I — Pir Zia Inayat Khan taught Concentration I (C1–C10) across two retreat weekends in September and October 2025. His teachings ground the student in the prayers, breath practices, sensory concentration, and the deep wisdom of the Inayati lineage.

Part II — Urs Qutbuddin Schellenberg taught Concentration II (C11–C20) across two retreat weekends in November and December 2025. His approach centers on the body as vessel, the five elements, and the gentle art of attention.

Part III — Guide Mansur provides personal transmissions outside the classroom — the most intimate layer of the Suluk journey. His prescribed practices, counsel, and wisdom form the daily practice backbone.

The handbook contains 291 teachings extracted from class transcripts, organized into 26 topic chapters across the three parts. Within each part, chapters are organized by topic — Prayers, Practices, Breath, Teachings, Stories, and more — so you always know whose voice you are reading while still being able to find any teaching by subject.

"Concentration is not merely a practice — it is a way of life."

— Pir Zia Inayat Khan

May this handbook serve as a living reference — not a museum of words, but a doorway back into the practices and states from which they arose. Return to it often. The teachings deepen with every reading.

✿

Concentration I · September–October 2025 · 5 Classes · 10 Sessions

Pir Zia Inayat Khan is the spiritual leader of the Inayatiyya and grandson of Hazrat Inayat Khan. He taught Section I of the Concentration program (C1–C10) across two retreat weekends: September 12–14 and October 11–12, 2025.

Weekend 1: September 12–14, 2025 (C1–C6)

Weekend 2: October 11–12, 2025 (C7–C10)

134 Teachings · 9 Chapters

✿
Part I · Chapter 1

PRAYERS & INVOCATIONS

The Sacred Words That Open the Way

Prayer in the Sufi tradition is the soul's conversation with the Divine. Pir Zia taught the foundational prayers of the Inayatiyya — the Invocation, Aman, Saum, Salat, and Salawat — with their physical movements, inner orientations, and progressive layers of meaning across his 10 sessions.

9 Entries · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

✿

Saum and Salat — The Two Daily Prayers

C1 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Two prayers transmitted through Pir-o-Murshid Inayat Khan form the daily foundation of Suluk practice. These are Saum and Salat (also called Salawat). Both involve specific postures, gestures, and words.

The Two Daily Prayers

PrayerMeaning & Addressed ToDescription
**Saum**Repose · Addressed to the One Divine BeingPrayer of repose addressed to the One. Deepens relationship with the divine being.
**Salat / Salawat**Benediction · Addressed to the Light of the RasoolBenediction addressed to the Spirit of Guidance — the first manifested light. Brings travelers closer to each other in the inner worlds.

Important Note on Practice

"These prayers are not intended to displace the prayers of the religion to which you belong, but rather to shine a light that reveals the depths of your faith even more clearly than ever before."
• • •

Salat — Prayer of Benediction

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Distinction Between Salat and Salawat

Salat is the foundation, the form given by Murshid, invoking the light of the prophet — the figure that functions through all the prophets and saints and sages of all time and all space. Here, the beings who are named are fewer.

Salawat — the very name of which suggests a kind of multiplication — we invoke more beings. We recognize that in each dispensation of prophecy, there is a syzygy, a constellation of beings working together. The prophetic impulse is carried by a constellation of historical figures. It's never just one human individual.

"There is more than one version of the pluralized invocation of the multiple figures of multiple syzygies. And we'll have a chance to speak about how we experience these, including male as well as female exemplars."

Salat - Full Text

Most gracious Sovereign,

Messenger, Messiah, and Savior of humanity,

We greet Thee with all humility.

Thou art the First Cause and the Last Effect,

the Divine Light and the Spirit of Guidance,

Alpha and Omega.

Thy Light is in all forms,

Thy Love in all beings:

in a loving mother, in a kind father, in an innocent child,

in a helpful friend, in an inspiring teacher.

Allow us to recognize Thee in all Thy holy names and forms:

as Rama, as Krishna, as Shiva, as Buddha.

Let us know Thee as Abraham, as Solomon, as Zarathushtra,

as Moses, as Jesus, as Muhammad,

and in many other names and forms, known and unknown to the world.

We adore Thy Past,

Thy Presence deeply enlightens our being,

and we look for Thy blessing in the future.

O Messenger, Christ, Nabi, the Rasul of God!

Thou Whose heart constantly reaches upward,

Thou comest on earth with a message,

as a dove from above, when Dharma decays,

and speakest the Word that is put into Thy mouth,

as the light filleth the crescent moon.

Let the star of the Divine Light shining in Thy heart

be reflected in the hearts of Thy devotees.

May the Message of God reach far and wide,

illuminating and making the whole humanity

as one single Family in the Parenthood of God.

Amen.

Additional Teachings

  • Saum — the opening prayer of each session; involves more movements; opening invocation
  • Salat — the closing prayer; simpler form given by Murshid; invokes the light of the Prophet (the spirit of guidance flowing through all prophets, saints, and sages of all times and spaces)
  • Salawat — from the root suggesting multiplication and plurality; invokes more beings — the constellation (syzygy) of illuminated souls in each dispensation of prophecy

Spiritual guidance is never carried by a single individual. In each age, there is a syzygy — a constellation of beings working together to transmit divine wisdom, including male and female exemplars, functioning on subtle levels even today. In Suluk 2025, we begin with the original simplest form of Salat.

Most gracious Sovereign, Messenger, Messiah, and Savior of humanity,

We greet Thee with all humility.

Thou art the First Cause and the Last Effect, the Divine Light and the Spirit of Guidance, Alpha and Omega.

Thy Light is in all forms, Thy Love in all beings: in a loving mother, in a kind father, in an innocent child, in a helpful friend, in an inspiring teacher.

Allow us to recognize Thee in all Thy holy names and forms: as Rama, as Krishna, as Shiva, as Buddha. Let us know Thee as Abraham, as Solomon, as Zarathushtra, as Moses, as Jesus, as Muhammad, and in many other names and forms, known and unknown to the world.

We adore Thy Past, Thy Presence deeply enlightens our being, and we look for Thy blessing in the future.

O Messenger, Christ, Nabi, the Rasul of God! Thou Whose heart constantly reaches upward, Thou comest on earth with a message, as a dove from above, when Dharma decays, and speakest the Word that is put into Thy mouth, as the light filleth the crescent moon.

Let the star of the Divine Light shining in Thy heart be reflected in the hearts of Thy devotees. May the Message of God reach far and wide, illuminating and making the whole humanity as one single Family in the Parenthood of God.

Pir Zia's teaching on the deeper meaning of Salat before closing the session.

"Salat is a practice of giving one's attention to the ONE — the collectivity of beings who serve the furtherance of creation in God's name."

The Divan is the vast network of illuminated beings — of various kinds: Jalali, Jamali, and Kamali; some physically incarnate, most existing on other planes — who work together, each with a particular mission, to advance the disclosure of the divine in creation.

  • Together they manifest the mind of the Spirit of Guidance — the soul of the universe
  • The more we are aware of them and align our lives with their work, the more we participate in that work
  • Sacred knowledge and sacred service go hand in hand

Salat invokes the Spirit of Guidance as Alpha and Omega — first and culmination of creation — and then affirms how the light of the universe manifests through human expressions: loving mother, kind father, innocent child, helpful friend, inspiring teacher — and most emphatically, in those beings who become the path itself.

Salat acknowledges 180,000 prophets — impossible to name all — as an image of the vast network of sacred service. Names open into syzygies (constellations of beings), which are mutually interrelated, linking unnamed syzygies, comprising the circuitry of a vast luminous mind. This cosmological vision is implicit in every recitation of Salat.

"Sacred knowledge is given to those who are sworn to sacred service — to go hand in hand."

"Those beings who, in following the path, become the path, become expressions of the path, become guides on the path — and every culture knows their names because those names are remembered with reverence."

• • •

Amān — The Prayer of Sanctuary

C3 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Aman is not one of the 99 Names of God — it is a mantric word expressing a deep aspiration. Murshid gave it specifically for times of extreme suffering, calamity, and communal pain in the world.

Aman vs Fazal

Fazal — a universal practice of blessing; creates an atmosphere of benediction and positive vibration; used regularly.

Aman — more specific; invoked when witnessing great calamities, communities experiencing extreme harm, deprivation, and suffering.

What Aman Affirms

  • We witness suffering without turning away — refusing to insulate ourselves from the pain of others.
  • We stand in solidarity with all who suffer, treating every life as precious and sacred.
  • We commit to justice, healing, and transformation — not as abstraction, but as living intention.
  • Whatever happens to one being happens to all of us spiritually — we are one human family.
  • Prevents spiritual numbness — keeps the heart awake to the world's condition.
  • Music supports the practice by uplifting and attuning the heart to compassion.

Key Teachings

"We wish to be part of a transformation that heals these insufferable wounds, that mends the breaches, that doesn't allow any life to be disregarded as less than precious."

"Whatever we do, bring our heart to it."

"We want to witness what others are going through, we don't want to turn away from it, we want to be in solidarity, and we take it very seriously."

Additional Teachings

Each day of Suluk begins with the prayer Amān — acknowledging that all is not well in the world, that there is great suffering, violence, and injustice in our time. Amān is the prayer that holds the earth's heartbreak with compassion before turning toward the divine.

This prayer serves as a bridge between worldly awareness and divine connection, honoring the reality of suffering while seeking divine protection and guidance.

• • •

Prayer of the Artificer — Blessing Devices

C3 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Practice

Our devices (computers, phones) are vibrationally near to our aura and consciousness. They are made of metallic ores from the earth, shaped by generations of human ingenuity — and can be regarded as having spiritual quality.

The Prayer

Place fingertips on the device and recite:

"Oh, Artificer of the heavens and the earth, bless this artifact. Shower it with Thy love and light, and let it glorify Thy holy name. Amen."

Understanding

Our homes and devices become extensions of ourselves, imbued with our thoughts and intentions — and can be treated as mirrors of our consciousness.

The internet is a mirror of the human condition — full of troubled impressions and unawakened impulses. Rather than fleeing it, the path calls us to meet it wisely and transformatively, navigating it with awareness.

• • •

Saum — Prayer of Repose

C5 · September 14, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Pir Zia gave line-by-line commentary on the Saum prayer, illuminating the meaning of each phrase. The prayer can be performed with or without movements; the movements make it embodied.

Full Text of Saum

Praise be to Thee, Most Supreme God,

Omnipotent, Omnipresent, All-pervading, the Only Being.

Take us in Thy Parental Arms, Raise us from the denseness of the earth.

Thy Beauty do we worship, To Thee do we give willing surrender.

Most Merciful and Compassionate God, The Idealized Sovereign of the whole humanity,

Thee only do we worship, and toward Thee alone do we aspire.

Open our hearts toward Thy Beauty, Illuminate our souls with Divine Light.

O Thou, the Perfection of Love, Harmony, and Beauty!

All-powerful Creator, Sustainer, Judge, and Forgiver of our shortcomings,

Sovereign God of the East and of the West, of the worlds above and below,

And of the seen and unseen beings.

Pour upon us Thy Love and Thy Light,

Give sustenance to our bodies, hearts, and souls,

Use us for the purpose that Thy Wisdom chooseth,

And guide us on the path of Thine Own Goodness.

Draw us closer to Thee every moment of our life,

Until in us be reflected Thy Grace, Thy Glory, Thy Wisdom, Thy Joy, and Thy Peace. Amen.

Line-by-Line Commentary

"Praise be to Thee, Most Supreme God"

The first gesture opens the chest — a physical act of glorification, not intellectual. Gather all impulses of thankfulness and adulation from throughout your life and offer them in the most universal, unbounded terms. We were born for this.

"We were born for this — born for glorification, and in the absence of it, we desiccate, we dry out, become brittle."

"The praise that we offer to the One comes from the One, returns to the One, flows through all things."

"Omnipotent, Omnipresent, All-pervading, the Only Being"

Omnipotent — all energy in the universe is endlessly transferred and ricochets through the cosmos; all emanations of one Kudrat (power/nature). This is the one's constant expression.

Omnipresent — not far away; closer to us than we are to ourselves; equally close to someone on the other side of the world.

All-pervading — not confined to spirit or matter; ubiquitous throughout the entirety of the tricosm.

"Take us in Thy Parental Arms"

Parental arms are a code for nurturance itself, love itself — invoking our first experience of being held. Not sentimental but deeply cosmic — the embrace of the soul by its Source.

"Parental arms are a code for nurturance itself, love itself."

"Raise us from the denseness of the earth"

Not a rejection of material existence — a call to remember the subtle while living in the dense. We have undergone incarnation from sheer spiritual light, through the imaginative self (nafs), into physical form. Too often we suffer forgetfulness and become alienated from the formless dimension of our being. This prayer calls us to reintegrate all levels.

"Through an imaginative form, the soul began to think itself. And in the process, too often we've suffered forgetfulness — we've become alienated from the formless dimension of our being."

"Thy Beauty do we worship — To Thee do we give willing surrender"

All surrender to beauty willingly and to power unwillingly. The surrender evoked here is chosen — moved by the splendor and meaningfulness of the divine. This is the surrender of beauty.

"All surrender to beauty willingly and to power unwillingly. Unwilling surrender is disgrace, is humiliation, a violation of our freedom. But that surrender which is chosen — because one is moved by the splendor — that is the surrender of beauty."

"Most Merciful and Compassionate God (Rahman and Rahim)"

These two attributes signify the primal motive of creation itself. Mercy (Rahman) — the outpouring of existence. Compassion (Rahim) — the nurturing care that sustains it.

"This whole world could have had no other cause, no other motive force, than that of mercy and compassion."

"The Idealized Sovereign of the whole humanity"

None of us can see the Divine as it is — it would be like looking into the sun. Instead, we each look into the lake of our heart and find the reflection particular to our own need and aspiration. The Divine ideal is mirrored uniquely in each heart.

"We each look into the lake of our heart to seek your reflection — and the reflection that meets us there is our own highest vision of truth."

After the Prayer

After every practice, linger with what has arisen. The radiance, the atmosphere, the silence that follows is just as valuable as the practice itself.

"What comes at the end of the prayer is just as valuable — the radiance, the atmosphere, the silence — just as valuable as what is happening during the practice."

Additional Teachings

"Find the place of your strength — and then offer your obeisance."

  1. Palms forward — releasing weight from the shoulders, opening the chest, letting air in. "Praise be to the most supreme God."
  1. Hands draw closer together — "Omnipotent, omnipresent, all-pervading."
  1. Hands come down to sides — "The Only Being. Take us in Thy parental arms."
  1. Bend forward, hands on knees — "Raise us from the denseness of the earth."
  1. Rise, then lean forward with palms extended toward the ground — "The only do we worship. Toward the alone do we aspire."
  1. Hands together at waist — "Most merciful and compassionate God, the idealized sovereign of the whole humanity."
  1. Open the heart center (Qalb) — "Open our hearts toward Thy beauty. Illuminate our souls with divine light."
  1. The Qalb-Ruh connection, then Khafi-Nafs connection — invoking the subtle anatomy.
  1. Final surrender — "Pour upon us Thy love and Thy light... Draw us closer to Thee every moment of our life until in us be reflected Thy grace, Thy glory, Thy wisdom, Thy joy and Thy peace. Amen."

Pir Zia mentions that there are two versions of the Saum prayer:

  1. Standing version — the version practiced in these classes, where the prostration is performed "in the air" with a bow while standing
  2. Prostrating version — where "one is going right down onto the ground and prostrating with your forehead"

"Thy beauty do we worship — now that the hands are forward, palms facing the ground. There's another version of Saum in which one is going right down onto the ground and prostrating with your forehead. We're doing the standing version for now. So even the prostrating is just in the air. Thy beauty do we worship. To thee do we give willing surrender."

The prostration — whether standing or full — enacts a surrender to divine beauty:

"All surrender to beauty willingly and to power unwillingly. But as we're bowing down, it's the beauty of the divine that's eliciting our found surrender."

"Unwilling surrender is disgrace, it's humiliation, it's a violation of our freedom. But that surrender which is chosen, and it's chosen because one is moved by the splendor, by the meaningfulness of what sweeps you up and brings you back to the truth of it all, that is the surrender of beauty."

• • •

The Invocation

C5 · September 14, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Toward the One, the Perfection of Love, Harmony, and Beauty, the Only Being, United with all the Illuminated Souls Who form the Embodiment of the Messenger, the Spirit of Guidance.

Pir Zia gave an extended teaching on the meaning of each phrase of the Invocation.

Turning Toward the One

The Invocation turns attention toward the Oneness that excludes nothing — everywhere, always. It names three qualities that naturally align us with this Oneness:

Love — self-overcoming devotion; the melting away of self-regard in encounter with what lifts consciousness to its highest awareness.

Harmony — when self and other exist, they discover a music of unfolding melodies and relationships, not static but alive.

Beauty — what is born of love and harmony; mysterious and yet intimately present; spellbinding and transformative.

"The ways of being that naturally bring us closest to the oneness are the qualities of love, harmony, and beauty."

Nature of the Soul — All Souls Are Luminous

The phrase "United with all the illuminated souls" does not mean only some souls are illuminated. Every soul is light by essence — already luminous. Awakening is the process of coming to terms with this truth, embodying it, and enacting it.

"The soul itself is light. All souls are luminous and illuminated. Awakening is the process of coming to terms with this, embodying it, enacting it."

Awakening as Companionship

Turning toward the One is not an isolated act — it puts us in the company of all beings on all planes who are awakening. We are inspired by those who have awakened and transmitted this reality; together all beings are advancing toward this realization, each at a different juncture.

The Rasool — The Messenger

The Divan of Bodhisattvas, prophets, saints, and sages — past, present, and future, on all planes — forms the embodiment of the Messenger. Each has a particular gift and work, but the common ground is Awakening itself, wakefulness, and the glorification of the divine.

  • The Rasool embodies the soul, mind, and body of the universe — together as a tricosm
  • The Rasool is the mirror in which the Divine Being beholds Divinity's own face
  • The common ground among all prophets, saints, sages, and bodhisattvas is Awakening itself

"Each bodhisattva has a particular gift and a particular work, but there is a common ground which is universally shared, which is Awakening itself."

"The messenger embodying the spirit of guidance — the mirror in which the Divine Being beholds Divinity's own face."

Additional Teachings

"The Spirit of Guidance is the first of creation, the cosmic being — the mirror of the Absolute."

The Invocation first invokes the One Being — the absolute — and then evokes the light of guidance that is the essence of creation. There is a soul of souls, a mind of minds, a body of bodies: not the infinite absolute itself, but the wholeness composed of all souls, all minds, all bodies — the cosmic being that is the first of creation and the mirror of the absolute.

The criterion for right from wrong is the wholeness of the cosmic being — in whom all poles are balanced and every individual has a place within the totality. The Spirit of Guidance is personified in those human beings who awaken to life's purpose, work together, serve, and advance the ongoing revelation of the divine in creation.

"There's a soul of souls, a mind of minds, a body of bodies — still created, still ephemeral, not the infinite one that is all and everything, but rather the essence of creation."

We say the Invocation to crystallize this vision — to orient ourselves at the start of each session toward the absolute and the soul of creation.

Morning Practice: Pir Zia recommends saying the invocation when you wake up — so the very first idea, the very first words that come from your mouth consist of this orientation to the absolute and to the soul of creation.

• • •

Khatum — The Closing Prayer

C6 · September 14, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

All Suluk gatherings close with the Khatum — a prayer of gratitude toward everyone visible and invisible who has enabled the work, ultimately toward the One beyond all names and forms.

O Thou, Who art the Perfection of Love, Harmony, and Beauty,

The Sovereign of heaven and earth,

open our hearts, that we may hear Thy Voice,

which constantly cometh from within.

Disclose to us Thy Divine Light,

which is hidden in our souls,

that we may know and understand life better.

Most Merciful and Compassionate God,

give us Thy great Goodness,

Teach us Thy loving Forgiveness,

Raise us above the distinctions and differences which divide us,

Send us the Peace of Thy Divine Spirit,

And unite us all in Thy Perfect Being.

Amen.

Additional Teachings

O Thou,

Who art the Perfection of Love, Harmony, and Beauty,

The Sovereign of heaven and earth,

open our hearts, that we may hear Thy Voice,

which constantly cometh from within.

Disclose to us Thy Divine Light,

which is hidden in our souls,

that we may know and understand life better.

Most Merciful and Compassionate God,

give us Thy great Goodness,

Teach us Thy loving Forgiveness,

Raise us above the distinctions and differences which divide us,

Send us the Peace of Thy Divine Spirit,

And unite us all in Thy Perfect Being.

Amen.

• • •

The Amen Gesture - Physical Cascade Practice

C7 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

At the end of the daily prayers, we always say Amen and lift our hands as if to take the whole sum of resonance that has emerged in the prayer. You take it into your hands as in a vessel and lift it up over your head and pour it down as a cascade.

The cascade washes over the body in sequence:

  • Face
  • Neck
  • Shoulders
  • Chest

The accumulated resonance of the entire prayer is physically received through this gesture.

Understanding Amen

The word Amen is shared across the three Abrahamic traditions: Amin (Judaism), Amen (Christianity), Ameen (Islam) — the same root, the same word.

"It comes from the same root as the word Aman that we just intoned. It's related to the word Amana — the Covenant. It bespeaks faithfully upholding a trust, respecting a covenant older than time, a fundamental agreement between ourselves and the Absolute."

You'll notice that the syllables themselves have an effect — the vibrational impact of Amen is experiential, not merely semantic.

• • •

Salawat — The Complete Form

C10 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The class rose and the full Salawat was offered — the gender-inclusive prayer of the Inayatiyya, naming the divine through feminine and masculine sacred figures across all traditions.

Salawat

Most gracious Sovereign,

Messenger, Messiah, and Savior of humanity,

we greet Thee with all humility.

Thou art the First Cause and the Last Effect,

the Divine Light and the Spirit of Guidance,

Alpha and Omega.

Thy Light is in all forms,

Thy Love in all beings:

in a loving mother, in a kind father, in an innocent child,

in a helpful friend, in an inspiring teacher.

Allow us to recognize Thee in all Thy holy names and forms:

as Sita and Rama, as Radha and Krishna,

as Parvati and Shiva, as Tara and Buddha.

Let us know Thee as Sarah, Hagar, and Abraham,

as Deborah and Solomon, as Anahita and Zarathustra,

as Asiya, Aaron, Maryam and Moses,

as Mary and Jesus, Khadija and Muhammad,

and in many other names and forms, known and unknown to the world.

We adore Thy Past,

Thy Presence deeply enlightens our being,

and we look for Thy blessing in the future.

O Messenger, Christ, Nabi, the Rasul of God!

Thou Whose heart constantly reaches upward,

Thou comest on earth with a message,

as a dove from above, when Dharma decays,

and speakest the Word that is put into Thy mouth,

as the light filleth the crescent moon.

Let the star of the Divine Light shining in Thy heart

be reflected in the hearts of Thy devotees.

May the Message of God reach far and wide,

illuminating and making the whole humanity

as one single family in the Parenthood of God.

Amen.

Murshid's Closing Prayer

"Thou art the perfection of love, harmony, and beauty. The liege of heaven and earth."

"Open our hearts that we may hear thy voice, which constantly cometh from within."

"Disclose to us thy divine light, which is hidden in our souls, that we may know and understand life better."

"Most merciful and compassionate God, give us thy great goodness, teach us thy loving forgiveness, raise us above the distinctions and differences which divide us."

"Send us the peace of thy divine spirit and unite us all. Thy perfect being."

Closing Blessing — Pir Zia

May your heart be filled with heavenly joy.

May your soul be illuminated with divine light.

May your spirit unfold the divine message.

May you go on in the spiritual path.

May God's peace abide with you. Forever and evermore.

Amen.

Additional Teachings

Pir Zia explains: "Salawat is an expansion of the original form [Salat] in which some of the syzygy, some of the constellations of beings who stood at the center of the dispensation of a wave of prophetic revelation at various times and places in history — that these beings are mentioned."

Syzygy = celestial alignment — constellations of sacred beings at the center of each wave of prophetic light.

Most gracious Sovereign,

Messenger, Messiah, and Savior of humanity,

we greet Thee with all humility.

Thou art the First Cause and the Last Effect,

the Divine Light and the Spirit of Guidance,

Alpha and Omega.

Thy Light is in all forms,

Thy Love in all beings:

in a loving mother, in a kind father, in an innocent child,

in a helpful friend, in an inspiring teacher.

Allow us to recognize Thee in all Thy holy names and forms:

as Sita and Rama, as Radha and Krishna,

as Parvati and Shiva, as Tara and Buddha.

Let us know Thee as Sarah, Hagar, and Abraham,

as Deborah and Solomon, as Anahita and Zarathustra,

as Asiya, Aaron, Maryam and Moses,

as Mary and Jesus, Khadija and Muhammad,

and in many other names and forms, known and unknown to the world.

We adore Thy Past,

Thy Presence deeply enlightens our being,

and we look for Thy blessing in the future.

O Messenger, Christ, Nabi, the Rasul of God!

Thou Whose heart constantly reaches upward,

Thou comest on earth with a message,

as a dove from above, when Dharma decays,

and speakest the Word that is put into Thy mouth,

as the light filleth the crescent moon.

Let the star of the Divine Light shining in Thy heart

be reflected in the hearts of Thy devotees.

May the Message of God reach far and wide,

illuminating and making the whole humanity

as one single family in the Parenthood of God.

Part I · Chapter 2

CHIVALRIC RULES & IRON RULES

The Ethical Foundation of the Path

The Chivalric Rules and Iron Rules form the moral skeleton of the Suluk journey. Pir Zia introduced these rules as mirrors for self-refinement — each one revealing a subtler layer of the ego's tendency and the soul's aspiration.

6 Entries · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

✿

The Chivalric Rules Overview and Rule 1 - Make No False Claims

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Overview of the 40 Rules

40 rules over 40 days: 10 Iron, 10 Copper, 10 Silver, 10 Golden. Each rule is a choice, not an obligation.

"These rules are yours to pledge yourself to when and if the rule lights up your conscience. No one is enforcing these ways of being. The rules consist of reminders of possibilities which, if we choose to pledge to them, will remind us in times when we might be likely to become distracted."

"Each rule is a prism, a magnifying glass, for investigating how we truly wish to live — and then living it."

Rule 1: My Conscientious Self, Make No False Claims

"My conscientious self, make no false claims."

Personal Reflection

"You could just look back over the last week or so. Is there something that you might have said — and now you look back and you see: why did I say that, it wasn't really true? Just said it. It seemed the easiest thing to say, or some part of me wanted to make a good impression."

Application
  • The rule doesn't require saying harsh things — staying discreetly quiet is always an option
  • It does mean always speaking in sincere accordance with all that one knows
  • Consider the "cost to the light of your own integrity — that pure transparency that is available to you when you are aligned, when your speech actually lines up with your true experience of reality."

The Pledge Ritual

"I'm going to say the rule once, and we're going to close our eyes. No one is looking at anyone else. And then if you've come to the decision that you'd like to take this on — then the second time I say it, you say it too. You join your voice with mine. And if you feel you're not sure that you want to make that commitment, then it's just fine. Just don't say it and just listen and take it into your own reflection."

"Those commitments that truly do represent your ideal and which move you and which you know will bring into blossom with greater fullness who you truly are — making that commitment is a very powerful thing."

• • •

The Chivalric Rules and Day 1 Rule

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Chivalric Rules are a daily spiritual and ethical practice for the 40 days of Suluk. There are 40 rules in four categories of 10 each: Iron Rules, Copper Rules, Silver Rules, and Golden Rules.

Nature of the Rules

  • Not about obedience — each rule is a choice, a personal pledge, not an external imposition
  • Each rule is a prism — a magnifying glass to investigate how one truly wishes to live
  • The purpose — to unite our ideals with our day-to-day way of being
  • Rules begin with "My conscientious self" — no one is imposing; one is inviting oneself

The Rule for C2 — Day 1

"My conscientious self, make no false claims."

This rule concerns authenticity in speech: how we represent ourselves and reality to others. It is a commitment to speak truthfully, sincerely, and honestly — not to say what is not true, even for short-term personal benefit or convenience.

Guidelines
  • Silence is always an option — the rule does not require harshness, only the absence of untruth
  • Applies only to oneself — we are not involved in anyone else's decisions
  • Even non-adoption becomes a contemplation — what are the circumstances where untruth seems justified?
  • The cost of false claims — even when no one is harmed, there is a cost to the light of one's own integrity
How the Rule is Received

The rule is received communally: Pir Zia says it once with eyes closed; those who choose to pledge join their voice the second time. Those who are uncertain simply listen and reflect.

• • •

Iron Rule 2 - Speak Not Against Others in Their Absence

C3 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

"My conscientious self, speak not against others in their absence."

This rule addresses the common tendency to make critical or mocking remarks about someone when they are not present — reasoning that "no harm is done" since they cannot hear. Pir Zia dismantled this reasoning:

Why This Rule Matters

  • We are all interconnected — thoughts and words carry vibrations that reach others even across distance, consciously or not.
  • Beneath the visible surface, life is a web of pulsing vibrations. When we think harshly of someone and verbalize it, it is heard one way or another.
  • The keyword is "against" — not all speech about others is forbidden, but speech that diminishes, mocks, or criticizes in ways one would not say in their presence.

The Criterion

"If we're going to speak about someone, is it possible to imagine them in the room and think of them as a soul as well as a body — and then speak?"

"How would you speak about someone in the presence, not only of that person, but of the human being who is the exemplar of your highest ideals — and in the presence of all the bodhisattvas, and in the awareness of the divine immanence?"

Nuance in Professional Contexts

In positions of responsibility, addressing problematic behavior involving colleagues — sometimes confidentially — may be necessary. This rule does not prohibit that. It calls for clarity, dignity, and mindfulness: free of unnecessary negativity or surplus sentiment, speaking as one would speak in the person's presence.

The Spirit of the Rule

  • Not a prohibition only — each rule is a contemplation, an invitation to refined ethical attention.
  • Naturalness and consideration are not opposites — speak with friends, be merry, speak of life, but with a wakeful heart.
  • Speak with recognition of the divinity in every human being.

Inspiration from Noor-un-Nisa

Noor-un-Nisa Inayat Khan's saying, recalled by her friend Jeanne Overton Fuller:

"I never speak ill of a flower for fear of offending the fairy that is doing its best to make the flower beautiful."

• • •

Iron Rule 3 - Do Not Take Advantage of Ignorance

C5 · September 14, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

"My conscientious self, do not take advantage of a person's ignorance."

The first two rules relate to speech: make no false claims (Rule 1), and speak not against others in their absence (Rule 2). A person might take refuge from both by simply staying silent. But silence is not always the ethical position.

When Transparency is Required

If you are trading or selling something and know a salient fact the other person would need in order to make an informed decision — staying silent is itself a form of deception. If they would not have made the transaction knowing this fact, they must be told.

  • Transparency and fairness in all dealings
  • Truth will eventually be revealed — attempts to conceal are ultimately futile
  • The rule is a reminder to be forthcoming, transparent, and fair, not merely to avoid outright lies

"Everything's eventually going to come to light — whether it's in this world or in the next world, it doesn't matter. So trying to hide a relevant fact... there's going to be a reckoning sooner or later."

The Power of Commitment

These rules may seem obvious. But that is precisely the point — taking up a rule and practicing it magnifies our choices in a way we might otherwise overlook. Making a commitment to what we already know is right is a very powerful act.

"Taking up the rule, practicing it, magnifies our choices in a way that otherwise we might overlook. Things that are self-evident — making a commitment to them is a very powerful thing."

• • •

The Fourth Iron Rule - Do Not Boast of Your Good Deeds

C7 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

"My conscientious self, do not boast of your good deeds."

These rules are really contemplations. They're opportunities for reflection rather than merely do's and don'ts.

Learning from All — Everyone is a Teacher

"We can find the path of beauty by studying the beauty shown to us in the way of life of those who inspire us. And when a way of being is not so beautiful — there too is a lesson. Instead of blaming a person or succumbing to alienation, we could simply see that in their various ways of being, people are teaching us many things. We have many teachers. Everyone is a teacher."

When Deeds Lose Their Glow

When someone performs a genuinely inspiring act and then claims credit for it, the beauty diminishes:

"The deed seems to lose its glow. One isn't so very moved anymore. Whereas that which was done and forgotten, done and left unheralded — it retains a place in our heart. There's a greater elegance in it because it was understated. The action spoke for itself. It didn't need magnifying."

Reflective Questions
  • Why is it that one feels the need to call attention to one's actions?
  • Whose approval are we seeking?
  • And even if one gains the attention of any number of people — what naturalness is lost? What simplicity is lost?

The Omniscient Witness

"That which is widely observed in the world is unheeded by the angels, and that which no one in the world notices, the angels notice."

"When God is the omniscient, omnipresent witness — who else do we need to inform of our actions and intentions?"

"All is already understood from first to last. And when we understand this, we can relax in a certain way. This approval-seeking, this attention-seeking, can relax. There's no one to impress."

"Give so that the left hand doesn't know what the right hand has given."

• • •

The Fifth Iron Rule - Do Not Claim What Belongs to Another

C9 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

"My conscientious self, do not claim that which belongs to another."

"These rules, these contemplations can be understood on more than one level."

Level 1 — Material Ownership

The obvious level: something is yours only if you were given it, inherited it, purchased it fairly, found it ownerless, or created it yourself. Otherwise — do not claim it. It belongs to another. It would be theft.

  • Given / inherited / purchased fairly → yours
  • Found with no owner → yours
  • Created by you → yours
  • None of the above → not yours — do not arrogate it

Level 2 — Ownership of Ideas, Teachings, Experience

"How do you know what really belongs to you — in your mind, in your heart? It becomes a living question."

"Just repeating what someone else has said or what someone else has done doesn't seem to suffice. It's not yours — at least not yet."

"Is there a way of living it, of being it, of embodying it, of enacting it? That means you're not just latching on to someone else's experience — you've found your own experience of something, you're really living it."

"It's one thing to be attracted by something interesting, something inspiring, and to identify with it, to quote it, and to associate with it. But is it yours?"

"It can only be yours when you own it, when you stand for it, when it effervesces in the cells of your skin."

What We Take With Us

"At the moment that we leave this world, the material objects that we've collected — we won't be able to take them with us. They will end up with a relative or sold at a thrift store."

"What will be ours on that day? What will we take with us? Only that which we've taken into our hearts. And nothing else can be claimed."

"Claims are notoriously dubious. Making assertions, making pronouncements — just because one argues something doesn't make it real. What is real? How we live. How we love."

The Commitment — Two Levels

The commitment operates at two levels:

  1. Material: not taking anything that isn't yours; being absolutely punctilious in all dealings
  2. Deeper: being very careful about any kind of assertion — whether verbally or internally — and instead living in the ownership of what is immediately your own felt, tasted apperception of being
✿ ✿ ✿
Part I · Chapter 3

BREATH PRACTICES

The Bridge Between Worlds

Breath is the medium through which the soul touches the body and the body touches the soul. Pir Zia taught the soles-breathing practice, the Nazar Par Kadam principle, and the foundational breath teachings across his sessions.

5 Entries · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

✿

Rightful Breathing Practice

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Pir Zia led a guided breathing practice with these instructions:

Instructions

  1. Sit upright — shoulders open and relaxed, spine elongated naturally, tailbone rooted to earth, crown lifted to sky
  1. Let the breath enter without forcing — observe its flow through the nostrils, down the windpipe, filling the lungs and bloodstream
  1. Do not be in a hurry to exhale — give the whole process its natural time
  1. Observe the exhalation as expansion — the exhaled breath disperses into the atmosphere; the inhalation as contraction — surrounding air spirals inward, penetrating the cells
  1. Let all muscles, tendons, and bones yield to this flow — without collapsing — to maximize refreshment, invigoration, calm energy, and clarity

Key Insight

The chest and belly expand with inhalation and contract with exhalation, while the "aerial body" of breath moves in the opposite direction — a vortex flowing in and out.

• • •

The Invisible Rain - Full Body Breath Practice

C3 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Pir Zia led a guided breath practice using the image of invisible rain — a subtle, continuous flow streaming through the sky, entering through every pore.

The Practice Steps

  1. Invisible Rain Visualization — sense a subtle rain always falling, flowing into you through all pores, the body opening to receive it.
  1. Breath Awareness — feel a wave coming in with each inhalation; guide breath down the windpipe, filling the lungs.
  1. Postural Alignment — adjust every vertebra, rib, and muscle gently; find spaciousness without rigidity.
  1. Full-Body Breath — sense the breath traveling down the arms, through the hips and thighs, into the feet, up through the neck, head, and scalp.
  1. Cellular Awareness — recognize the body as a vast congregation of cells, floating, humming, thirsting for breath.
  1. Quenching — feel the thirst of each cell satisfied by the inhalation, cascading right down to the tips of the toes.
  1. Exhalation as Communion — the cells release what is superfluous to this body, but thirsted for by the green beings — trees, algae, plants. We breathe in concert with all plant life.

Key Imagery

"Each inhalation cascading through the body right down to the tips of the toes, satisfying a deep thirst."

"In this communion, in this participation, breath by breath, there is joy for the cells, and peace, and an inkling of the oneness of all being."

Connection to Daily Life

Breath shares the characteristics of water — it flows and moves in tides, waves, ripples, and surges.

• • •

Purification Breathing Practice with Emotional Stages

C7 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Posture & Awareness

  • Sit upright — shoulders open, chest open, eyes closed
  • Watch the belly rise and fall; observe the ribs expand on the sides

Exhalation — Releasing Murkiness

"As you breathe out, let the breath go all the way out, gradually rolling out into the distance, like a long carpet unrolling."

"As you exhale, you're aware of the dust that is flowing out on your exhalation — there's a certain murkiness in the exhalation, a certain opacity. It's not entirely transparent. But you let that murkiness filter out, let it dissipate."

Emotional dimension of release: "And it's a relief to let it go. At first when you see it, it might be startling because you didn't realize it was in you — but now you're just happy that it's resolving."

Inhalation — Influx of Radiance

"Let the incoming breath fill you, pervade you, reaching right down into every cell — as far as the tips of your toes."

The Sponge Analogy

"If you would rub a dusty surface with a sponge, the grime would fill the sponge, and then if you would squeeze the sponge in water, the water would become murky."

The body-mind is that sponge. Each exhalation squeezes out what is heavy or clouded. The murky water = impurities being released.

Stages of Purification — Progressive

  1. Murkiness visible on breath — a signal it is departing: 'The very fact that you see it on the breath means that it's departing.'
  2. Murkiness decreasing: 'The more that you squeeze a sponge, the less dust comes out of it.'
  3. Clear channel: 'It's just breath itself that's going out. Just a clear channel.'
  4. Emergence of radiance: 'There's a definite light in the breath, a glow.'

"This wakeful breath is a form of purification — we're washing ourselves."

• • •

The Elemental Purification Ritual

C9 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Step 1 — Discern the Elemental Character

"Since the character of the burden that you're holding — is it earthy? Is it gritty? Like sand and stone? Or is it aqueous? Is it damp? Perhaps it's fiery — it's hot to the touch. Blistering. Or is it aerial? As light as a breeze and yet heavier than anything else."

  • Earth — earthy, gritty, like sand and stone
  • Water — aqueous, damp
  • Fire — hot to the touch, blistering
  • Air — as light as a breeze and yet heavier than anything else

Identify the elemental quality and then go to that element in nature to perform the transmutation.

🌿 EARTH — Burial

  1. Go to a place and ask its permission — address the spirit of the place: 'Will you receive and break down, transform this piece of energy I've been carrying?'
  2. If there is no assent, respect the answer and find another place until you find the place that will accept it
  3. Dig a hole. Give the energetic imprint — that charge, that impression — into a form already on the brink of dissolution. Something ready to rot into the earth: an autumn leaf, whatever form is willing to partner in the transmutation
  4. Bury it. Cover the whole with earth. Feel with conviction: you have finished something, you have ended something
  5. Walk away. Do not turn and look back

🌊 WATER — Pouring

  1. Go to a stream or the seashore. Bring a little portion of water willing to carry with it what you are letting go
  2. Go to a place where the assent is there
  3. Pour it out — into the stream, into the ocean — to be washed, dissolved, and swept away on the current
  4. Walk away. Do not look back

🔥 FIRE — Burning

  1. Inscribe the impression in some form on a bit of paper — a word, words, a symbol, or any rendering. The inscription could even be entirely by way of concentration
  2. The impression is given over to the paper
  3. Build a fire when it is there and willing to receive it
  4. GREAT VIGILANCE IS NEEDED: take great care that your clothing and hair are protected
  5. With vigilance and care, give this impression over to the fire. Let it burn away, then let the fire burn down
  6. Ensure it is fully extinguished
  7. The matter is finished. Do not look back

🌬️ AIR — Release into Wind

  1. On a windy day, perhaps on a hilltop — find permission
  2. Give the impression to something very light: like the seeds of a dandelion — something you can cast into the wind to be swept away
  3. Let it go into the current of the wind. Let it be swept into the sky and dissolved into the vast blue
  4. Turn without looking back. It is finished

The Post-Ritual Purification Prayer

After completing the elemental ritual, these words are to be spoken:

I come from a perfect source,

and I am bound for a perfect goal.

The light of the perfect being is kindled in my soul.

I live, move, and have my being in God.

And nothing in the world of the past or present

has power to touch me if I rise above all.

Safety and Reverence

"Take care whether you're working with fire or water or air or any element. It's a moment of profound mystical awareness — but also great vigilance — so that you are fully safe and so that the place is respected to the utmost and there is no pollution, physically or subtly."

"There's no pollution because the intention of the giving over of the impression is so clear — and because you are so clear in finding alignment with the place and with the forces that will expeditiously transform the substance."

Nature's Cyclical Wisdom

"Nature works in cycles, and that which is one creature's refuse can be the basis of the fertility that nourishes another — but only within bounds that are mutually agreeable."

"Everything goes back to the earth. But the question is: what is the manner of giving it back? What is the intention? What is the method? And if it's done with reverence, the Earth powerfully works with us to transform us, purify us."

• • •

Five Aspects of Breath — Complete Review

C10 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Pir Zia reviewed all five aspects of breath as they had been developed across the five days:

First Aspect — Exhalation

"Noticing the breath going out, the exhalation. Letting it go far and wide."

Second Aspect — Depth and Breadth

"The depth of the inhalation. The breadth of the exhalation — the range of the exhalation."

Third Aspect — Centering in the Belly

"Not just breathing shallowly up here, but breathing through the diaphragm right down into the place where etherically the breath begins — and that is just beneath the navel."

Fourth Aspect — Rhythm

"Not only that the out-breath goes out and the in-breath comes in, but that those two answer each other, enhance each other. And a rhythm develops."

"You come to feel it and to know its naturalness — so that when you're far from that rhythm, you're aware you've stepped out of balance."

Fifth Aspect — Scope of Breath

"The scope of the breath is discerning the breath not only in the movement of the air filling you and emptying you, but in the whole life field."

"The physical breath, the movement of the air, is just one example — one effect of an oscillation, a fluctuation that is actually operating on multiple planes of being."

"Not only is your body breathing, your heart is breathing, your soul is breathing. Breathing is this continuous give and take."

"The awareness of the movement of your breath opens you up to the awareness of subtler currents — the electricity in your body, the flashing of electromagnetism, and the tides of the inner worlds."

This fifth aspect of breath is where physical practice opens into the mystic field. The body's breath becomes a window onto the breathing of the soul itself.

Part I · Chapter 4

CONCENTRATION, VISUALIZATION & MEDITATION

Training the Sovereign Attention

Concentration — the first stage of the Suluk path — is the art of gathering scattered attention into a single point. Pir Zia's sessions covered color concentration, sensory practices, gemstone visualization, jalali and jamali objects, and the multi-dimensional vision teachings.

32 Entries · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

✿

Standing Posture for Prayer - The Alif Position

C1 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Complete Standing Posture

Before prayer, establish this foundational posture that embodies the sacred letter Alif:

  1. Feet: Firmly rooted in the earth
  2. Spine: Erect like the trunk of a tree
  3. Tailbone: Send a root deep into the earth
  4. Crown: Open to the vastness of the sky

The Symbolism of Alif

This posture embodies the Alif — the Arabic upright line that symbolizes the number One.

"The upright line suggests heaven, perfection, straightforwardness, firmness, life, rising, and unity — as it shows oneness with the whole. The upright line is the first line, and all forms and figures are nothing but the change of direction of that line."

The Alif position connects earth and heaven, representing the seeker's role as a bridge between the material and spiritual realms.

• • •

The Four Stages of Suluk Method

C1 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Suluk works through four progressive stages, each building upon the previous. These are not separated from daily life but are rehearsals for bringing attentive, heartful presence to every moment.

The Four Stages

StageNameDescription
**1****Concentration**Returning scattered attention to presence. The whole of you gathered in one place. Foundation of all prayer, meditation, creation, and love.
**2****Contemplation**Dwelling with a quality or state of being. Moving beyond imagery into subtler domains of sensation and feeling.
**3****Meditation**Tasting pure essence — beyond quality and form. Experiencing the uncolored essence of being.
**4****Realization**Re-entering the visible world with the invisible essence illumining all. Marriage of the visible and the invisible.

The Foundation: Concentration

"Concentration means the whole of you is in one place. You are not scattered. You are not dispersed. You are not diffused. You are gathered. If one can learn to concentrate, then one can pray. If one can learn to concentrate, then one can meditate. If one can learn to concentrate, then one can create. If one can learn to concentrate, then one can love. The whole of life depends on concentration."

Khalwat dar Anjuman

The concept of Khalwat dar Anjuman — 'solitude in the crowd' — means that even when meditating in silence, one is never alone. The class meets in the inner worlds through the intention that joins them.

• • •

Color Black Concentration Practice

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Practice

"Attention is a substance that can be moulded into any form, can be given any colour. So let's give it a colour — not a form in this case, just a colour. Colour black. Fill your mind with the colour black. Be blackened inside and out. No other colour appears now, just black itself — ebony, obsidian."

Instructions
  1. This is not a time to think about the meaning of black or imagine black things — simply visualize blackness
  2. If the mind wanders, return calmly to black, even if it happens 10, 100, 1000 times
  3. Let the black dissolve — allow other colours to come
  4. At this transition, notice resonances, associations, moods

Murshid's Nature Meditations on Black

"In the colour black, I feel the depth of Thy being."

"Thou showest in black Thy eternal being."

"In black Thou givest me a proof of being above all changes."

"Who is behind utter darkness? Thy endless self."

"Black is death. Yet life eternal."

• • •

Color Visualization: Black

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

"Attention is a substance that can be molded into any form, can be given any color."

Instructions

  1. Close the eyes — settle into stillness
  1. Gather attention — recognize it as a moldable substance
  1. Fill the mind completely with the color black — ebony, obsidian. No meanings, no black things, just pure blackness
  1. If the mind wanders — gently return to black, no matter how many times
  1. Let the black dissolve — allow other colors or impressions to arise naturally
  1. Notice resonances — feel associations, moods, or shifts at the transition

Murshid's Nature Meditation on Black

"In the colour black I feel the depth of thy being. Thou showest in black thy eternal being. In black thou givest me a proof of being above all changes. Who is behind utter darkness? Thy endless self. Black is death, yet life eternal."

• • •

Gemstone Concentration Practice

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Practice

  1. Close the eyes
  2. Let a crystalline, translucent gemstone appear before the mind's eye
  3. Observe its facets, shape, lustre, glow, and specific hue
  4. Let it slowly revolve so it is seen from all sides
  5. Avoid associations (value, stories, history) — only direct encounter
  6. Let it fade
  7. Notice any resonance remaining

"See it as clearly as you can — not by forcing it into a shape, but by inviting its disclosure."

Murshid's Gemstone Properties

"Murshid has given a few indications about the effects of some of them:

  • Sapphire is conducive to art and inspiration
  • Diamond promotes righteousness, integrity
  • Topaz breeds harmony"

Underground Caverns

"Under the earth, there are whole vast caverns of gemstones, unbeknownst to human beings."

• • •

Gemstone Visualization Practice

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

A visualization practice using a translucent precious stone as the object of concentration:

Instructions

  1. Close the eyes — imagine a translucent gemstone (sapphire, diamond, ruby, emerald, or any crystalline stone)
  1. Observe its qualities — shape, facets, glow, specific hue
  1. Let it slowly revolve — observing from all sides
  1. Avoid associations — no thoughts of monetary value or story. Stay with direct perception only
  1. Let the stone fade naturally once the image is complete
  1. Notice resonances — subtle feelings, moods, or impressions that arise when the stone disappears
  1. Rest in the afterglow — without overthinking, simply receiving

Notes on Stone Qualities from Murshid

  • Sapphire is conducive to art and inspiration
  • Diamond promotes righteousness and integrity
  • Topaz breeds harmony
• • •

Rightful Breathing Practice - The Aerial Body

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Basic Posture and Approach

  • Sit upright — shoulders open, spine elongated, tailbone rooted to earth, crown open to sky
  • Watch as breath enters — don't suck it in, let it enter gradually
  • Air moves through the nostrils, glides down the windpipe, fills the lungs, fills the bloodstream
  • Don't be in a hurry to breathe out — give the whole process its natural time

Visualization of Exhaled Air

"One can almost imagine the molecules of the exhaled air flying out in all directions up into the sky, some resulting down the street."

The Aerial Body Paradox

"So the exhalation is a great movement of expansion, even though your chest and belly are contracting as you exhale. And the inhalation is a contraction — the surrounding air spirals in and penetrates your very cells while the chest and belly widen. Can you feel both aspects — the contracting and expanding of the trunk of your body — and at the same time, in a converse direction, the contracting and expanding of your aerial body, that vortex of breath that whirls in and out again?"

Physical Yielding

"Let all of your muscles and tendons and bones yield themselves to this flow. By no means collapsing, but adjusting so as to maximize the movement of breath through the body — and the refreshment that this brings, the invigoration, the calm energy, the clarity."

• • •

Sandpaper Exercise — Touch Practice

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

A practice in pure tactile attention:

Instructions

  1. Take the sandpaper in your hand
  1. Close the eyes — let sight, sound, and other senses fall away
  1. Give whole attention to the fingertips — feel every ridge, every grain, every prick
  1. Stop rubbing — remain with the tactile memory
  1. Set it down — sense the state that remains

Murshid's Teaching on Observation

"The first step to concentration is observation. The one who lacks observation cannot concentrate well. Observation depends upon steadiness of mind. And this steadiness can be brought about by interest."

"There is no better way of cultivating one's memory than observation of a single object at a certain time."

Key Insight: Concentration and Eternity

"That which your heart meets, in some mysterious way, is introduced into eternity."

  • What we attend to with genuine interest lives on in the soul's lasting memory
  • What we touch mechanically — without care — leaves no imprint and is gone
  • Beings without bodies wonder what it would be like to wear a hand of flesh — reminding us to cherish our human senses

Sandpaper Touch Concentration and Beings Without Bodies

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Practice

  1. Hold the sandpaper
  2. Close the eyes and let all other senses fall away
  3. Give whole attention to the little ridges of the fingertips and thumb rolling across the sandpaper
  4. Feel acutely every little prick, every stab of a minute grain of sand
  5. Stop, set it down, and sense your state

Murshid on Observation and Concentration

"The first step to concentration is observation. The one who lacks observation cannot concentrate well. Observation depends upon steadiness of mind. And this steadiness can be brought about by interest. Those who have no interest in anything or anybody have no steadiness of mind."

"As long a time a person observes an object, so long in proportion its memory lasts. There is no better way of cultivating one's memory than observation of a single object at a certain time. The observant show by their very looks a powerful will, a steady mind, and a capacity for concentration."

Traditions That Teach This Secret

Murshid names two traditions: Bhakti Yoga (Hindu) and Tasawur Murshid (Sufi).

Beings Without Bodies - A Profound Teaching

"There are beings who don't wear bodies. If they haven't yet incarnated — maybe some of them never will incarnate. They wonder very much what it would be like to wear a hand of flesh and to have in their fingers the grid of sand and to rub it. That's something that right now we can feel. And we won't always be able to feel this. The sand may go numb. We may — the body itself may dissolve. We don't know when."

"But wherever we are, in whatever realm, to meet that realm with the whole of our being, with the whole of our interest, with the whole of our love — that's concentration."

The Eternity of Heart-Met Experience

"That which you experience but you don't really experience because your heart's not in it — when it's gone, it's gone. But that which your heart meets — in some mysterious way, it's introduced into eternity."

• • •

Sensus Communis — The Common Sense

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Pir Zia introduced the classical philosophical concept of Sensus Communis (Latin: the sense within all senses) as the foundation of concentration.

Key Principles

  • Five senses — sight, hearing, taste, smell, touch — are all channels of one sensation
  • Sensation converges at one point — the Sensus Communis, the common sense
  • Synesthesia — when the senses criss-cross (hearing a color, seeing a taste) — is evidence of their common root
  • Ilm-e-Huzuri — knowledge by presence — is the Sufi name for this faculty of pure attention
  • Even in sleep or death, the light of attention continues, turned inward

"If you give attention to attention, then it flourishes, it blossoms, it becomes very luminous."

Connection to Hazrat (Presence)

This is why great beings are addressed as Hazrat (from Huzur, meaning presence). Murshid is Hazrat Inayat Khan — one in whom presence is profoundly embodied.

• • •

The Invisible Rain Breath Practice

C3 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Pir Zia led this guided breath practice using the image of invisible rain — a subtle, continuous flow streaming through the sky, entering through every pore.

The Complete Practice

1. Invisible Rain Visualization

Sense a subtle rain always falling, flowing into you through all pores, the body opening to receive it.

2. Breath Awareness

Feel a wave coming in with each inhalation; guide breath down the windpipe, filling the lungs.

3. Postural Alignment

Adjust every vertebra, rib, and muscle gently; find spaciousness without rigidity.

4. Full-Body Breath

Sense the breath traveling down the arms, through the hips and thighs, into the feet, up through the neck, head, and scalp.

5. Cellular Awareness

Recognize the body as a vast congregation of cells, floating, humming, thirsting for breath.

6. Quenching

Feel the thirst of each cell satisfied by the inhalation, cascading right down to the tips of the toes.

7. Exhalation as Communion

The cells release what is superfluous to this body, but thirsted for by the green beings — trees, algae, plants. We breathe in concert with all plant life.

Key Quotes

"Each inhalation cascading through the body right down to the tips of the toes, satisfying a deep thirst."

"In this communion, in this participation, breath by breath, there is joy for the cells, and peace, and an inkling of the oneness of all being."

Connection to Water

Breath shares the characteristics of water — it flows and moves in tides, waves, ripples, and surges.

Visualization - Calling a Loved One

C3 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

A concentration practice led by Pir Zia:

The Practice

  1. Think of a person dear to you
  2. Let their name resound in the mind
  3. Allow their face and form to emerge from the name
  4. Let the form dissolve back into the name
  5. Rest with the residue of the encounter

This practice demonstrates how concentration can work with memory, visualization, and the subtle connections between beings.

Visualization Practice — Calling a Loved One

C3 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Practice

Pir Zia led this brief concentration practice as an exercise in visualization and mental focus.

Steps

  1. Think of a person dear to you
  2. Let their name resound in the mind
  3. Allow their face and form to emerge from the name
  4. Let the form dissolve back into the name
  5. Rest with the residue of the encounter

Purpose

This practice develops the faculty of concentration through the natural magnetism of love and connection, using visualization to strengthen mental focus and inner sight.
