Breath Visualization Through Soles of Feet

C4 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

A lying-down practice for developing wakeful sleep — the foundation of all future contemplation and meditation work.

Preparation

  • Lie down on the ground — not on a bed. The ground enhances connection to the earth and stabilizes subtle energy flow
  • Lie on your back with arms and legs fully extended. Do not bend knees or elbows — let all limbs rest completely
  • Enter the deepest possible relaxation while remaining fully awake — this is wakeful sleep

The Practice

  1. Become aware of breath — not merely as air in and out, but as a larger cosmic process: expansion and contraction, assimilation and disgorgement
  2. Recognize breath as the medium linking all cycles: spring and fall, sleeping and waking, birth and death, inner and outer worlds
  3. Place attention on the soles of the feet as a passageway between inside and outside
  4. Inhale through the soles — receive an influx of subtle breath, prana, etheric breeze. Let it flow up the legs, through the midsection, chest, arms, and head, filling the body completely
  5. Gentle transition — do not hold the breath, do not rush the exhale. A smooth, unhurried flow between inhalation and exhalation
  6. Exhale through the soles — trace the departure of energy as it drains down the legs and out through the feet into the ground

Duration: approximately 10 minutes at a time. No note-taking during practice — simply be with the experience.

Key Teaching

"As though you would lie down on the seashore with your feet pointing out to the sea — a wave comes in, washes over you, fills you, first striking the soles of your feet and then pervading you completely. And then the wave drains back out into the sea."

• • •

Color Visualization Practice - White

C4 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

A visual concentration exercise using the color white as the focal point to train the mind in focus, steadiness, and self-observation.

The Two Approaches

Approach 1 — Replace: Leave behind all the hues seen behind closed eyelids and replace them with white, summoned from memory or from within.

Approach 2 — Amplify: From the medley of colors naturally visible, pick out the grains of white and promote, increase, and maximize white until it prevails and all other colors fade away.

The Practice

  1. Close the eyes — observe the natural mixture of hues behind the eyelids
  2. Choose your approach (replace or amplify) and bring white to the foreground
  3. Rest patiently in the vision of pure white — without commentary or elaboration
  4. When distracted, return to white gently and patiently, as many times as needed
  5. Finally, let the white fade back into the mixture or disappear entirely
  6. Sense the impact: how do you feel? What arose — memory, image, or emotion?

Self-Observation Questions

  • What thoughts intervened — were they genuinely urgent or simply habitual?
  • Did attention leave the color completely, or was the color still present alongside the thought?
  • Which was foremost — the color or the thought?
  • Were you aware of the switch in the moment, or only afterward?
  • How did you return to the color white?

The Role of Love in Attention

"What enables keen attention is essentially love. We can call it interest, but interest is a manifestation of love."

"Every object that I choose or that is given to me is another opportunity to discover a relationship and a light that was otherwise hidden — light that was hidden until I gave it my care."

• • •

Concentrating on a Flower Practice

C4 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

A Jamali-natured concentration object. Even with a Jamali object, both Jalali and Jamali must be brought to the practice.

The Practice

  1. Settle into ease — "There is nowhere to go, nothing to do, no hurry about anything."
  1. Notice the spirit of agitation — the impulse that insists the mind must be busy. Simply observe it without obeying.
  1. Be like a calm person in a busy train station — thoughts are busy travelers; you stand calmly in the center, unaffected.
  1. Jalali: give attention to a plant — roots in the ground, stalk rising, leaves unfurled. Trace all the way to the flower. Actively observe the shape of petals, the stamen, color, texture, fragrance.
  1. Jamali: let the active portrayal give way to a gentle embrace of what is shown — an easeful meeting.
  1. Give your goodbye to the flower. Return to your own quality of attention.

Transition: Mouth and Nectar

After the flower practice, attention shifts inward to the Sensus Communis concentrated in the mouth:

  • Move the Sensus Communis inward — bring attention to the tongue and the water of the mouth
  • Gently touch the tip of the tongue to the roof of the mouth, then lower it — notice the subtle tang
  • "The yogis call it a nectar — one of the fundamental nectars of the body."
• • •

Tasting Practice with Cardamom Seed

C4 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

A practice in pure sensory awareness using taste as the concentration object — the deepest possible immersion in direct experience.

The Practice

  1. Place a cardamom seed on the tongue
  2. Bite once to release the spice — allow the sharp taste to fill the mouth
  3. If no cardamom is available — taste the water of the mouth instead
  4. At this moment: no thought, no speculation. Only the encounter between awareness and taste
  5. Let the taste fill time and space — there is no taster and no tasted. There is only the tasting

Working with Distraction

The key instruction: do not fight distractions. Fighting distractions binds you more tightly to what you are trying to push away.

Instead, cultivate a combination of interest and indifference:

Interest — concentrated engagement; drawing awareness inward; making attention palpable.

Indifference — non-attachment; not being consumed by what arises; not grasping or pushing.

"If you fight those distractions, you move further away from the sheer experience."

"What we have to cultivate is a combination of interest and indifference."

• • •

Avoiding the Word "I" - 24 Hour Practice

C5 · September 14, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Reflection on the Previous Task

The 24-hour practice of avoiding the word "I" revealed two key insights:

  1. How words roll off our tongue — choosing words requires great and constant attention
  2. How often the self is the constant reference point in all speech

The Deeper Question

The practice opened a deeper question: What is this "I" we use so casually hundreds of times a day?

  • On one level — the I is a construct, an illusion, a figment of inter-subjective perceptions, all transitory
  • On another level — the I is being itself, the fundament of the universe
  • It is the whole spectrum — everything in between these two poles

"Who is this I? What is this I?"

"On the one hand, the I is just a construct, just an illusion. On the other side, the I is being itself, the fundament of the universe. And it's everything in between. This word that we use a hundred times a day — its meanings are immense."

• • •

Geographical Orientation - Daily Task

C5 · September 14, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Know where you stand on the Earth — and stay oriented for 24 hours.

The Task

Determine which way is north, south, east, and west. Then stay continuously aware of your geographical situation throughout the day — without relying on technology.

The Practice

  1. Determine which direction is north, south, east, and west from where you are now
  2. Know: which way would you walk to reach the nearest seashore?
  3. Know: in which direction do the nearest mountains loom?
  4. Know: where is the river that runs near your city?
  5. Wherever you are — in whatever room, on whatever street — remain situated. Know where you stand on your continent

The Deeper Teaching

Geographical Awareness — knowing directions and locating natural features (rivers, seas, mountains) around oneself.

Embodied Orientation — moving through daily life with spatial consciousness; staying aware of one's place in relation to the continent and Earth.

Technology vs Natural Attunement — GPS and phones have replaced instinctual orientation; we risk losing the felt sense of our place on Earth.

Spiritual Lesson — to be grounded in the world, one must consciously situate the self. Orientation is not just geographical but existential: knowing one's place in the larger whole.

"Take responsibility for our own situatedness on the earth."

• • •

Color Visualization: Yellow - Alchemical Sequence

C6 · September 14, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The third in the alchemical color sequence: black → white → yellow. This sequence is rooted in Khem (ancient Egypt) and is the basis of alchemy. Yellow symbolizes illumination, clarity, and awakening.

The Practice

  1. Close the eyes — invite yellow into the mind's eye
  2. Let yellow gradually fill the entire field of inner vision — like daylight shining behind the eyelids
  3. Immerse in yellow — become tinctured by it, like a piece of cloth soaked in golden light. Be stained, dyed, saturated by yellow from within
  4. Observe the precise shade — ochre, gold, canary yellow. Don't analyze; simply see and experience yellow as purely as possible
  5. Maintain concentration — whenever the mind wanders, gently return to yellow without frustration
  6. Let go — after a few minutes, release yellow. Allow it to fade naturally, noticing any lingering afterimage or mood
  7. Reflection — what did yellow evoke? How would you move through the day in a "yellow mood" — radiant, open, bright?

Murshid's Reflections on Yellow

  • "In yellow I see the flame of Thy light."
  • "I see in yellow Thy love and Thy light."
  • "Thou hast ordained with yellow the earth and Thy heavens."
  • "Let my heart ripen as a green leaf ripens to yellow."
  • "I see Thy two wings in the green water and the yellow earth."
  • "Let the yellow flames of Thy divine light turn my false ego into ashes."

Daily Practice Extension

Throughout the day, notice every yellow hue in your environment — a practice of attention.

• • •

Jalali and Jamali: The Star - Celestial Practice

C6 · September 14, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Building on previous practices with terrestrial objects (gemstone = Jalali / flower = Jamali), we turn to a celestial object — the star — to experience Jalali energy at its most radiant.

The Progression

  • Day 1 — Jalali terrestrial: gemstone — firmness, structure, strength, enduring radiance of the earth
  • Day 2 — Jamali terrestrial: flower — delicacy, fragrance, grace, the soft beauty of creation
  • Day 3 — Jalali celestial: star — fierce, radiant, actively burning, the luminous power of divine majesty

Teaching on Stars and Flowers

The flowers of the earth and the stars of the sky mirror each other: as starlight shines down, the earth lifts up flowers that beam back at the stars. Flowers are star-shaped. Stars are Jalali; the crescent moon is Jamali.

"The stars are more Jalali than Jamali. The crescent moon is reflective, but the star is actively radiant."

"Earth lifts up flowers that beam back at the stars — so the flowers of the sky are the stars."

Star Visualization Practice

  1. Close the eyes — envision the vast night sky
  2. Choose one shining star — blazing, burning, radiant with fierce Jalali energy
  3. Come face to face with it — feel its intensity illuminating your entire being
  4. Breathe in the starlight — clarity, strength, illumination entering with each inhalation
  5. Breathe out — dissolve into the star; you become the star you gaze upon
  6. The star recedes — withdrawing into the night sky as dawn approaches
  7. Rest in the afterglow — the quiet luminosity that remains within

Additional Teachings

Building on previous practices with terrestrial objects (gemstone = Jalali / flower = Jamali), this practice turns to a celestial object — the star — to experience Jalali energy at its most radiant.

• • •

Journey Through the Mind: Sensation → Memory → Imagination

C6 · September 14, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

A guided exploration of the three faculties of mind, building sequentially through the retreat.

The Three Faculties

  1. Sensation — the first faculty: presence functioning through the five senses, bringing us face to face with what is physically here now.
  2. Memory — the second faculty: carrying prior embodied experiences into the present; moving in Malakut, where images no longer wear matter.
  3. Imagination — the third faculty: creating and discovering images in Malakut; the bridge between the seen and unseen, the known and the becoming.

Step 1: Sensation — Gateway of Presence

Bring awareness to the present moment. Notice what the senses are perceiving — temperature, weight, texture, sound.

"Sensation functions through the five senses, bringing us face to face with what is physically here before us — an encounter attended to by presence."

Step 2: Memory — The Living Archive

Bring to mind a memory that left a deep impression. Let it unfold naturally. The vividness of the memory depends on two things: how present you were then, and how present you are now.

"The more present we were at that time, and the more present we are now, the more vivid the revival of the memory — so much so that one can enter a memory and feel oneself completely there."

Memory is not mere fantasy — it is movement into Malakut, where images exist without physical substance. What once existed outwardly still exists inwardly as image and meaning.

"In memory, we're moving away from what is physically right before us. We're actually moving in the realm of Malakut, where images don't wear matter."

Step 3: Imagination — Active Perception in Malakut

Imagination does not mean unreal whimsy — it means active perception and discovery of images in Malakut. It is the bridge between seen and unseen, known and becoming.

"The third faculty of mind is imagination — which doesn't mean unreal whimsy; it means creating and discovering images in Malakut."

The Exercise: Think of someone you have never met — a teacher, historical figure, or beloved artist. Let their name arise. The name becomes a herald announcing the one it designates. A presence forms. See them vividly — expression, height, color of apparel. If the picture fades, revive it. Then let the figure pack itself back into the name. Let the name fade into silence. You are left with pure awareness — the ground of all images.

Return and Integration

Bring awareness back to the physical — touch, taste, smell, hearing, sight. The imaginal and physical are not separate; they interpenetrate. Both levels are equally true.

"I dreamed I was a butterfly, and now I don't know if I'm a man who dreamed he was a butterfly, or a butterfly dreaming he's a man. Both levels are equally true." — Zhuangzi

• • •

Sensory Exercise: Smell (Fire Element)

C6 · September 14, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The third sensory exercise in the Sensus Communis sequence. Having worked with Touch (Earth — sandpaper) and Taste (Water — cardamom), we now turn to Smell, associated with Fire — for it arises through burning incense, rising vapors, and subtle essences.

The Elemental Sequence

  • Touch — Earth: The most immediate, palpable sense; the whole skin feels it
  • Taste — Water: Whatever enters the mouth presents taste
  • Smell — Fire: Subtler than taste; usually only noticed when fragrance is strong, yet always present

The Practice — Rose Essence

  1. Close the eyes — bring attention inward. Ask: "What is the fragrance of this moment?"
  2. Lift the paper with rose essence to the nostrils. Breathe in slowly and deeply
  3. Fill your nostrils with the scent — fill your whole being with it
  4. Lose yourself in it — no visualization needed. Don't imagine the rose garden; become the fragrance
  5. Reach the point where there is no one smelling and nothing being smelled — only fragrance itself, making itself known
  6. Set down the paper — remain still. The scent lingers as a state of being, not merely an odor
  7. The impression remains — even hours later you can return to this location in consciousness simply by remembering

Key Teaching

"Lose yourself in it, until there is no one smelling and nothing being smelled — only fragrance itself, making itself known."

"You'll always be able to find that location, because it's become your own now."

"The sense of smell is always present, though seldom noticed. By awakening it, we awaken the quality of presence in our lives."

Daily Practice Extension

Throughout the day notice every subtle variation of fragrance — morning air after rain, dry warmth of sunlit stone, the invisible perfume of leaves, flowers, or wood. Each fragrance is a reminder to awaken.

• • •

Color RED Concentration Exercise

C7 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

"See red. Not a red thing, but redness itself — scarlet, crimson, deep and glowing. Let it fill your mind and flood your senses. Let the color red arise within you, not as an object, but as a living atmosphere. Feel how it radiates, how it warms, how it moves through your being."

Two-Phase Instruction

Phase 1: Hold Redness as Living Atmosphere
  • Hold redness as living atmosphere
  • Sense your state, what is coming through?
Phase 2: Let Red Fade and Notice Resonance
  • Let the red fade from the mind's eye
  • Note: 'The resonance of red is there'
  • How has it left you feeling? Alert, alive, passionate, or tender?

The resonance persists after the color fades.

Murshid's Words on Red

In the red color, I see thy glowing countenance.

In red, I see the bleeding of thy heart in sympathy for thy creatures.

Red shows me thy life in its perfect glow.

Red brings life to my hungry heart.

Dye my heart red that it may take the color of thine own life.

Day-Long Practice Extension

"So now throughout the day, I would encourage you to notice red wherever it appears. Just let it pop up and strike you wherever it occurs. Take in the mood of it all through the day."

The exercise does not end in the session. Red as a living transmission is to be received continuously through ordinary life.

• • •

Jamali Practice - The Crescent Moon

C8 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Context in the Sequence

This is the third practice in a sensory/elemental sequence:

  1. Jalali (radiant, strong) terrestrial object — the precious stone
  2. Jamali (gentle, beautiful) terrestrial object — the flower
  3. Jamali (gentle, receptive) celestial object — the crescent moon

The Nature of Moonlight

"The moon that receives the light of the sun and is kindled by it, reflects it. The sunlight in itself is so fiery, so intense. But when sunlight reflects from the moon, it is cooled, becomes gentle and diaphanous."

"You can't stare into the sun, but you can gaze directly at the moon. And to gaze upon the moon is to be calmed, to be cooled, to be immersed in this gossamer light — that reminds you of something very fine, very gentle within your own being."

The Day-Cycle Turn

"When one has spent the whole day talking and writing and giving opinions and projecting thoughts into the world — there's a turn. And now one can just receptively rest."

"Does the moon have any opinions? The moon simply receives the light it's given and sends it onward."

Practice Instructions

  1. See a glowing crescent moon hovering in the sky of your mind
  2. Trace its gentle arc — observe its soft silver hue
  3. Sense the tenor of its light: calming, receptive, cooling
  4. Embody its quality: be serene, reflective, receiving light and radiating it softly
  5. Let opinions, words, and outward projection fall silent — become receptivity itself
  6. Gradually let the image fade until only the vastness of inner sky remains

Reflection After the Practice

"Where has the crescent gone? It's no less in you now than it was when you saw it. But when you saw it, you manifested it."

"What else lies in wait within you, capable of being manifested at any time?"

"Perhaps the better question would be — what doesn't lie in wait within you, capable of being manifested at any time?"

Key Qualities

  • You become moon-like, become lunar
  • Receptivity without opinion
  • Cooling the fiery intensity of day
  • Gentle reflection rather than direct projection
• • •

Seeing and the Divine Will - Green Dot Practice

C8 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Context: Working with the Senses

This sight practice is part of a series working with the senses one by one — following sandpaper (touch) and cardamom (taste/smell) in prior sessions.

The Problem of Habitual Sight

"Sight is the sense that we use so much that we hardly know we're using it. We take it for granted. It's just as if the world appears. We're not even conscious of looking. The world just shows itself."

"The way we look determines what we see. Our glance has developed in concert with the brain along a track that prioritizes discerning things — picking out this thing and that thing, differentiating one thing from another."

Shifting from Things to Qualities

Instead of identifying objects (window, door), notice qualities: redness, roundness, luminosity, texture. What is a thing but a particular combination of qualities?

"Instead of immediately outlining the boundary of a thing, we discern the ways in which qualities advance and recede and mingle on all of the horizons in a constant flux."

The Light of the Glance - Meeting of Lights

"The impression that reaches your eyes is significant — but just as significant in the act of seeing is the light that goes out through your glance to what you see. Send that light out. Send out two beams. Illuminate what you see. There's a meeting of lights."

"As Jesus said, don't hide your light under a bushel — acknowledge it, utilize it."

Visual Ray Awareness

"As you open your eyes — beware of the rays, like the headlights of a car, wherever you turn. The sensation is not so different from having a hand by which you can reach out and touch something. You're reaching out through your glance. The ray is going out, touching, and shaking hands with what you see."

Green Dot Practice Instructions

  1. Sit upright, relax the face — no tension in forehead, temples, or jaw
  2. Find the green dot (or point) on the wall
  3. Without tensing — reach out through the glance, reach through the air, and touch the point
  4. Let the point glimmer with the touch of your attention
  5. Hold the steady gaze for about one minute
  6. Close eyes — sense your state
  7. Open eyes again — feel the rays extending outward

Rapturous Eyes - The Invitation

"Let your eyes become rapturous explorers of the divine manifestation in the visible and invisible worlds, rather than merely habituated reinforcers of preconceived expectations."

"Let your eyes surprise you, delight you. Let your eyes be practitioners of concentration, able to rest for moments at a time on something that in the eyes of the world is of no practical value."

Inner Vision Test

"What if you were to suddenly, right now, close your eyes? The room around you — can you still see it? If you don't see it anymore, did you really see it before?"

Additional Teachings

This is the third and final stage of the Green Dot concentration practice. Each day the dot has become smaller, refining the focus and training the mind to settle on a single point. After this session, the dot is no longer needed at all.

"The focus is refining itself — it's concentrating on a smaller point. And soon, you won't need the green dot at all."

Pir Zia shared a teaching of Imam Ali that illuminates why the dot has such depth:

  • The whole Quran is contained in Surah Fatiha.
  • The whole Fatiha is contained in Bismillahir Rahmanir Raheem.
  • The whole Bismillah is contained in the Ba.
  • The Ba is contained in the point beneath it.

"The very first thing one sees when opening the Quran already contains the whole revelation. It's all in that point. There's a lot in a dot."

The spirit of agitation may arise — the impulse to rip the glance away, to feel restless, bored, tired. The instruction: notice it, do not judge it, but hold the decision to stay.

"It won't always be easy, but we give our whole heart to it. And if we find ourselves distracted, we just keep coming back again and again to the dot."

After this session, no green dot is needed. Simply relax the glance, close the eyes, set your state (tailbone rooted, crown open), then open the eyes — and the point of attention itself remains as the field of awareness.

  1. Relax the glance
  2. Close the eyes
  3. Set your state (tailbone rooted, crown open)
  4. Open the eyes — the point of attention itself remains as the field of awareness

The Green Dot practice reinforces the faculty of directed outward attention through the glance.

  1. Stand like a tree — rooted. Let the weight come down off your shoulders. Breathe well.
  1. The Sensus Communis concentrates itself in the glance — projected out through both eyes as two beams.
  1. Both beams converge at the single point where the green dot stands on the wall.
  1. Gaze without rigidity — jaw relaxed, temples relaxed, shoulders relaxed.
  1. Calm does not numb the mind — precisely because of the state of calm, the whole care can be given to one point.
  1. Close the eyes — draw the beams back in. Let the Sensus Communis fill all five senses. Sit down.

"It's a gaze at the point without becoming rigid — and it's not a relaxation that numbs your mind. On the contrary, precisely because of your state of calm, you're able to give your whole care to that one point for a minute."

  1. Stand upright but relaxed facing the green dot on the wall
  2. Focus the glance on the dot — don't look at anything else
  3. Hold steadily for about one minute
  4. If the mind wanders, gradually let yourself come back to this moment, this gaze, this point
  5. Allow yourself this ease, this simplicity
  6. Close eyes, bring the energy back to all five senses
  7. Open eyes again and sit down

"Your whole attention goes to that point and that point lights up. Your sensation concentrates itself. All of the senses are concentrated in the Sensus Communis, which functions now first and foremost through the glance. And the glance lands on that point and gives its whole attention there."

A physical concentration practice using an external point of focus:

  1. Setup — place a green dot on the wall in advance. Stand upright, relaxed, facing it
  1. Fix your gaze on the dot — direct all attention to that single point
  1. Let the dot become the focal point — all senses converge in the Sensus Communis, functioning through the glance
  1. If the mind wanders — gently return without frustration. Stay with simplicity
  1. Completion — close the eyes briefly; gather the focused energy back into all five senses; open the eyes and sit down
• • •

Sovereignty of Attention - Three Parts

C8 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Shadow Side of Concentration

"What if you're holding in your focus something that depresses you? This is the flip side of concentration — not the concentration that is intentional, but the concentration that takes you over."

The Three-Part Sovereignty

True concentration requires mastery over three aspects:

  1. The ability to choose the giving of your consciousness to something
  2. The ability to choose the length of that giving
  3. The ability to choose what you give it to

The Art of Release

"True concentration requires the ability to utterly forget and disown any impression. We don't have to own everything because it met our glance once."

"Every time that you think it again, you're partaking of it, you're claiming it — and you don't need to."

The Teaching of Jesus: Each Speaks What He Owns

Once Jesus was walking with disciples when someone began reviling him with crude and insulting words. Jesus said nothing. When the disciples asked why he didn't correct the man, Jesus answered:

"Each speaks what he owns."

Pir Zia explains: "So Jesus didn't choose to own it himself. That man said it — it belonged to him. He left it at that. Didn't accept it into his own concentration."

Practical Application

There is so much that meets our eyes and ears that we have no need to hold in any way. The principle is simple: don't hold on to anything you don't need to.

"As soon as you let it go, it's just inconsequential — as if it never existed. And what a relief to exhale it and let it go."

• • •

Color Blue Exercise

C9 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Practice Instructions

"Let it appear, let it come, show itself — filling you, saturating you, tincturing you. Be dyed blue, like a garment plunged in blue dye, soaking it up in every fiber — till all you see, all you know, is blue."

"You can let the blue expanse that surrounds and fills you gradually dissipate to make room for other colors. It doesn't disappear altogether, but other colors join it."

Contemplation Questions

"Sense your stain. What secret does blue hold for you?"

"If you had to explain blue to someone who had never seen the color — but you had to explain blue without recourse to words, just by communicating a state and conveying that frequency to the other person — how would you silently express it?"

Murshid's Nature Meditations on Blue

"In the color blue, I get the glimpse of Thy heavens."

"I see heaven shining out in Thy blue eyes. I behold the blue of Thine eyes in the sky."

"Out of blue comes Thy uplifting influence which raiseth me from earth."

"In blue I see the purity of Thy nature."

"Raise me high in the blue spheres of Thy heaven."

"I feel Thy presence most when all is blue to me."

Cognitive Styles and Sensory Concentration

C10 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Pir Zia acknowledged that not all students are suited to visual concentration — that cognitive styles differ, and that any sensory channel is a valid path.

Any Sense Object as Perfect Concentration Object

"A sense object in any of the categories is a perfect object of concentration, whatever it is. It could be a note, a musical note, could be a fragrance, could be a taste."

"The practice then would be to stay with something and recreate it in your experience, even after the outer stimulus has disappeared."

Example: Sound Practice

Sound a note on an instrument. When the note fades out — keep hearing the note. Stay with it for five or ten minutes. That itself is concentration.

The Essential Principle

"What's less important is the object. Let it be an object that draws you, an object that you love. But the essence of the practice is staying with, lingering over an experience. And not just rushing on — it could be any of the senses."

What Was Worked With Over Five Days

  • Concentration — learning what it is and beginning to practice it
  • The Glance — focusing through the eyes with awareness, both open and closed
  • Visualization — perceiving things and beings, both eyes open (gaze) and eyes closed (inner image)
  • The Senses — worked through day by day: smell, taste, sight, hearing
  • Five colors worked with across the five sessions (Black, White, Yellow, Red, Blue)
  • Five Aspects of Breath worked with throughout the program
  • Five Aspects of Mind — Sensation, Memory, Imagination, Will, and Self
• • •

Gazing & Visualization — Crescent Moon + Star

C10 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

A two-phase gaze and visualization practice, integrating all the concentration work of the retreat.

Phase 1 — Open-Eyed Gaze

  1. Stay in the expanded awareness just cultivated.
  2. Open the eyes.
  3. Direct the gaze to a fixed point on the wall.
  4. Hold the gaze steady for a minute.

Phase 2 — Inner Visualization

  1. Close the eyelids and relax.
  2. Visualize the crescent moon — gentle, cool, diaphanous light.
  3. Just above the crescent moon: a splendid star, glittering with rays streaking outward.
  4. See both the crescent moon and the star together in your mind's eye — held in juxtaposition.
  5. Then let the image disappear. Sense your inner state.
  6. When ready, open the eyes again.

This practice serves as a crystallization of the entire retreat's concentration arc: from sensory outer attention → to inner visualization → to the awareness of pure Self that holds both.

• • •

Light & Breath Practice — The Orb / Auric Body

C10 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

A core visualization practice integrating the fifth aspect of breath with awareness of subtle anatomy.

Practice Instructions

  1. Let the breath be rhythmic, rooted in the belly, far-reaching and deep.
  2. Visualize the breath as a sphere — an orb of light.
  3. As you breathe out, watch it expand. As it expands, it fades and thins out.
  4. "At the culmination of your exhalation, that orb simply seems to lose itself in the darkness of space."
  5. As you inhale, it congeals anew. Its circumference shrinks down around you. Its light intensifies.
  6. Begin by focusing it in the belly. As you contract it, you can locate its concentrated center anywhere in your body.

Subtle Anatomy — The Auric Body

"As it expands and contracts, it brings to light various contours which aren't merely the visible contours of one's physical body. These lineaments describe subtle structures — subtle anatomy."

"So that increasingly you become aware of a body of light — an Auric body."

"Let it be rhythmic. Let it be rooted in the belly. Let it go far and enter deeply."

Sensory Integration — The Etheric Body

With the Auric body established, Pir Zia connected this subtle awareness back to everyday experience:

"When you're using your senses — whether touching or tasting or smelling, seeing, hearing — you're aware of doing so through the action not only of your obvious physical body, but also through this etheric body immersed in subtle light, breathing light in the way that the physical body breathes oxygen."

This teaching is the integration point of the five days: all sensory practices have been progressively building the student's awareness of this second, etheric layer of perception.

MOVEMENTS, RITUALS & TECHNIQUES

The Body as Sacred Instrument

The Sufi path is embodied. Pir Zia taught the prayer movements, ablutions, daily awareness exercises (like avoiding the word 'I'), and other physical practices that ground the teachings in the body.

Daily Task - Stepping Through Doors with Right Foot First

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Practice

When you step through any door — front door, room to room — be aware of the threshold and step right foot first.

Purpose

  • Cultivates attention, awareness, and concentration in everyday movement
  • Not a lifelong rule — just for today; though you may choose to continue in special moments

If You Forget

"You might walk from one room to another and then a minute later realize: oh, I just passed through a door and forgot. Don't be hard on yourself — but it's good that you remembered. Keep reminding yourself, even if you make a mistake, keep going."

The act of remembering is itself part of the practice.

• • •

Daily Task: Stepping Through Doors

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The task for Day 1: each time you step through a doorway — any door, any threshold — do so mindfully, with the right foot first.

Guidelines

  • Purpose — cultivates attention, awareness, and concentration in everyday movement
  • Not permanent — just for today, though the practice may be carried into special moments or pilgrimages
  • If you forget — do not be hard on yourself; the act of remembering is itself part of the practice
  • Threshold awareness — stepping through a door is a movement from one space into another; meet it consciously
• • •

Ablutions — Ritual Purification Practice

C3 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Purpose

Ablution is the act of washing parts of the body as a form of ritual purification. It is practiced upon waking and at intervals through the day — especially before prayers or spiritual practices.

The Complete Sequence

  1. Wash right and left hands — 3 times each
  2. Rinse the mouth — 3 times
  3. Sniff water into the nostrils and blow out — 3 times
  4. Wash the face — 3 times
  5. Wash arms up to the elbows — 3 times each
  6. Wash hair, behind the ears, and the neck — 3 times
  7. Wash feet up to the ankles — 3 times each

The Spiritual Significance

The body is in the shape of a five-pointed star — two hands, two feet, and the head as the five points. Vitalizing these extremities with fresh water stimulates, wakes, cleanses, and purifies.

"You're vitalizing these extremities with fresh water, which stimulates you, wakes you up, but it cleanses and purifies."

• • •

Blessing Devices - Prayer of the Artificer

C3 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Our devices (computers, phones) are vibrationally near to our aura and consciousness. They are made of metallic ores from the earth, shaped by generations of human ingenuity — and can be regarded as having spiritual quality.

The Practice

Place fingertips on your device and recite:

"Oh, Artificer of the heavens and the earth, bless this artifact. Shower it with Thy love and light, and let it glorify Thy holy name. Amen."

The Understanding

  • Our homes and devices become extensions of ourselves, imbued with our thoughts and intentions — and can be treated as mirrors of our consciousness.
  • The internet is a mirror of the human condition — full of troubled impressions and unawakened impulses. Rather than fleeing it, the path calls us to meet it wisely and transformatively, navigating it with awareness.
• • •

Saum Prayer Movement Instructions

C3 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Standing upright is itself a practice of concentration — an art the trees have perfected. "Send a root right down into the depths of the earth." The movements of the prayer begin from a place of strength, not from being crushed by the world's weight.

"Find the place of your strength — and then offer your obeisance."

The Sequence of Movements

  1. Palms forward — releasing weight from the shoulders, opening the chest, letting air in. "Praise be to the most supreme God."
  1. Hands draw closer together — "Omnipotent, omnipresent, all-pervading."
  1. Hands come down to sides — "The Only Being. Take us in Thy parental arms."
  1. Bend forward, hands on knees — "Raise us from the denseness of the earth."
  1. Rise, then lean forward with palms extended toward the ground — "The only do we worship. Toward the alone do we aspire."
  1. Hands together at waist — "Most merciful and compassionate God, the idealized sovereign of the whole humanity."
  1. Open the heart center (Qalb) — "Open our hearts toward Thy beauty. Illuminate our souls with divine light."
  1. The Qalb-Ruh connection, then Khafi-Nafs connection — invoking the subtle anatomy.
  1. Final surrender — "Pour upon us Thy love and Thy light... Draw us closer to Thee every moment of our life until in us be reflected Thy grace, Thy glory, Thy wisdom, Thy joy and Thy peace. Amen."

Practice Notes

At first the movements feel clunky and require thought. With practice they become fluid and natural — like water, no longer requiring conscious attention as the gestures and words merge into one living prayer.

• • •

Sleep and Waking Practices — Nostril and Threshold Work

C3 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Understanding Sleep and Meditation

Sleep and meditation are intimately related — sleep is the same process as meditation, with the one difference that in meditation we are awake. Sleep rejuvenates by turning energy inward, guiding us into transcendental spheres, and then gradually outward again.

Waking suddenly from deep sleep disrupts the natural transition through the planes — it is not conducive to wholeness.

The task: bring the outer world and inner world into communication by honoring thresholds.

The Nostril Practice on Waking

The Technique
  • Right side sleep promotes the left (lunar) nostril — conducive to deep sleep
  • Before waking, shift to the left side — this activates the right (solar) nostril, preparing for outward daytime consciousness
  • This mirrors the threshold practice of stepping through doors right foot first

"As you are nearing the time of waking up, switch sides — and then you emerge out of dreams."

Dream Recollection Practice

  1. On waking, pause — do not leap immediately into the day
  2. Gently bring with you the most salient images and words of the dream
  3. Adventitious impressions from the dream — release them; let them dissolve
  4. Meaningful dream content — carry it into the day and contemplate its significance

Threshold Practices

The Invocation on Waking

"I recommend saying the invocation when you wake up — so the very first idea, the very first words that come from your mouth consist of this orientation to the absolute and to the soul of creation."

Right Foot First

Step out of bed right foot first. The threshold of waking is honored exactly as the threshold of a doorway.

Water Drinking Practice

Drinking a glass of water first thing in the morning is recommended. The instruction: drink it with full awareness of its living-ness.

  • Water flows down from the icy peaks — the purest drink
  • Our bodies are most essentially made of this substance
  • Drink in thankfulness
• • •

Sleep, Waking and Dream Recollection Practices

C3 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Sleep and meditation are intimately related — sleep is the same process as meditation, with the one difference that in meditation we are awake. Sleep rejuvenates by turning energy inward, guiding us into transcendental spheres, and then gradually outward again.

The Problem with Sudden Waking

Waking suddenly from deep sleep disrupts the natural transition through the planes — it is not conducive to wholeness.

The task: bring the outer world and inner world into communication by honoring thresholds.

The Nostril Practice on Waking

  • Right side sleep promotes the left (lunar) nostril — conducive to deep sleep.
  • Before waking, shift to the left side — this activates the right (solar) nostril, preparing for outward daytime consciousness.
  • This mirrors the threshold practice of stepping through doors right foot first.

"As you are nearing the time of waking up, switch sides — and then you emerge out of dreams."

  1. On waking, pause — do not leap immediately into the day.
  2. Gently bring with you the most salient images and words of the dream.
  3. Adventitious impressions from the dream — release them; let them dissolve.

Morning Threshold Practices

Daily Task - Avoid the Word "I"

C4 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Do not say the word "I" for the next 24 hours.

Instructions

  • The previous task (stepping through doorways right foot first) has run its course
  • The new task: abstain from using the word "I" (the self-reference pronoun) for 24 hours
  • Permitted alternatives — "we," "one," "this person," or simply avoid self-reference altogether
  • Any substitution is acceptable — no choice is better than another
  • The only commitment — abstain from the specific word

Purpose

A direct practice in ego-observation and dis-identification with the personal self.

The Body as Temple — Opening Movement

C6 · September 14, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

C6 opened with gentle movement practices to awaken the body and prepare it as a sacred vessel for spiritual presence.

"We spoke of the body as a temple — and with the kinds of movements that re-up the circulation and the breath, that temple comes into still fuller cohesion and becomes a more spacious vessel for the spirit to function in."

"So it's really a blessing whenever we can experience this kind of fluidity and opening up of the channels."

Teaching

The body is understood as a temple — a sacred space that houses the spirit. Through gentle movements that awaken circulation and breath, this temple comes into fuller coherence and becomes a more spacious vessel for the spirit to function within.

The practice involves movements that create fluidity and open the channels, preparing the physical form to be a worthy container for spiritual presence and practice.

Daily Practice - Think of God After Every Statement

C8 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Practice

"Throughout the day, whenever you speak — whether a short phrase or a long sentence — when you're finished speaking, when you take a pause — think of God. Remember God. Just for a moment, just for a second."

The Mystery Beyond Speculation

"Whatever God means to you — we may not even know what we mean when we use a word that evokes the mystery that confounds all speculation. But it's enough just to invoke the being of beings, just to gesture within yourself toward the absolute."

Simple Implementation

After everything you say, for a moment — think of God. That is the task for today.

This practice works with:

  • Short phrases
  • Long sentences
  • Natural pauses in conversation
  • Any moment of speaking

The Gesture Toward the Absolute

The practice doesn't require theological certainty or conceptual clarity about God. It's enough to:

  • Invoke the being of beings
  • Gesture within yourself toward the absolute
  • Remember the Source for just a moment
  • Touch the mystery that underlies all speech

Integration with Daily Life

This transforms ordinary conversation into a continuous practice of remembrance, weaving the sacred into the mundane rhythm of daily communication.

• • •

The Swing of Breath - Ha Practice

C9 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Childhood Swing Memory

"Do you remember, as a child, swinging on a swing? The sheer delight of it — but why was that experience so peaceful and exhilarating at the same time?"

The movements of the swing imitate the movements of the breath:

  • Inhale = swing swings back and up — reaching the farthest place behind and above, a perch where for a fraction of a second the swing pauses
  • Exhale = swing swings forward and out and up — then a momentary perch at the end of exhalation

Each half mirrors the other — inward and outward, descending and ascending

Body Mechanics of the Swing

"Do you remember what you did as a child to make the swing go further and further? When you swung forward, you leaned back and pushed your feet out — and so the outward swing was lengthened. And then when the momentum turned and you fell back, you leaned forward — and so the inward swing was boosted."

"The farther in you went, the further out you went. And the further out you went, the further in and up you went. Each half of the movement mirrored the other half."

The swing swings between the outer and the inner, between the visible and the invisible, between the world and the soul.

Grounding — The Earth Beneath

The frame on which the swing hangs is standing on the ground. Feel two feet planted on the floor, tailbone rooted in the chair. Beneath the floor: ground, crust, mantle, core.

"The core is said to be hotter than the sun — so that in its way, the Earth is a star."

"To give one's attention to it is to begin to notice the upwelling of chthonic energy, telluric life — which moves in the tailbone, in the channel that arises from the tailbone up through the spinal shaft, through the belly, up into the chest."

Ha — The Sacred Sound in the Chest

In the chest, the current of life becomes a resonance — the sound of the breath vibrating in the thoracic cavity: Ah, Ah.

"It's said that the words La ilaha illa Allah boil down to three sounds: Ha, Hu, and He. And the Ha is in the chest, and it has its roots deep in the earth."

Each of these three Beej mantras — Ha, Hu, He — corresponds to one of the dimensions of the primal created being, which is to say: the universe itself.

Ha = the body of the primal/universal creature

The Little Body and the Great Body

Our body is a fraction of the body of the whole universe — and in each fraction, the whole is represented:

"The design of this body epitomizes, summarizes everything that is in the universe. We're a miniature of the cosmos."

"We are establishing a rapport between the little body — our own personal body — and the great body, the body of the universe. The two are linked."

"We're offering our own little body to our own great body, which is the universe itself. And we're offering the great body to this little body in the chest, resounding."

Practice Instructions — Ha × 11

  1. Sit straight but relaxed — shoulders open, chest open, belly rising and falling
  2. Ground: feel feet on floor, tailbone rooted, Earth's telluric energy rising through the spine
  3. On the breath, intone Ha eleven times
  4. As you intone, offer the little body to the great body, and receive the great body into the little

Ha… Ha… Ha… (×11)

This practice is to be done every day.

Ittisal Conjunction

"This is the first in a sequence of intonations, connecting us with the cosmic person by way of Ittisal conjunction."

Ittisal (Arabic: اتصال) = junction, connection, conjunction — the mystical union between the individual soul and the cosmic being. Ha is the first link in this sequence.

• • •

Walking Practice — Two-Year Encouragement

C10 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Pir Zia closed the teaching content with an ongoing practice prescription for the full two-year Suluk arc.

The Prescription

"Over the next two years, I would like to encourage you to walk from time to time. Go for a walk every day if possible — but as often as you can. And this walk will be a space of practice."

Beginning Instructions

"In your first walks, it's enough just to do this: feel your footsteps. Feel gravity holding you to the earth. And feel every footstep — feel the touch of the earth. Feel the contact between your body and the ground and value it, honor it."

"These feet won't always step this way. Each step is an intimate act. So walk when you can, and feel every footstep."

Closing Sufi Saying

"Let your soul be where your soles are. Let your soles be where your soul is."

Purpose

This walking practice grounds all the interior work of the five days — concentration, breath, self-awareness, sensory refinement — into bodily presence, into earth contact, into every day of the two-year journey.

Part I · Chapter 6

TEACHINGS & WISDOM

The Living Transmission

The living transmission of the Inayati lineage. Pir Zia brought the teachings of his grandfather Hazrat Inayat Khan alive through personal commentary, deep scholarly knowledge, and luminous presence across all 10 sessions.

46 Entries · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

✿

Amān — The Opening Prayer of Each Suluk Day

Source: Concentration P1 · C1 · 2025-09-12 · Pir Zia Inayat-Khan

Meaning of Amān

Amān = Sanctuary · Safety · Security · Protection · Refuge

Purpose

Each day of Suluk begins with the prayer Amān. It is not a prayer of denial or avoidance — it is a prayer of compassionate witness. Before turning toward the divine, before entering practice, the Salik pauses to acknowledge:

  • That all is not well in this world
  • That there is great suffering, tremendous violence, and injustice
  • That human beings both endure and inflict tremendous pain upon each other

The Cosmological Context

In the story of Mount Qaf, it was precisely this vision — the Earth foreseeing the tragedies, violence, and heartbreak of humanity's history — that caused her to wobble in her orbit. God's response was to raise Mount Qaf as an anchor.

The prayer Amān holds this same awareness:

"We begin each of our days with the prayer Amān to acknowledge that all is not well in this world, that there is great suffering, that there is tremendous violence and injustice in our very time. And can you imagine the mind and the heart of the earth foreseeing all of this?"

Practice Note

Amān is said at the beginning of each day during Suluk — before other practices. It grounds the spiritual work in compassionate awareness of the world's condition, making the entire practice a form of service and refuge for the world.

• • •

Arabic & Sufi Terms — Concentration P1 · C1

**Suluk**Travel; fine mannerThe path of intentional inner travel + the art of traveling well
**Salik** (pl. Saliks)Traveler on the pathOne who undertakes the Suluk journey intentionally
**Sohbet**Heart-centered conversationA form of spiritual companionship and sharing
**Murshid / Pir**Spiritual guide / ElderHazrat Pir-o-Murshid Inayat Khan — transmitter of the Inayatiyya

**Lahut**Divine planeFourth plane — realm of pure divinity
**HaHut**Plane of the AbsoluteFifth and highest plane — the Absolute beyond all names
**Divan**The League of BodhisattvasSpiritual guardians of the world; their seat is the emerald peak of Mount Qaf

**Gayathri**Sacred hymnsHymns transmitted through Pir-o-Murshid; used throughout Suluk

Concentration — The First Stage of Suluk

Source: Concentration P1 · C1 · 2025-09-12 · Pir Zia Inayat-Khan

Definition

"Concentration means the whole of you is in one place. You are not scattered. You are not dispersed. You are not diffused. You are gathered."
"Concentration means to be whole, not fragmented. To be fully there, not absent."

Why Concentration is the Foundation

"If one can learn to concentrate, then one can pray. If one can learn to concentrate, then one can meditate. If one can learn to concentrate, then one can create. If one can learn to concentrate, then one can love. The whole of life depends on concentration."

The Challenge

Our habitual state is one of distraction — constantly scattered across tasks and thoughts. Concentration requires pulling attention back, centering it, and staying with one thing. This can feel uncomfortable at first — boring, wasteful, unproductive — because we are conditioned to distraction.

Common reactions when beginning concentration practice:

  • Feels wasteful or boring
  • The action seems to be "somewhere else"
  • Impatience — "I just don't have the patience for it"

The Cultivation

Concentration is not about suppressing energy but molding it. The energy of interest, desire, love, or will — when flung in all directions, it is scattered; when gathered with intention, it deepens.

"If one has the intention to take ownership of your attention — to take it into your own care, to allow it to slow down, to give it breathing room — you may find that actually there is a satisfaction. It isn't the obvious gratification. It's a different kind of satisfaction. But it grows and it deepens."

Integration with Daily Life

Concentration is not separate from life's responsibilities. It infuses family, work, and ordinary moments with presence. The practices of Suluk are rehearsals for living this quality of attentive presence in every moment.

"The cultivation of concentration is not about separating or segregating the practice from our daily life and responsibilities but integrating it in every action and every moment."

The Four Stages (Overview)

  1. Concentration — gathering scattered attention into presence
  2. Contemplation — dwelling with a quality of being
  3. Meditation — experiencing pure essence beyond quality
  4. Realization — returning to the visible world with the invisible essence illumining all
• • •

Source: Concentration P1 · C1 · 2025-09-12 · Pir Zia Inayat-Khan

On the Journey

"We're like a flock of birds that have landed in a field and are having a look at each other and just wondering what it's going to be like to form a murmuration in the sky to fly together."
"The journey is a journey of recollection — recollecting yourselves, bringing the parts back together. Remembrance — bringing the different members back into unity."
"Our intention is to reunite body with mind, mind with heart, heart with soul, soul with the soul of souls. And in the process we'll see that what might have seemed at the beginning like an individual journey is in fact the journey of the whole universe."
"Everyone comes from the same source, is returning to the source, is sustained all the while by the source."
"We are there for each other on the hilltops, but also in the shadowed valleys."
"In this world, there is no friendship like the friendship on the path." — Sayed Abu Hashim Madani

On Intention

"If the intention is clear, if it's sincere, if it's focused, we'll get through everything easily."
"There's a spark in us. There's a gem seeking its mine. A spark seeking the sun."
"All of the prayers, all of the practices, all of the readings, all of the conversations, everything we'll do is simply fuel for that ember. The flame is already there."
"The eyes must be sun-like to see the sun."
"The truth that is awakening in your spirit is looking for a mirror. And our intention here, all of us, is to be a mirror to each other."
"Al-Mu'min Mir'atu'l-Mu'min — The believer is a mirror to the believer."

"Concentration means the whole of you is in one place. You are not scattered. You are not dispersed. You are not diffused. You are gathered."
"If one can learn to concentrate, then one can pray. If one can learn to concentrate, then one can meditate. If one can learn to concentrate, then one can create. If one can learn to concentrate, then one can love. The whole of life depends on concentration."

"A Salik could do one practice for their whole life and reach the divine presence."

Mount Qaf — The Spiritual Mountain and the Name of This Class

Source: Concentration P1 · C1 · 2025-09-12 · Pir Zia Inayat-Khan

The Story of the Earth and Mount Qaf

When God created the Earth, she was revolving in space in a rapture of ecstasy, dreaming of the life that would unfold — oceans, continents, greenery, animals, birds, and finally the human being. Her vision filled her with joy. But as she foresaw the course of humanity's history — the tragedies, the violence, the suffering that human beings would not only endure but inflict on each other — she came face to face with heartbreak.

She began to shake. She began to wobble in her orbit.

All the heavens were focused on her. Something was needed. And so God decreed the raising up of a monumental mountain. And that mountain was established. Though not visible to eyes of flesh, it encompasses the Earth. Its roots work through the roots of all the mountain ranges of the earth and feed those mountain ranges. Its roots are sunk deep into the mantle of the earth and into the earth's core.

The Function of Mount Qaf

Mount Qaf is a great spiritual circulatory system — a cosmic anchor between the Earth and the divine realms.

It mounts through the planes of existence:

  • Nasut — Physical plane
  • Malakut — Angelic / subtle plane
  • Jabrut — Plane of power / force
  • Lahut — Divine plane
  • HaHut — Plane of the Absolute

This creates a direct connection between the physical earth and the spiritual depths from which it emerges — anchoring the earth in the invisible.

The Emerald Peak and the Divan

"At the crown of the mountain is an emerald peak. Emerald — in the alchemy of Sufism — is the color that outlasts all others, sums them all up, and bespeaks the perfect integration of all opposites. There the Divan, the League of Bodhisattvas who guard and guide the world, have their seat."

The emerald symbolizes the perfect integration of all opposites — the marriage of visible and invisible, earth and heaven, fragmentation and wholeness.

This Class Is Named Mount Qaf

The Suluk class of 2025–2027 is named Mount Qaf (Qaf) — the cosmic mountain that stabilizes, anchors, and connects. A fitting name for a fellowship of travelers seeking to anchor themselves in the spiritual while living fully in the physical.

• • •

Saum and Salat — The Two Daily Prayers of Suluk

Source: Concentration P1 · C1 · 2025-09-12 · Pir Zia Inayat-Khan

Overview

Two prayers transmitted through Pir-o-Murshid Inayat Khan form the daily foundation of Suluk practice. Both involve specific postures, gestures, and words, and are said together every day — in group or individually.

The Two Prayers

PrayerMeaningAddressed To
**Saum**ReposeThe One Divine Being
**Salat / Salawat**BenedictionThe Light of the Rasool — Spirit of Guidance, first of creation

Salat — Deeper Description

"Salat is addressed to the spirit of guidance, the first of creation, that first manifested light from which the world derives, and which constitutes the luminous core through which the divine guidance pours into the world, and which is embodied in the consciousness of all who are awakened to the divine truth."

Key Teachings

  • These prayers are not intended to displace the prayers of one's own religion
  • They "shine a light that reveals the depths of your faith even more clearly than ever before"
  • They deepen the relationship with the divine being and with the light of guidance
  • They subtly bring travelers closer to each other in the inner worlds
  • Say them every day — in group or individually
  • Both prayers involve gestures as well as words

Note on the Inayatiyya

The Inayatiyya is not a religion. These are hymns and orisons that connect the Salik to the inspiration that came through the Murshid and to fellow travelers in the inner worlds.

• • •

Suluk Class Names — A Legacy of Beautiful Names

Source: Concentration P1 · C1 · 2025-09-12 · Pir Zia Inayat-Khan

The Tradition

Each Suluk caravan receives its own unique name reflecting the spiritual character and collective spirit of that particular gathering. Each configuration of Saliks has its own soul.

"Each, each configuration of Saliks has its own character. And that becomes even more palpable as we go along, as we're weaving our prayers, our practices, meeting together, speaking together, getting to know each other, helping each other. A vessel is emerging."

Previous Class Names

Class NameMeaning / Description
**Khosar**River of Paradise (first four classes named after rivers of paradise)
**Kafur**River of Paradise
**Salsabil**River of Paradise
**Tasneem**River of Paradise
**Nasim**The breeze that blows through the garden
**Gulzar**The rose garden
**Zindarud**The living river
**Luluvamarjan**Pearls and coral — the spiritual treasures deep in the ocean of soul

This Class — Mount Qaf (2025–2027)

The current class is named Mount Qaf — the invisible spiritual mountain that anchors the Earth between the physical and divine planes, whose emerald peak is the seat of the Divan — the League of Bodhisattvas who guard and guide the world.

Khalwat dar Anjuman

The vessel that forms through the class is described by the Sufi concept of Khalwat dar Anjuman — "solitude in the crowd" — meaning that even when the Saliks are scattered across the world meditating in silence, they are meeting each other in the inner worlds through the intention that has joined them.

• • •

The Five Planes of Existence — Nasut, Malakut, Jabrut, Lahut, HaHut

Source: Concentration P1 · C1 · 2025-09-12 · Pir Zia Inayat-Khan

The Five Planes

In the Sufi cosmological framework of the Inayatiyya, existence is understood through five ascending planes. Mount Qaf serves as the spiritual circulatory system connecting all of them:

PlaneArabic NameDescription
1st**Nasut**The physical plane — the world of matter and ordinary sensory experience
2nd**Malakut**The angelic / subtle plane — realm of subtle forms, images, inner perception
3rd**Jabrut**The plane of power / force — realm of divine attributes and qualities
4th**Lahut**The divine plane — realm of pure divinity, beyond name and form
5th**HaHut**The plane of the Absolute — the Absolute, beyond all planes, beyond all comprehension

Mount Qaf as Connector

Mount Qaf is described as a great spiritual circulatory system that creates a direct vertical connection between all five planes — from the physical earth all the way to the Absolute.

"There's a great spiritual circulatory system that functions through the mountain — visible mountain ranges which culminate in the invisible mountain that in turn mounts up through the plains from Nasut to Malakut, from Malakut to Jabrut, from Jabrut to Lahut, and onto HaHut, through all of the planes, creating connection between them on Earth in the most direct possible way, anchoring the Earth in the spiritual depths from which the Earth emerges."

The Divan at the Summit

At the emerald peak of Mount Qaf (highest visible point of the invisible mountain) sits the Divan — the League of Bodhisattvas who guard and guide the world. Their emerald seat symbolizes the perfect integration of all opposites — the marriage of every plane.

Relevance to Practice

Understanding the five planes provides the cosmological map for the four stages of Suluk:

  • Concentration operates primarily in Nasut (physical, sensory)
  • Contemplation begins to access Malakut (subtle, quality)
  • Meditation approaches Jabrut (essence, beyond quality)
  • Realization recognizes that all planes are present simultaneously — the Absolute as the context of everything
• • •

The Standing Posture Before Prayer — Embodying the Alif

Source: Concentration P1 · C1 · 2025-09-12 · Pir Zia Inayat-Khan

The Posture

Before prayer, one stands and settles into the posture of the upright line — the Alif:

  • Feet firmly on the ground — like roots of a tree
  • Spine erect — like the trunk of the tree
  • Tailbone sends a root deep into the earth
  • Crown of the head open to the vastness of sky and space beyond
  • Grounded in the density of the earth below; overlit by the heavens above

Only when this orientation is experienced does one begin with the words "Praise be to thee..."

The Symbolism of the Upright Line (Alif)

"The upright line suggests the one, and the number one is represented by an upright line. The upright line suggests heaven, perfection, straightforwardness, firmness, life, rising, and unity — as it shows oneness with the whole. The upright line is the first line, and all forms and figures are nothing but the change of direction of that line."

The Alif is the Arabic letter from which Allah begins. It is the root from which all other letters emerge. To embody the Alif is to embody unity itself.

Practice Instruction

Stand. Feel your two feet on the ground. Feel yourself like a tree rooted in the ground. Spine like the trunk of the tree. Tailbone sends a root deep into the earth. Crown at the top of the head open to the vastness of sky. Experience this grounding and openness. Then begin the prayer.

• • •

The Story of the Boy and the Alif — Quality Over Quantity

Source: Concentration P1 · C1 · 2025-09-12 · Pir Zia Inayat-Khan

The Story

In a village in the Punjab, a teacher was teaching children the Arabic alphabet — beginning with Alif, the straight upright line. One child showed exceptional enthusiasm for the Alif. When the teacher moved on to the next letters, every other child followed — but this boy kept writing Alif.

The teacher grew frustrated. The parents tried to encourage the boy to move on. But he simply could not or would not leave the Alif. Feeling that he had disappointed everyone, he left home and went out into the jungle. He was not seen for many years.

One day, the same teacher was teaching a new group of children in the same classroom. Suddenly, a man entered — approached the blackboard — and wrote Alif. A great light filled the room, and the room shook. Everyone could see that he had truly understood the meaning of one thing.

He went on to master Bay, Tay, Se — and became one of the greatest Sufi poets of the land.

The Teaching

"This is a story about the power of the straight line. It's the story of the power of standing straight — rooted in the earth, tailbone grounded, crown open to the heavens. That posture — it's a story of the power of it. It's also a story about quality rather than quantity."

The boy's story carries multiple layers of meaning:

  • Power of the Alif — unity, oneness, divine perfection as root of all things
  • Quality over quantity — one thing practiced with wholeness transforms more than a thousand things collected
  • Wholehearted giving — the essence is not the technique but the spirit with which one gives oneself to the work
"A Salik could do one practice for their whole life and reach the divine presence. It's good to learn the techniques that have been passed down, but the essence of it all is the spirit in which we give ourselves to this work — the faith, the wholeheartedness. This is what transforms."

Application to Suluk

In Suluk, there are many subjects and many practices. One could spend a lifetime accumulating forms — hundreds of practices, thousands of books. But what transforms is not accumulation. It is bringing one's whole being to whatever the practice is.

• • •

The Suluk Journey — Path of Recollection and Unity

Source: Concentration P1 · C1 · 2025-09-12 · Pir Zia Inayat-Khan

The Nature of the Journey

"The journey is a journey of recollection — recollecting yourselves, bringing the parts back together. Remembrance — bringing the different members back into unity. And not only within ourselves, because what is a self? A self itself is a fragment of a greater whole. The journey is one of rediscovery, of long-forgotten unities, the revelation of patterns, connections, affinities that bring wholeness to a world that is otherwise broken apart in our psyche."

The Suluk Path is a Path of Recollection and Unity. Its purpose: to reunite body with mind, mind with heart, heart with soul, soul with the soul of souls.

"Our intention is to reunite body with mind, mind with heart, heart with soul, soul with the soul of souls. And in the process, we'll see that what might have seemed at the beginning like an individual journey is in fact the journey of the whole universe."

The Caravan Within the Caravan

Participants form a close-knit fellowship — a caravan within the caravan. Like a flock of birds learning to fly in murmuration, they travel together in familiar and unfamiliar territory, supporting each other across hilltops and shadowed valleys.

The Meaning of SULUK

The word carries two inseparable meanings:

  1. Travel — the universal inner journey
  2. Fine Manner — the art of traveling well: gently, thoughtfully, considerately, wisely, discerningly, balanced

These two are not separate. To travel on this path is to cultivate the manner of travel itself.

Intentional Journey

"If there is a difference, it's only this — that we're making a decision here to journey intentionally. We're aware that this is a journey and we want to, as far as possible, travel well."

Everyone is a seeker. Everyone comes from the same source, is returning to the source, is sustained all the while by the source. The difference for the Salik is the intention to journey consciously — following those who blazed the trail before.

The Friendship on the Path

Murshid Sayed Abu Hashim Madani said: "In this world, there is no friendship like the friendship on the path."

This friendship widens — step by step one realizes that everyone encountered is in media res, in the midst of a journey embedded within the journey of the whole of being.

• • •

Previous Suluk Class Names and Their Meanings

C1 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Each Suluk caravan receives its own name that reflects its particular spiritual character. The tradition began with the first four classes named after the rivers of paradise:

The Named Classes

  1. Khosar — River of Paradise
  2. Kafur — River of Paradise
  3. Salsabil — River of Paradise
  4. Tasneem — River of Paradise
  5. Nasim — The breeze that blows through the garden
  6. Gulzar — The rose garden
  7. Zindarud — The living river
  8. Luluvamarjan — Pearls and coral (spiritual treasures deep in the ocean of soul)
  9. Mount Qaf — The cosmic anchor (this current class)

The Pattern of Naming

The names progress through beautiful spiritual imagery:

  • Rivers of Paradise (the first four classes)
  • Garden imagery (breeze and rose garden)
  • Living waters (the living river)
  • Ocean treasures (pearls and coral from the depths)
  • Cosmic mountain (the spiritual anchor between realms)

Each name captures both the unique character of that particular group and their place in the ongoing tradition of Suluk classes.

The Power of Intention in Suluk

C1 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Supreme Importance of Intention

The sincerity and clarity of intention is the single most important factor in the Suluk journey.

"If the intention is clear, if it's sincere, if it's focused, we'll get through everything easily."

A clear, focused, sincere intention overcomes all obstacles. A murky or half-hearted intention limits progress regardless of favorable outer circumstances.

The Inner Spark Already Knows

There is already a spark within each seeker — a gem seeking its mine, a spark seeking the sun. All prayers, practices, readings, and conversations are fuel for this existing ember. The work of Suluk is to shelter, kindle, and center this flame.

"The eyes must be sun-like to see the sun. Whatever elevates you, inspires you, motivates you, reassures you, consoles you — it does so because it meets in you the truth that is already there."

Mirroring the Divine

Al-Mu'min Mir'atu'l-Mu'min — The believer is a mirror to the believer.

The spirit of companionship on this path is to mirror the divinity shining out from each one.

Key Points on Intention

  • Sincerity of purpose matters most — clear intention overcomes all obstacles
  • Murky or half-hearted intention limits progress even in ideal circumstances
  • The inner spark already knows where to go — it hears the call
  • Prayers, practices, readings, conversations: all are fuel for the ember
  • Shelter, kindle, and center the flame — let it glow and blaze
  • Eyes must be sun-like to see the sun — inner truth recognizes outer truth
  • The believer is a mirror to the believer — we mirror each other's divinity
• • •

The Suluk Journey - Path of Recollection and Unity

C1 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Essence of Suluk

The Suluk Path is fundamentally a Path of Recollection and Unity. Participants form a 'caravan within the caravan' — a close-knit fellowship traveling together like birds learning to fly in murmuration.

"The journey is a journey of recollection — recollecting yourselves, bringing the parts back together. Remembrance — bringing the different members back into unity. And not only within ourselves, because what is a self? A self itself is a fragment of a greater whole."

The Process of Reunification

The journey involves reuniting:

  • Body with mind
  • Mind with heart
  • Heart with soul
  • Soul with the soul of souls
"Everyone comes from the same source, is returning to the source, is sustained all the while by the source."

The Dual Meaning of SULUK

The word SULUK carries two meanings:

  1. Travel - the journey itself
  2. Fine manner - a way of being that is gentle, thoughtful, considerate, wise, discerning, and balanced

Suluk is both the journey and the art of traveling well.

Key Characteristics of the Suluk Journey

  • Caravan within the caravan — a fellowship of intentional travelers
  • Sohbet: heart-centered conversation as a vehicle of companionship
  • Present for each other — on hilltops and in shadowed valleys
  • Unique friendship: 'In this world there is no friendship like the friendship on the path' — Sayed Abu Hashim Madani
  • Everyone is a seeker — the circle of companionship widens beyond the class
  • Decision to journey intentionally — aware of the path, traveling well
  • Following those who blazed the trail — inheriting maps and directions
