Breath as Medium of Teaching - Saheb al-Anfas

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

"When I'm speaking and you're listening, the medium between us is the air. It's air that is carrying the current of the words, air that's vibrating. The medium between us is breath."

Key Principles

  • There is no voice without breath
  • There is no speech without respiration
  • When we go into silence, when the words fall away, what remains is inhalation and exhalation
  • Breath moves between what is outside of us and what is within us — between mind and body, and even between mind and soul

We pay attention to people's words and judgments — but how much attention do we pay to the breath? For Suluk, this is at the center of everything.

Saheb al-Anfas

"One of the definitions of a Sufi is 'Saheb al-Anfas' — one who breathes well. The possessor of breaths."

• • •

Heart-to-Heart Teaching Story - Hazrat Inayat Khan and His Murshid

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Hazrat Inayat Khan, though born into a family with a Sufi tradition, sought a living teacher. When he found his Murshid — a retired scholar — he visited him regularly. For months, months, the Murshid spoke only of ordinary things: milk, butter, different kinds of trees.

"Finally, one day, the Murshid began to speak about the planes of being. And Hazrat's ears perked up and he discreetly took out a notebook. And just as soon as Hazrat took out his notebook, the Murshid went back to speaking about the ordinary things."

Hazrat always looked back on this as a real teaching: his Murshid intended him to receive whatever was coming through directly in his heart — without differentiating between the obviously mystical and the apparently ordinary.

Core Teachings

  • Transmission happens heart-to-heart — true wisdom isn't only in mystical words but in presence
  • Don't separate the ordinary from the sacred — all speech carries spiritual meaning when received openly
  • The real notebook is the heart — teachings are first inscribed inwardly through deep attention
  • Presence over documentation — the living moment takes priority

Note on Note-Taking

"This isn't because there is a proscription against taking notes in our order. In later times, among Hazrat's own circle, he sometimes asked for those present to note down his words. It isn't that notes are a bad thing, but we're lucky in Suluk that there is no need for any of you to take down notes. The notes are taken anyway and shared with you. So you can just give your whole attention to this moment, put aside pen and paper, and just be with what's coming through."

• • •

Heart-to-Heart Teaching and Sacred Transmission

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Pir Zia opened with a profound story from Hazrat Inayat Khan's relationship with his Murshid, illustrating the true nature of spiritual transmission.

Though born into a Sufi family, Hazrat sought a living teacher and found one. He would visit his Murshid regularly at home, and the Murshid received him warmly. Yet for months, the Murshid spoke only of ordinary things: milk, butter, trees.

One day the Murshid began speaking of the higher planes of being. Hazrat eagerly reached for a notebook — and immediately the Murshid returned to ordinary conversation. Hazrat later saw this as the real teaching.

"Not to differentiate between what seemed obviously mystical and what didn't seem particularly mystical — but instead just to listen to everything, take in everything, and engrave it on the notebook of your heart."

Core Principles

  • Transmission happens heart-to-heart — wisdom lives in presence, not just in "mystical" words
  • Do not separate the ordinary from the sacred — all speech, all encounter, is transmission when received with openness
  • The real notebook is the heart — teachings must first be inscribed inwardly through deep attention
  • Presence over documentation — in Suluk, notes are taken and shared; students can give full attention to the living moment
  • Timeless connection — reading Murshid's words a century later still brings his presence alive
• • •

Murshid's Complete Teaching on Breath - The Secret of Both Worlds

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

"To a mystic, the subject of breath is the deepest of all the subjects with which mysticism or philosophy is concerned. Because breath is the most important thing in life. The very life of the human being is breath. One lives in the presence of breath, and in the absence of breath, one is called a corpse."

"Breath is that which keeps all of the parts in connection with each other, working together, depending upon one another. It is that which enables one to move, to put one's muscles into action, to keep the whole mechanism of the body at work. There is no other force or power concerned with all this than the power of breath."

"Wherever we look — be it the changes of the seasons, the changes of the weather, or even the constant circles which the Earth describes on its journey — all these show the same underlying current, the current of the whole of nature, which is the real breath."

"The whole universe is going on with a certain rhythm. There is a current which keeps the whole universe going. It is one breath, and yet it is many breaths."

"Breath is a channel through which all the expression of the innermost life can be given. Breath is an electric current that runs between the everlasting life and the mortal frame. Those who have attained any intuition or miraculous power have achieved it by the help of the breath."

The Spine as Serpent

"The breath makes a circuit through the body, and the channel through which it makes the circuit is the spine. The mystics give this channel great importance. They call it the serpent. They picture it as a serpent holding its tail in its mouth. In almost all symbols, the serpent represents the channel of the breath."

"When this channel is made clear by the method of breathing, this is not only a help to physical health, but it also opens up the faculties of intuition and the doors that are within, where lies the real happiness of the human being."

"In order to clear this channel of all that blocks the way, one must follow the rules of mystical ablutions and of rhythmic breathing."

The Master Key

"People look for phenomena, but there is no better phenomena than breath itself. Because breath is life and light, and in the breath is the source of life and light. The mastery of breath is the secret of both worlds."

• • •

Murshid's Teaching on Breath as Life and Light

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Pir Zia read directly from Hazrat Inayat Khan's writings on breath:

"Breath is the most important thing in life. The very life of the human being is breath. One lives in the presence of breath, and in the absence of breath, one is called a corpse."

"The whole universe is going on with a certain rhythm. There is a current which keeps the whole universe going. It is one breath, and yet it is many breaths."

"Breath is an electric current that runs between the everlasting life and the mortal frame. Those who have attained any intuition or miraculous power have achieved it by the help of the breath."

"The breath makes a circuit through the body, and the channel through which it makes the circuit is the spine. The mystics call it the serpent. When this channel is made clear by the method of breathing, it opens up the faculties of intuition and the doors within, where lies the real happiness of the human being."

"Breath is life and light, and in the breath is the source of life and light. The mastery of breath is the secret of both worlds."

Key Principles

  • Breath is life — without it, the body is a corpse; with it, we live in constant connection
  • Breath is the bridge — linking body, mind, and soul; connecting the mortal with the eternal
  • The whole cosmos moves in one great rhythm — it is one breath expressed through many breaths
  • The spine is the channel (the serpent) — when purified through rhythmic breathing, intuition and spiritual faculties awaken
  • Saheb al-Anfas — the Sufi definition: one who breathes well, the possessor of breaths
  • Air and breath is the vibratory medium that carries words between speaker and listener
• • •

Sensus Communis - The Sense Within All Senses

C2 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Socratic Development

"What is it that sees through eyes and hears through ears and tastes through the tongue and smells through the nose and touches with fingertips? What do these five senses all have in common? They're all sensory apparatuses — they all participate in sensation itself. Sensation moves through five different channels, but those channels converge in essential sensing: the common sense."

Key Concepts

  • Sensus Communis = Latin for 'common sense' — the sense within all senses
  • Synesthesia — Sometimes senses criss-cross: hearing a colour, seeing a taste
  • All senses are expressions of one aspect of mind: sensation itself — an expression of presence and attention

Hudur and Ilm-e-Huzuri

Hudur (Arabic) = Presence — the foundation of all knowing

Ilm-e-Huzuri — Knowledge by Presence

"Sufis speak of that way of knowing which is called Ilm-e-Huzuri — knowledge by presence. All knowledge has this as its foundation: pure attention. The physical senses are just extensions of it. And even when the senses close — in sleep or in death — that light of attention continues, but turned inward."

Cultivating Attention

"It's like a plasma that can be shaped however the will wishes. And it can be grown, it can be intensified. If it's not cultivated — like anything that's not cultivated — it just languishes and becomes dull. But if you give attention to attention, then it flourishes, it blossoms, it becomes very luminous."

Etymology of Hazrat

"Why do we refer to great beings, awakened mystics, as Hazrat? We refer to Murshid as Hazrat Inayat Khan. Hazrat comes from that root Huzur — we're saying 'your presence.' We see in Murshid a profound sonification of the presence that exists in ourselves and is seeking cultivation."

Jesus in Gethsemane

"In the Garden of Gethsemane, Jesus said to the apostles: 'Stay awake with me.' But one by one they fell asleep. It's that wakefulness, it's that attentiveness, it's that ability to really hear, really see — it doesn't matter which organ of sensation is used — but whatever it is, to wake up to it."

• • •

Hejirat Day - Sacred Remembrance September 13

C3 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

September 13 is a doubly sacred day in the Inayatiyya lineage, observed on the day of this very session.

The Migration of Hazrat Inayat Khan

Hejirat Day commemorates the migration of Hazrat Inayat Khan from Baroda, India, accompanied by Sheikh Maheboob Khan and Murshid Ali Khan. This journey set in motion the transmission of all his prayers, teachings, practices, and the living light he manifested in the world. September 13, 2025 marks 115 years since this pivotal departure.

The Martyrdom of Noor-un-Nisa Inayat Khan

The same date, 84 years prior, marks the execution of Pirzadi Noor-un-Nisa Inayat Khan — Hazrat's firstborn child and direct spiritual heir — in Dachau concentration camp. Her final word was "Liberté" (freedom).

Her Legacy
  • She dedicated her life to the freedom of the soul and the right of all beings to realize it.
  • Facing the Nazi conquest of Europe, she chose to take a stand rather than flee.
  • She is remembered as an inspiration against oppression, cruelty, and supremacism of every kind.

"She lived life dedicated to the freedom of the soul and the imperative that all human beings be unimpeded in their own realization of freedom."

"So it's with great humility and at the same time high aspiration that we invoke the spirit of Pirzadi Noor-un-Nisa on this day — and her soul's fragrance, tinctured the entire atmosphere of the planet. God bless her being."

The Call to Students

Her life calls each student of the path to take seriously the opportunity of these few years given to us — to live in the fullest possible alignment with our highest vision of truth.

• • •

The Rabita - Heart to Heart Connection

C3 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Rabita is the heart-to-heart link established and sanctified through initiation (Ashik or Murid). It connects fellow travelers on the path regardless of physical or screen presence — an invisible cord between hearts that persists always.

Key Understanding

  • The Rabita is not dependent on being on screen together — it is always present.
  • Regular meetings (every couple of months, two to three days at a time) carry great power depending on the attention, sincerity, and care brought to them.
  • What is possible depends entirely on what attention and care we give to it.

"What is possible depends on what we give to it, what attention we give to it, what care we give to it. Everything is possible with that attention."

The Internet as Spiritual Territory

The internet is a mirror of the human condition — full of troubled impressions and unawakened impulses. Rather than fleeing it, the path calls us to meet it wisely and transformatively, navigating it with awareness.

• • •

The Spirit of Guidance and Cosmic Being

C3 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Teaching

The Invocation first invokes the One Being — the absolute — and then evokes the light of guidance that is the essence of creation. There is a soul of souls, a mind of minds, a body of bodies: not the infinite absolute itself, but the wholeness composed of all souls, all minds, all bodies — the cosmic being that is the first of creation and the mirror of the absolute.

What is the Spirit of Guidance?

The criterion for right from wrong is the wholeness of the cosmic being — in whom all poles are balanced and every individual has a place within the totality. The Spirit of Guidance is personified in those human beings who awaken to life's purpose, work together, serve, and advance the ongoing revelation of the divine in creation.

Key Quotes

"There's a soul of souls, a mind of minds, a body of bodies — still created, still ephemeral, not the infinite one that is all and everything, but rather the essence of creation."

"The Spirit of Guidance is the first of creation, the cosmic being — the mirror of the Absolute."

The Rabita — Heart-to-Heart Link

The Rabita is the heart-to-heart link established and sanctified through initiation (Ashik or Murid). It connects fellow travelers on the path regardless of physical or screen presence — an invisible cord between hearts that persists always.

  • The Rabita is not dependent on being on screen together — it is always present
  • Regular meetings (every couple of months, two to three days at a time) carry great power depending on the attention, sincerity, and care brought to them
  • What is possible depends entirely on what attention and care we give to it

"What is possible depends on what we give to it, what attention we give to it, what care we give to it. Everything is possible with that attention."

• • •

Jalali and Jamali - Two Aspects of Concentration

C4 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Concentration has two essential and complementary qualities that must be held in balance.

Definitions

Jalali — active, assertive, forceful. The quality of rock. Projecting, depicting, manifesting an image in the mind.

Jamali — receptive, gentle, embracing. The quality of a flower. Resting with, holding, listening to an image.

Analogy: Conversation

A conversation requires both speaking and listening. A friend who only talks (all Jalali) makes conversation impossible. A friend who only listens and never responds (all Jamali) is equally frustrating. True exchange requires both.

In Concentration Practice

Jalali — you actively portray, project, and hold the image in the mind. Without this, the image never forms.

Jamali — you rest with the image, embrace it, sustain it. Without this, the image fades quickly and the mind tires.

The rhythm — etch it, then hold it. Trace it, then sustain it. Right hand and left hand together.

Working with the Balance

  • When dullness arises — bring in more Jalali to retrace and re-enliven the image
  • When the image is present — yield to Jamali and simply be with it

"You can't just keep pushing it. You have to etch it and then hold it, trace it and then sustain it. It's these two things, right hand and left hand together — active and passive."

"Rock. That's Jalali. Flower. The words themselves tell you about the Jalali or Jamali character of what's being described."

• • •

The Faculty of Memory in Spiritual Practice

C4 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Yesterday's practice was presence as sensation — the first faculty of the mind: being awake in the here-and-now. C4 introduces the complementary faculty: memory.

What Memory Does

  • Locates us in time and space — the experience of waking in a dark room and slowly remembering where you are; memory returns and situates the temporal self within chronology
  • Allows revisiting the past — nothing is truly lost; the past lives in the mind
  • Enables wisdom — impressions can be engaged with, their wisdom extracted, and then released
  • Selective preservation — we can choose to let go of impressions that only bring regret, while preserving and returning to moments that nourish the heart

The Practice — Revisiting a Beautiful Moment

  1. Close the eyes
  2. Recall a beautiful moment in your life — go right there, be there now
  3. Remember exactly where you were. What time of day? What fragrance was in the air? Who else was there?
  4. What was the quality of the light? What colors were predominant?
  5. Relive that moment fully — it is not lost; it lives in you

"It isn't lost. It isn't going to slip away. It's just a place that will always be there. It lives in you. The past is available."

• • •

Living a Balanced and Pure Life - Murshid's Prescription

C5 · September 14, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Pir Zia shared Murshid's prescription for a wholesome way of life — the foundation for walking this path over time. The body is the Temple of Light (Hayakal al-Nur), a profound trust entrusted to our care.

Murshid's Prescription for Health

"The best medicine is a pure diet, nourishing food, fresh air, regularity in action and repose, clearness of thought, pureness of feeling, and confidence in the perfect being with whom we are all linked and whose expression we are."

Pure Diet

The body is a miniaturization of the whole cosmos — showing it respect is showing respect to creation itself. The questions to ask:

  • What truly nourishes you?
  • What leaves you energized, grounded, sustained?
  • Where did your food come from?

We take in not only physical molecules but the condition and etheric trace of what we consume. There is no single rule for all — it is a question of knowing your own body and constitution.

Fresh Air

Step outside, breathe a fresh breeze, go for a walk — especially first thing in the morning. Just this one act changes everything. The word inspiration derives from respiration.

Regularity in Action and Repose

Balance is essential for the long path. Deep repose is not mere inactivity — it is the relinquishing of all cares and fears, entering deep silence. One who learns deep repose finds even greater energy and effectiveness in activity.

Clearness of Thought and Pureness of Feeling

The essence of both is sincerity — sincere intention. It requires only a decision: to think clearly, to feel purely. Moving from the noise to the message. Not staying on the surface.

Confidence in the Perfect Being

We have been plucked out of the void, endowed with soul, mind, body. The world has been brought forth out of great mystery. Trust in the process; trust in the great benevolence behind all of this.

"With trust in God, with goodwill, self-confidence, and a hopeful attitude towards life, one will always win one's battle, however difficult."

"The only way to live in the midst of inharmonious influences is to strengthen the willpower and endure all things — yet keeping fineness of character and nobility of manner together with an ever-living heart full of love."

"No one can take from you the character of your heart."

• • •

Understanding Prayer - Al-Ghayb and the Invisible

C5 · September 14, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Pir Zia addressed potential resistance to prayer, particularly the word "God," and gave a profound teaching on what prayer actually is.

Al-Ghayb — The Invisible

Modern materialist rationalism challenges what is called Al-Ghayb — the invisible. The assumption is that if something is not quantifiable, it should be disregarded. But divinity is encountered in the wholeness of our being, of which the critical rational function is just one fraction. The sincerity of questioning and seeking is itself spiritual.

"One's belief in God is challenged by people enacting atrocities in the name of God. That sincerity is itself a spiritual intuition."

"Divinity is encountered in the wholeness of our being, of which the critical rational function is just one fraction."

"The word God may give some speakers pause — but what if you allow it to be a placeholder for mystery? You don't rush to define it, but let it be an ever-dawning discovery, never fully known."

Hazrat Inayat Khan's Story — The Key Turning in the Lock

As a boy, Hazrat Inayat Khan performed the daily prayers of Islam punctiliously, until he began to question: Is this just a performance? What is the real intention? He brought his deep question to his grandfather Maulabaksh, who pointed to a verse of the Quran:

"We will show them Our signs on the horizons and in themselves, and they will know that We are God."

At that moment, the key turned in the lock. He saw that prayer was not merely ritual — it was a path, a search, a quest for the signs found on the horizon in everything encountered, and in oneself in the depths of one's own being.

  • What is without shows itself within
  • What is within shows itself without
  • In the confrontation of the internal and external, divine attributes reveal themselves through their reflection
  • Prayer is a vessel for that journey of discovery

"He saw that it wasn't merely a ritual — it was a path. It was a search. It was a quest for the signs which are to be found on the horizon in everything that we encounter and in ourselves, in the depths of our own being."

"What is without shows itself within. What is within shows itself without. Prayer is a vessel for that journey of discovery."

• • •

Deep Teaching on Salat: Darood, Majma-ul-Bahrain, Syzygies

C6 · September 14, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

What Salat Is

Salat (benediction) is not the five-times daily Islamic prayer — it has a wider meaning. In the Quran: "Indeed God and the Angels extend their benediction to the Nabi — O you who believe, likewise present your benediction." This prayer is a Darood: paying respect to the light that is the inner being of all prophets, which flows into saints and sages.

"The Spirit of Guidance is that prism through which the divine light is refracting and reflecting into creation."

Forms of the Spirit of Guidance

The Spirit of Guidance can take any manner of forms: loving mother, kind father, innocent child, helpful friend, inspiring teacher. The great prophets and teachers of history are focal points of vast movements of people — messengers, bringers of healing and remembrance. There are at least 180,000 such beings; many names have been forgotten.

Majma-ul-Bahrain — The Mingling of Two Oceans

A phenomenon in both inner and outer worlds that the Quran calls Majma-ul-Bahrain — the mingling of two oceans. In India, reflected in the confluence of the Ganga and Yamuna rivers — where one dispensation meets another. The names in Salat include Biblical, Quranic, and Eastern figures — suggesting an intersection of lineages pointing to a vaster pattern.

"There is a very meaningful phenomenon in both inner and outer worlds which the Quran refers to as the Majma-ul-Bahrain, the mingling of two oceans."

Nuzul and Manzil — Revelation and Its Accommodation

Revelation (Nuzul) pours into the world. There is a Manzil — an accommodation, a readiness — where it can alight. It lands everywhere, but certain constellations of individuals are prepared to be central channels. Revelation never happens in isolation; even those at the center collaborate with others holding the light.

"Revelation is coming upon the whole of humanity — even the ones who find themselves at the center of the whole pattern are in close rapport with others who are also holding that light."

Ahl al-Bayt — The Houses and Syzygies

Each name in Salat emblemizes a whole house (Bayt) — an Ahl al-Bayt constellation. When we say Rama, Sita, Lakshman, and Hanuman are all present — a syzygy, a shared house, an ecology of revelation. These houses include men, women, elders, children — all manner of relationships. Houses exist within houses within houses.

Each name points to an oikos — an ecology, the peoples of the houses, the symmetries and geometries between houses.

The Inayatiyya has elaborated Salat with additional names of Ahl al-Bayt constellations.

All of these beings belong to history but also have presence within us — discovering them awakens parts of our own spiritual heritage.

"Each name is just pointing out to an oikos, an ecology, the peoples of the houses, the houses within houses, the symmetries and geometries between the houses — opens out into all of this."

• • •

From Concentration to Contemplation - Armored to Porous

C7 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

This session continues Concentration 1, the first stage of a four-stage path unfolding over the program:

Concentration → Contemplation → Meditation → Realization

Timeline: 'over the course of the next two years' — Suluk Academy 2025–2027.

"We're just at the beginning." — This is the very earliest stage.

The Task of Concentration

The foundational task of concentration is deceptively simple: slow down, be fully present, and take conscious responsibility for attention.

"The task is simply to slow down, be present, be awake, mind one's senses, take responsibility for one's attention, sculpt it, direct it, and in this way, choose what you will create with your mind."

"Mental creation comes into full flower in contemplation. In concentration, we're just beginning — learning to dwell on an experience, to linger over a sight or a sound."

Relearning Concentration

"We live in a world that has sped up so fast that, strangely, concentration hardly comes naturally to us anymore. We have to relearn it — with patience, with dedication, and most of all with the willingness to bring your heart to the moment — a readiness to be in a state of intimacy with what is right here, right now."

Everything we do in our practices together, conversations, prayers — everything is an opportunity to bring the heart to the center of our life.

From Armored to Porous

"After we've been so armored, so bounded, so closed, we're learning to reopen, to be porous. It doesn't mean we're going to soak up every impression and let every idea reverberate in our minds."

Porousness does not mean passive absorption of everything. The same ease that draws the in-breath meets the world; the out-breath releases:

"The same ease with which we learn to draw in a breath and meet the world as it is, characterizes the out-breath, where we let it all go — or at the very least, let go of all that we don't need or wish to carry."

Quality Over Quantity

"We don't actually need lots of practices. Sometimes we do many, but it isn't the number that matters. It's a way of being — a certain gentleness, fineness, loving-kindness, and porousness."

• • •

Sobriety and the Body as Spiritual Instrument

C7 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Murshid's Teaching from the Gathas

"Sobriety is most necessary in the path of spiritual evolution. Especially in the first stage, when the body must be made pure for spiritual revelation. Everything intoxicating deadens the nerves more or less, and the centers — which are the factors for spiritual realization — become dead."

"The centers which show sensitiveness during intoxication become weary and lifeless afterward. Fakirs or yogis who take intoxicants to excite the centers become dependent on material objects for spiritual experience — and in the end, their seeming advancement becomes fatal."

On Smoking and the Spiritual Centers

"Even hard smoking may block not only the channels of breath, but even the spiritual centers — and thereby intuition is confused. Smoking gives momentary comfort — it brings a kind of repose to the smoker. But it is only a passing comfort. Smoking not only has an effect upon the throat or lungs — the two most important centers, the heart and the brain, upon which all spiritual progress depends, will become blocked."

The Path to Self-Sufficiency

"The principal thing in spiritual attainment is to be self-sufficient. The first step to self-sufficiency is to make one's body independent of all such things upon which its comfort and enjoyment depend."

Pir Zia's Commentary on the Lataif

Pir Zia extends Murshid's teaching with a subtle-body (etheric) explanation:

  • Intoxicants act on the Lataif (subtle centers), exciting and stirring them
  • The sensation obtained is the result of this artificial excitement
  • The centers are left depleted afterward — an artificial high, a corresponding low
  • This is well known to anyone who drinks a lot and then feels exhausted and depressed in the morning
  • Each Latifa has the capacity to awaken itself naturally — that capacity diminishes with external dependency

The Natural Path to Altered States

"Drugs can open the doors of perception and reveal dimensions unacknowledged in the collective paradigm of our time — hence their attraction. But many of those who discovered the invisible this way realized before long that there is a path into the invisible that doesn't require the use or abuse of substances — and which instead involves the cultivation of our own natural capacities."

"We can appreciate the possibility of taking our consciousness as our own responsibility — and learning to craft it, to sculpt it, to elevate it, and to lift it down into states of repose — all by means of the clarity of our own intention through the medium of the awakened breath."

• • •

Vanity - The Magic Plant That Cannot Be Rooted Out

C7 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Murshid's Teaching on Vanity and the Ego

"The whole manifestation is the expression of that spirit of Logos, which in Sufi terms is called Kibria. Through every being, this spirit is manifested in the form of vanity, pride, or conceit. Vanity, expressed crudely, is called pride. Had it not been for this spirit working in every being as the central theme of life, no good or bad would have existed in the world, nor would there have been great or small. All virtues and every evil are offspring of this spirit."

"The art of personality is to cut off the rough edges of the spirit of vanity, which hurts and disturbs those one meets in life. The person who says 'I' — the more he does so, the more he disturbs the mind of his listeners. Yet if this spirit of vanity is pronounced, it will creep up in spite of all good manners and beautiful language — calling aloud: 'I am, I am.' If a person be speechless, his or her vanity will leap out in the expression of his or her glance."

Vanity vs. Passions - The Harder Battle

"For adepts, the struggle in life is not so great with the passions and emotions, which sooner or later, by more or less effort, can be controlled. But vanity — it is always growing. If one cuts down its stem, then one cannot live, for it is the very self. It is the I. The ego, the soul, or God within — it cannot be denied its existence. But struggling with it beautifies it more and more, and makes more and more tolerable that which in its crude form is intolerable."

The Magic Plant - Vanity Transformed

"Vanity may be likened to a magic plant. If one sees it growing as a thorny plant and cuts it down, it will grow in another place as a fruit tree. And when one cuts it down again, it will spring up as a bush of fragrant roses. It exists just the same, but in a more beautiful form — which gives happiness to those who touch it."

"The art of personality does not teach the rooting out of the seed of vanity, which cannot be rooted out as long as one lives — but its crude outer garb may be destroyed, in order that, after dying several deaths, it may manifest as the plant of desires."

Working with the Ego

The ego is inherent in human constitution and in the cosmos itself — it is an expression of the Divine, not an accident. It cannot and ought not be rooted out. Yet it tends to develop in unconsciousness, seeing itself as the sole center of the universe.

"The universe is a circle whose center is everywhere and whose circumference is nowhere."

How do we work with the ego? By watching its workings, seeing it in action, then slowing it down:

  • If it wasn't charming when someone else was boasting — is our own boasting any different?
  • What is the real need? If I've imagined a need for a certain kind of attention — that's a distraction.
  • What truly fulfills, nourishes, and advances me in the journey of being?
• • •

Living Concentration as a Way of Life

C8 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Single-Mindedness is the Secret

Murshid teaches us that true concentration becomes a way of being:

"When a person develops concentration, she does not need a regular concentration, although a Sufi likes to do it, for her life becomes a concentration."
"If she is speaking on a certain subject, she does not suddenly change the subject of the conversation. If she is thinking about something, she does not change her mind and leave it half done in order to accomplish something else. She continues at every moment the work she is doing at that time until it is finished. That is the secret of concentration."

Pir Zia's Commentary on Everyday Practice

"Eventually concentration doesn't need to be a practice that one does in the way of visualizing red or visualizing an emerald. Every moment becomes an opportunity to practice attention."

Signs of a Scattered Mind
  • Thinking two thoughts at once and not doing justice to either
  • Walking into a room and forgetting why you went there
  • Starting sentences that end with "dot, dot, dot" instead of completion
The Practice of Completion

"Completing what one starts is itself a great practice. If one has taken something up — just to finish it — is important. It brings completeness and gives you more energy for what is to come next."

Being Serious - Not Solemn

"Not serious in the way of being solemn and grim, but serious in the sense of giving it one's heart, meeting it with care, and being ready to put into it all that it's going to require."

Self-inquiry questions before undertaking anything:

  • "Am I ready to give my heart to it?"
  • "What is that going to mean?"
  • "Am I going to really follow through?"
Escorting Thoughts Deeper

"Maybe think fewer thoughts, but honor your thoughts. Escort your thoughts to the deeper spaces within your own psyche. That's concentration — and it leads to contemplation and on to meditation."

"We're not going to be led to the center of everything if we just skim the surface. What leads us down, down to the center is this care, this steadiness, this giving of the heart to what we're confronting."

• • •

Sacrament of Attention and Theophanies

C8 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Letting Go - The Quality of Release

"Don't hold on to anything you don't need to. As soon as you let it go, it's just inconsequential — as if it never existed. And what a relief to exhale it and let it go."

"You breathe out and that cloudy, viscous, murky dust starts dissipating. You know it's going. And you know that you've been accumulating this residue for a long time. Finally, now, you're letting it go."

The Sacrament of Holding

"This precious energy that is in your awareness — this focus, this heartfulness — to give it purposefully, meaningfully, bestow it as you will. And in that bestowal, feel the sacrament of holding a process, an experience, an object of attention for the full term of wished-for witnessing, discovery, revelation — and then let it go and meet what is next."

Theophanies - Divine Disclosures

"And the theophanies, the disclosures from the source of being are never repeated, never identical. Stay with the color till you reach the end of it. And go on and meet the color that is coming."

The Uniqueness of Each Moment

Each color, each practice, each moment of genuine attention is a unique disclosure from the Source — never to be repeated. This is why presence matters: each theophany is once only.

The Sacred Arc of Attention

  1. Purposeful Bestowal - Give attention meaningfully
  2. Full Term Witnessing - Stay present for the complete revelation
  3. Sacred Release - Let go when the disclosure is complete
  4. Meeting What Comes Next - Open to the new theophany

The Sacrament Defined

Attention itself becomes sacramental when we:

  • Recognize its preciousness
  • Give it purposefully
  • Hold the full arc of witnessing
  • Release completely to meet what follows

This transforms every moment of concentrated awareness into a sacred encounter with divine disclosure.

• • •

Vision as a Cross-Section of a Multi-Dimensional Landscape

C8 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Beyond Habitual Seeing

Pir Zia teaches that our ordinary way of seeing — picking out objects, differentiating things — is only one mode of vision. The eyes have developed to prioritize discerning "this thing and that thing," but there are other ways of looking.

"Instead of immediately outlining the boundary of a thing, we discern the ways in which qualities advance and recede and mingle on all of the horizons in a constant flux."

The Invisible Dimensions

"There's much that is not visible because it belongs to another wavelength. The eyes only see certain wavelengths. Or because it's occluded — for instance, the entire interior of our own bodies. When we partake of a meal, we don't witness the process of digestion."

"If we could see it, it might alter the impression we have of being a thing, bounded, separate. We could see the breath moving through the bloodstream, through the cells, the water that we drink churning in our bloodstream. We would see more."

The Full Reality

"Our vision is just a little cross-section of a multi-dimensional landscape that consists not so much as an array of objects as it does a constant process of transformations involving all manner of organic and inorganic configurations of energy."

The Invitation

"Let your eyes become rapturous explorers of the divine manifestation in the visible and invisible worlds, rather than merely habituated reinforcers of preconceived expectations."

"Let your eyes surprise you, delight you. Let your eyes be practitioners of concentration, able to rest for moments at a time on something that in the eyes of the world is of no practical value."

• • •

Will as Divine Power and Sacred Trust

C8 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Will = All the Power That Is

"Will is not a power. It is all the power that is." — Murshid
"The creation of the world is an act of will by God. Therefore, that in us which we call willpower is in reality God-power. When this power is recognized and affirmed, it increases in potential and strength." — Murshid

Physical Manifestation of Will

"Our hands, with their perfect mechanism, would not be able to hold even a glass of water if there was no willpower to support them. A person may seem to be healthy, but if willpower fails him, he will not be able to stand. It is not the body which makes a person stand upright. It is our willpower." — Murshid
"Success and failure are the phenomena of willpower." — Murshid

Will = Love = God

"What is willpower made of? In metaphysical terms, willpower is love. If one says God is love, it really means God is will. God loves creation — only after God came to will its creation." — Murshid
"Will and consciousness are fundamentally the same. It is the dual expression of the same thing. In action, it is will. In stillness, it is consciousness. It is just as sound and light are fundamentally one thing — in one condition producing light through the friction of vibrations, in another producing sounds that are audible." — Murshid

Will as Sacred Trust

"This will that is in us, this will that is ours, is far more precious than anything we may believe we own."

"When we are unaware of it, it fragments, weakens, and we become easily caught up in the will of others — because we don't know our own will."

"When we know that will is our sacred trust, then we perceive the responsibility that comes with it. It's the ultimate power of creation."

Aligning with the Divine Will

"As this will in us is divine in origin, divine in essence — the highest purpose, the fullest, deepest purpose to which we can devote it — is in responding to the divine will, aligning with the divine will, seeking to embody the divine will. Not by way of presumption, not by way of making any kind of claim — but by the giving over of that which is most free in us, the offering of it up to the all-pervading."

Concentration as Gathering the Will

"When we practice concentration, we're accepting responsibility for our own consciousness — endeavoring to make this energy that is within us, this power, this luminous substance — to make it whole, to collect it, to concentrate it."

"How can we offer our will to the divine when it's scattered? We don't even know the location of its parts. Concentration is drawing it together, affirming it, exercising it."

"The exercises that we're doing are not ends in themselves. They're simply opportunities to put into practice the concentrating and enlivening and reawakening of this freedom that's in us."

• • •

Commentary on Burden - Lightness and Letting Go

C9 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

"So don't be discouraged if you've stumbled, even if you've failed at your endeavors a thousand times. Never mind — keep going. Hope guides."

The Weight of Carried Impressions

"Don't carry with you the impressions of the past which weigh you down. The jarring pictures, the voices of despair — none of us can afford to carry such a load."

"Lightness, lightness of mind, quickens our steps on the journey. Clears our sight."

Direct Personal Address

"Is there something that's weighing on you? Something that has burdened you now for too long? You needn't carry it. No one is requiring this of you. It's your choice to carry it or not carry it."

Unconscious Carrying

"Too often these choices are made unconsciously. One doesn't mean to carry it, but one carries it nonetheless. The time has come to be intentional and choose to lay it down."

• • •

Progress vs Standstill - The Clock Analogy

C9 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Clock Analogy

"As dust gets into the works of a clock and stops the clock, so the effect produced by all impressions that are void of beauty and harmony, and which disturb your peace, keeps you from progress."

"The mind cannot act properly when it is hindered by impressions which have a paralyzing effect upon it."

Life is Progress

"Life is progress. And stopping from progress is death."

"Failure does not matter in life. To a progressive person, even a thousand failures do not matter. He has before his view success — and success is his, even after a thousand failures."

"The greatest pity in life is that standstill when life does not move farther. A sensible person prefers death to such a life as that. It is a paralysis of the soul, of the spirit, which is always caused by holding bad impressions in the mind."

The Soul's Natural Happiness

"No soul is deprived of happiness in reality. The soul's very being is happiness. Man brings unhappiness upon himself by holding in one's hands the clouds of bad impressions, which fall as a shadow upon one's soul."

"Once a person is able to clear from their mind, by whatever process, the undesirable impressions — a new power begins to spring from his heart, opening a way before him, attracting to him all that he requires, clearing from his path all obstacles, and making his atmosphere clear for him to live and move, and to accomplish all one wishes to accomplish."

• • •

Purity of Mind - Five Methods of Destroying Impressions

C9 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Murshid's Core Teaching

"Purity of mind requires the destroying of all bad impressions collected there or received at present. One can destroy these impressions by five methods — and the method is chosen according to the impression one has to destroy."

The Five Methods

  1. Wash off from the mind
  2. Erase from the surface of the mind
  3. Shake off like dust from the clothes
  4. Burn like wood in fire — after its test by fire, it turns into ashes
  5. Drown so that they will never come up again

Additional Method:

"Bury certain impressions like a corpse. Find every way of annihilation that is suited to each impression, so that your mind may be clear."

The Mind as King

"The mind is not only a means of thinking or reasoning, but the king of one's being. Upon the condition of the mind, one's health, happiness, and peace in life depend."

What to Collect / What to Destroy

"Collect and keep all that is beautiful — destroy all that is void of beauty."

"Collect and keep all that is agreeable — destroy all that has a disagreeable effect upon you."

"Collect and keep all that is harmonious — destroy all that creates disharmony in yourself."

"Collect and keep all that is restful — destroy all that disturbs the peace of your life."

• • •

The Meaning of Suluk - Traveling the Path

C9 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

"Suluk means travel. Saliks are travelers. We're on a journey."

"We've come to realize there's a destination. And there's a way."

"Since, in any case, all is change. Nothing stays the same."

Reactive vs. Wakeful Response

"Anything is possible. At the same time, we know that whatever arises may be met reactively, unconsciously, distractedly — or it may be met wakefully, conscientiously, compassionately, wisely."

"Our intention is to meet the changing terrain of life with wisdom."

"Our intention is to navigate this world and the worlds beyond in the most beautiful way possible."

The Mountaineer's Path

"How does a mountaineer passing through the rugged peaks and deep chasms travel well?"

"It's wise to follow a route that has been already explored."

"The ones who have gone ahead have blazed the trail and even removed obstacles from the path in advance. And as we travel behind them, we benefit from their foresight."

"Debris may have meanwhile interposed itself" — our responsibility to clear fresh debris.

"Our task is to follow the path that has been revealed and do our part in keeping the path clear for those who come after."

• • •

What to Carry - Lightness as Imperative

C9 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

"If one is traveling a very short distance, then one might succeed in dragging along many heavy things. But if one is going a great distance, then a light load is imperative."

The Weight Test

"Does its usefulness justify its weight?"

Three Ways to Release What We Carry

  1. Pass Along: Things others could beneficially use → pass them along
  2. Return to Nature: Things to give back to nature itself
  3. Conscious Dissolution: Things to consciously pulverize and return to dust

"We stop at way stations along the way. And at each way station, there's an opportunity to re-examine what we're carrying."

"Certain things are best returned to the cosmos by very consciously pulverizing them, reducing them to dust."

The Guiding Question

"Is there something that I'm carrying that the time has come to relinquish?"

• • •

Five Aspects of Mind — Complete Teaching

C10 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Pir Zia enumerated all five aspects of mind in sequence, forming the interior architecture the program has been developing. Each aspect is both a faculty of mind and a station on the path of inward concentration.

The Five Aspects

  1. Sensation — the most immediate faculty of mind
  2. Memory — the faculty that holds and retrieves
  3. Imagination — the creative/generative faculty
  4. Will — the faculty of intention and direction
  5. Self — the deepest aspect, introduced as the culminating fifth

The Hierarchical Chain

The five aspects of mind form a hierarchical chain: each faculty arising from and resting in the deeper faculty below it, until the deepest — Self — dissolves into soul.

"Will emerges from it, and imagination, and memory, and sensation. But these other faculties again and again find their repose in the I."

"Which is the essence of mind. It's where the mind merges into the soul."

• • •

Listening to Murshid's Melody — Orchestrated by Count Sergei Tolstoy

C10 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Fifth Sense: Hearing

As part of the concentration practices engaging all five senses, Pir Zia introduces a listening practice using a melody communicated by Hazrat Inayat Khan and orchestrated by Count Sergei Tolstoy.

The Practice

"And listen well, give a whole heart to it. For listening — if you wish to have your eyes open, you are welcome to do so, but also very welcome to keep your eyes closed."

"Just be relaxed, settle into a position in which you can stay for the next 5 or 10 minutes. And realize there's nowhere else you have to be. Nothing else you have to do and so you can entirely give yourself to this piece of music."

"We're going to listen to a melody communicated by Murshid and orchestrated by Count Sergei Tolstoy. Let's begin."

Reflection After Listening: Who is the Self Listening?

After the music, Pir Zia poses the question of identity:

"Who has listened? Who is the self listening? Is it the persona — this character on the stage of life consisting of self-image, a self-image that is composed of a variety of attitudes, judgements, assumptions, and which is a constant negotiation between how we would like to be seen and how others see us?"

"Or is it something that looms behind this character? Something that was awake before we were born. Before we were conceived. And which will be awake after we die."

Historical Note

Count Sergei Tolstoy was a Russian musician and the son of the famous writer Leo Tolstoy. He orchestrated melodies that Hazrat Inayat Khan had communicated, preserving the musical dimension of the Sufi teachings.

The Fifth Aspect of Mind — Self (Persona vs. Witness)

C10 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

This is the culminating teaching of the entire five-day retreat. After the listening practice, Pir Zia opened direct inquiry into identity and selfhood.

The Central Question

"Who has listened? Who is the self-listening?"

The Persona — The Subjective Self

Pir Zia described the persona as the constructed, social, ever-negotiating self:

"This character on the stage of life, consisting of self-image — a self-image that is composed of a variety of attitudes, judgements, assumptions — and which is a constant negotiation between how we would like to be seen and how others see us."

"This persona that's patched together, forged of various influences, and which is always a work in progress."

The Witness — The Objective Self

"Something that looms behind this character. Something that was awake before we were born, before we were conceived, and which will be awake after we die. That doesn't change when the opinions of the character change or when the social profile of the character alters."

"The I that is the EYE. The I that is the space of experience. Not so much the character on the stage as the theater itself — the witness."

"It's this sheer, luminous presence that hosts all manner of perceptions and emotions — but isn't them."

Both Are Ourselves

"Which one is oneself? The persona or the pre-existing I-ness? Both are ourselves. One the subjective self, the other the objective self. And each has its part to play in the story of the soul."

"But which goes deeper? Which lasts longer? Which is steady when the other is careening? We know the answer."

STORIES & PARABLES

Teaching Through the Heart's Ear

Stories are the Sufi's oldest teaching tool. The stories shared by Pir Zia — from the boy who only wrote Alif to Rumi's shepherd and Moses — plant seeds directly in the heart.

5 Entries · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

✿

The Story of Mount Qaf - Earth's Spiritual Anchor

C1 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Story

When God created the Earth, she orbited the sun in ecstasy and began to envision the unfolding of life — oceans, continents, animals, humanity. But as she foresaw the course of human history — the tragedies, the violence, the suffering — she began to shake and wobble in her orbit.

To anchor and stabilize her, God raised up Mount Qaf — a monumental spiritual mountain. Though not visible to physical eyes, its roots work through all the mountain ranges of the earth, sinking deep into the earth's mantle and core.

The Function of Mount Qaf

Mount Qaf functions as a great spiritual circulatory system, creating connection between the planes of existence:

  • Mounting from Nasut to Malakut
  • From Malakut to Jabrut
  • From Jabrut to Lahut
  • And onward to HaHut

Anchoring the physical earth in the spiritual depths from which it emerges.

The Emerald Peak and the Divan

At the crown of the mountain is an emerald peak. Emerald — in the alchemy of Sufism — is the color that outlasts all others, sums them all up, and bespeaks the perfect integration of all opposites.

There the Divan, the League of Bodhisattvas who guard and guide the world, have their seat.

This Class Name

This class is named Mount Qaf — Qaf — the cosmic anchor between Earth and the divine realms.

• • •

The Story of the Boy and the Alif

C1 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Story

In a village classroom, a teacher began teaching the Arabic alphabet. One child showed exceptional devotion to the very first letter — Alif, the upright line — and refused to move on to the others.

Dismissed and misunderstood by his teacher and peers, he left home and disappeared into the jungle for years.

When he finally returned and wrote Alif on the blackboard, the entire room shook with light. He had truly mastered the one. He then went on to master all the other letters and became one of the greatest Sufi poets of the land.

The Teaching

"A Salik could do one practice for their whole life and reach the divine presence. What is powerful is to bring one's whole being to whatever it is."

This story teaches quality over quantity — depth over accumulation. The essence of Suluk is not in multitudinous practices but in the wholehearted spirit with which one gives oneself to the work.

The Lesson for Seekers

True mastery comes not from rushing through many practices, but from bringing complete dedication and presence to whatever practice is given. The depth of engagement matters far more than the breadth of techniques.

The boy's devotion to the single letter Alif — the symbol of Unity — ultimately opened all doors to him, demonstrating that the One contains the All.

• • •

The Young Lady and the Man in Prayer

C4 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

A teaching story about concentration and the power of love.

The Story

A young lady was on her way to meet her beloved. Fully absorbed in anticipation, she walked directly in front of a man who was praying — a breach of normal decorum. The man quickly finished his prayer and stopped her: "Didn't you see I was praying to God at that moment?"

She replied with sincere apology: "I am so sorry — I didn't see you. All my thought was with the one I love and whom I am going to see."

In that instant the man was struck: she did not see him because she was absorbed in her beloved — but how was it that he saw her, when his prayer was directed to the Beloved of all?

The Teaching

  • Sincere love makes concentration natural and effortless — the young lady's love was single-pointed and undistracted
  • Distraction in devotion reveals the heart is not yet fully absorbed in the Beloved
  • The path moves from single-object love (one beloved) toward perceiving the Beloved in every being, every direction, every trace of existence
  • Every stage has value — the distracted man and the absorbed young lady are both on the journey toward ever-vaster love

"It's a story about concentration and how love, sincere love, makes concentration possible."

• • •

The Story of Hazrat Ali - Breath and Right Action

C7 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Pir Zia uses this account to illustrate breath as the arbiter of right action under provocation.

"Hazrat Ali was fighting a fierce enemy and was about to deal the decisive blow when just at that moment, his enemy spat in his face. And then, instead of striking down his foe — as it was fully in his power to do — he sheathed his sword and walked away."

When asked why he withdrew from victory, Hazrat Ali answered that when he fought in the first place, it was for the noble cause — for the cause of defending the beleaguered. But when this opponent spat in his face, he aroused his anger. And as Hazrat Ali was determined never to act in anger, he sheathed his sword.

"One might say that Hazrat Ali observed a change in his own breath, and that change required him to withdraw — to bring his breath back into its fundamental rhythm before taking action of any kind."

The Teaching Applied Universally

  • Certain provocations will temporarily throw us out of rhythm — this cannot always be prevented
  • The question: are we aware of that departure from the natural rhythm of the breath?
  • If aware: do we have the clarity to pause, recalibrate, and only then proceed?

"Whatever is done with breath askew will be badly done. Whatever is done with breath aligned will be well done."

• • •

Birbal and Emperor Akbar - The Crescent and Full Moon

C8 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Story

Birbal was the witty minister at the court of the Mughal King Akbar. One day Akbar sent Birbal as ambassador to the court of the Emperor of Iran.

At the Iranian court, Birbal addressed the monarch:

"Oh your majesty — you are such a tremendous force in this world. You are, if I may say so, the full moon — as compared to our own Akbar Shah, who is more like a mere crescent."

The Shah was delighted and honored Birbal with great largesse, sending him back with many gifts.

Birbal returned to Fatehpur Sikri — Akbar's court — where his fellow ministers reported what he had said.

Akbar confronted Birbal: "Now, Birbal — I can hardly believe it. Did you really say such a thing?"

And Birbal said: "Of course I said that! I meant every word."

Birbal's Explanation

"I said he's like a full moon. What's going to happen to the full moon? It's going to wane — it's going to start fading. The crescent moon is that power that's rising and rising, becoming fuller and fuller. It's on the ascendancy."

Akbar was happy with that explanation — and Birbal was doubly rewarded.

The Sufi Teaching

The crescent is the symbol of spiritual ascent — rising, filling, on the ascendancy.

Birbal's wit demonstrates:

  • Presence in the moment
  • Intelligence that sees deeper meanings
  • The ability to transform a potential offense into deeper understanding
  • How the same words can carry multiple layers of truth

Spiritual Symbolism

  • Full Moon: Apparent completion that contains the seed of decline
  • Crescent Moon: The power of ascendancy, continuous growth toward fullness
  • Double Reward: The fruits of wisdom that serves multiple purposes simultaneously

The story illustrates how spiritual insight can navigate worldly diplomacy while revealing deeper truths about the nature of spiritual development.

Key Quotes from Pir Zia - Concentration Class 1

C1 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

On the Nature of Self and Journey

"The journey is a journey of recollection — recollecting yourselves, bringing the parts back together. Remembrance — bringing the different members back into unity. And not only within ourselves, because what is a self? A self itself is a fragment of a greater whole."

On Intention

"If the intention is clear, if it's sincere, if it's focused, we'll get through everything easily."

On Recognition of Truth

"The eyes must be sun-like to see the sun. Whatever elevates you, inspires you, motivates you, reassures you, consoles you — it does so because it meets in you the truth that is already there."

On Concentration

"Concentration means the whole of you is in one place. You are not scattered. You are not dispersed. You are not diffused. You are gathered. If one can learn to concentrate, then one can pray. If one can learn to concentrate, then one can meditate. If one can learn to concentrate, then one can create. If one can learn to concentrate, then one can love. The whole of life depends on concentration."

On Quality vs Quantity

"A Salik could do one practice for their whole life and reach the divine presence. What is powerful is to bring one's whole being to whatever it is."

On the Alif

"The upright line suggests heaven, perfection, straightforwardness, firmness, life, rising, and unity — as it shows oneness with the whole. The upright line is the first line, and all forms and figures are nothing but the change of direction of that line."

Key Teachings from September 13 Session

On Aman Prayer

"Find the place of your strength — and then offer your obeisance."

On Attention and Possibility

"What is possible depends on what we give to it, what attention we give to it, what care we give to it. Everything is possible with that attention."

Noor-un-Nisa on Speaking of Others

C3 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Noor-un-Nisa Inayat Khan's saying, recalled by her friend Jeanne Overton Fuller:

"I never speak ill of a flower for fear of offending the fairy that is doing its best to make the flower beautiful."

This saying was shared in the context of Iron Rule 2: "My conscientious self, speak not against others in their absence."

It beautifully illustrates the recognition of the divine presence working through all beings, and the reverence with which we should speak of others, seeing them as souls as well as bodies.

• • •

Breath as Cosmic Process

C4 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

"Breath is the churning of the life field itself. Oxygen and carbon dioxide are just one component of the larger process of expansion and contraction, assimilation and disgorgement — essential to all of the patterns of this world and of the inner worlds."

"Spring and fall, sleeping and waking, birth and death — all of the cycles of our lives are expressions of this contraction and expansion, which is constantly occurring through the breath."

— Pir Zia Inayat Khan

C6 · September 14, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

"We spoke of the body as a temple — and with the kinds of movements that re-up the circulation and the breath, that temple comes into still fuller cohesion and becomes a more spacious vessel for the spirit to function in."

"So it's really a blessing whenever we can experience this kind of fluidity and opening up of the channels."

"May this mountain be the grounding, the stability in which we find renewal in the midst of the shaking of the earth — culminating in its emerald peak where physical and spiritual worlds coincide, and where the divan gathers in service to the furtherance of creation."

Final Blessing

May your heart be filled with heavenly joy.

May your soul be illuminated with divine light.

May your spirit unfold the divine message.

May you go on in the spiritual path.

May God's peace abide with you forever and evermore. Amen.

Sayed Abu Hasim Madani on Breath as Virtue

C7 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

The Quote

"In this path there is one sin and one virtue — and virtue is the breath: breathe in with Divine awareness. The sin is the breath that escapes in negligence."

— Sayed Abu Hasim Madani

The Triple Alignment

From the wakeful, rhythmic, attuned breath comes a triple alignment:

  • Soul ↔ Mind ↔ Body
  • Soul ↔ Soul of Souls
  • Mind ↔ Mind of Minds
  • Body ↔ Body of all Bodies

"All felicity comes from this, from this alignment."

Recalibrating the Breath

"When we find ourselves in a scattered state, the most important thing is to recalibrate the breath."

The natural rhythm: balance between inhalation and exhalation — evenness, consistency — 'like a pendulum, like the tides on the shore of the sea.' If this rhythm was absent during a difficult episode, the outcome would have been very different.

Key Quotes from Concentration Session

C8 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

On Living Concentration

"When a person develops concentration, she does not need a regular concentration, although a Sufi likes to do it, for her life becomes a concentration." — Murshid
"Single-mindedness is the secret of concentration." — Murshid

"Will is not a power. It is all the power that is." — Murshid
"Will is essential. Will is divine." — Murshid

"Each speaks what he owns." — Jesus (as taught by Pir Zia)

DEEP STUDY & ARABIC TERMS

The Sufi path uses a rich vocabulary drawn from Arabic, Persian, and other sacred languages. Arabic terms, glossary entries, and deeper learnings from Pir Zia's sessions.

Arabic and Sufi Terms - Concentration Class 1

C1 · September 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Arabic/Sufi TermMeaningContext/Significance
**Suluk**Travel; fine mannerThe path of intentional inner travel + the art of traveling well (gently, wisely, balanced)
**Salik** (pl. Saliks)Traveler on the pathOne who undertakes the Suluk journey intentionally
**Sohbet**Heart-centered conversationA form of spiritual companionship and sharing among fellow travelers
**Murshid / Pir**Spiritual guide / ElderHazrat Pir-o-Murshid Inayat Khan — transmitter of the Inayatiyya teachings
**Murid**Student / seekerOne formally initiated into the Inayatiyya or other Tariqa
**Tariqa**Path / OrderA Sufi lineage or order (e.g., the Inayatiyya)
**Saum**ReposeDaily prayer addressed to the One divine being
**Salat / Salawat**BenedictionDaily prayer addressed to the Spirit of Guidance (light of the Rasool)
**Alif**First letter of Arabic alphabet; upright lineSymbol of unity, oneness, divine perfection — the root of all letters
**Khalwat dar Anjuman**Solitude in the crowdMeditating together in inner worlds even while physically apart
**Qaf / Mount Qaf**The spiritual mountainCosmic anchor connecting all planes; this class is named after it
**Amān**Sanctuary, safety, protection, refugeOpening prayer of each Suluk day — holding the world's suffering with compassion
**Ashik**Lover / devoted oneOne who has deep love for the path or the Murshid without formal initiation
**Gayathri**Sacred hymnsHymns transmitted through Pir-o-Murshid Inayat Khan, used continuously throughout Suluk
**Divan**The League of BodhisattvasSpiritual guardians and guides of the world; their seat is the emerald peak of Mount Qaf

The Five Planes of Existence

PlaneArabic TermDescription
1st**Nasut**Physical plane
2nd**Malakut**Angelic / subtle plane — realm of subtle forms
3rd**Jabrut**Plane of power / force — realm of divine attributes
4th**Lahut**Divine plane — realm of pure divinity
5th**HaHut**Plane of the Absolute — the Absolute beyond all names

Additional Teachings

Salat - Benediction, prayer. Not the five-times daily Islamic prayer but has a wider meaning. From the Quran: "Indeed God and the Angels extend their benediction to the Nabi."

Darood - Paying respect to the light that is the inner being of all prophets, which flows into saints and sages.

Majma-ul-Bahrain - The mingling of two oceans. A phenomenon in both inner and outer worlds where one dispensation meets another.

Manzil - An accommodation, a readiness where revelation can alight.

Ahl al-Bayt - The houses, constellations of spiritual beings. Each name in Salat emblemizes a whole house.

Bayt - House, referring to spiritual constellations or families.

Malakut - The realm where images exist without physical substance; the imaginal realm.

Jalali - The quality of divine majesty, power, fierce radiance.

Jamali - The quality of divine beauty, grace, delicacy.

Khatum - Closing prayer of gratitude in Suluk gatherings.

• • •

Nazar Par Kadam — Watchfulness of the Step

C4 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Two Sufi Principles in Practice

Pir Zia invokes two classical Sufi principles during the soles-breathing practice:

Nazar Par Kadam — "Be conscious of your breath with each step." Watchfulness of the step — the practice of bringing full awareness to each footstep, each breath, each movement. Whether walking or lying down, the attention rests on the soles of the feet as a passageway between inner and outer worlds.

Khilwat dar Anjuman — "Be in communion in meditation." Solitude in society — maintaining an inner meditative state even while engaged in the outer world.

The Teaching

"Be conscious of your breath Nazar Par Kadam. Feel the soles of your feet with each footstep or lying down with each breath Khilwat dar anjuman. Be in communion in meditation."

These two principles form the spiritual foundation of the soles-breathing practice: Nazar Par Kadam brings awareness to the physical point of contact (the soles), while Khilwat dar Anjuman holds the practitioner in a state of inner communion throughout.

Connection to Soles-Breathing Practice

The soles-breathing practice (lying down, breathing through the soles of the feet) is a direct embodiment of these principles — the practitioner watches the breath enter and leave through the feet (Nazar Par Kadam) while remaining in a state of wakeful meditation (Khilwat dar Anjuman).

• • •

Sensus Communis

C4 · September 13, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Sensus Communis - The unified faculty of perception that can be concentrated and directed through different sensory channels. In practice, it can concentrate itself in the glance (projected out through both eyes as two beams), or be drawn inward to fill all five senses, or be focused in specific areas like the mouth and tongue.

The Sensus Communis represents the common root of all sensory experience, the unified awareness that underlies and coordinates the individual senses.

• • •

Spiritual Terms from Salat Teaching

C6 · September 14, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Salat - Benediction, not the five-times daily Islamic prayer but a wider meaning of presenting benediction to the Spirit of Guidance

Darood - Paying respect to the light that is the inner being of all prophets, which flows into saints and sages

Majma-ul-Bahrain - "The mingling of two oceans" - a phenomenon in both inner and outer worlds where one dispensation meets another

Nuzul - Revelation that pours into the world

Manzil - An accommodation, a readiness where revelation can alight

Ahl al-Bayt - "People of the House" - constellations or ecologies of beings around each prophet/guide

Bayt - House, referring to the spiritual households or constellations

Oikos - An ecology, the peoples of the houses, the symmetries and geometries between houses

Syzygy - A shared house, an ecology of revelation where multiple beings work together

Malakut - The realm where images exist without physical substance, the imaginal world

• • •

Amen - Phonetics and Sacred Meaning

C7 · October 11, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Etymology and Universal Usage

The word Amen is shared across the three Abrahamic traditions:

  • Amin (Judaism)
  • Amen (Christianity)
  • Ameen (Islam)

Same root, same word.

It comes from the same root as the word Aman that we intone. It's related to the word Amana — the Covenant. It bespeaks faithfully upholding a trust, respecting a covenant older than time, a fundamental agreement between ourselves and the Absolute.

Phonetics of Amen — A Complete Arc of Existence

A — (Ah)
  • Mouth open, vibrating in the chest
  • The sound of LIFE
  • "Feel it right there in your chest"
M — (Mim/meme)
  • Lips closed
  • The sound of DEATH — but death as transformation, not ending
EN
  • Begins in the jawz (resonance point)
  • The sound of RESURRECTION: 'life revealing itself in a further mode of life'

Death and Resurrection Teaching

"Death doesn't mean what we think it means. Death is not the end. Death is a transformation. After the Mim comes the higher sound — after death, the resurrection, life revealing itself in a further mode of life. Death and resurrection — and this is brought home to us at the end of every prayer."

"All of us will physically die. And we don't know when. But this form of life, this mode of existence, is only for a time. But what we imagine is the end is not the end."

"Throughout all of the permutations of existence, the presiding imperative is the enactment of the ancient covenant — the realization of our agreement with the Absolute."

• • •

Beej Mantras - Seed Syllables

C9 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Beej Mantras: Sanskrit term for seed syllables

Context from Teaching

"It's said that the words La ilaha illa Allah boil down to three sounds: Ha, Hu, and He. And the Ha is in the chest, and it has its roots deep in the earth."

"Each of these three Beej mantras — Ha, Hu, He — corresponds to one of the dimensions of the primal created being, which is to say: the universe itself."

Ha = the body of the primal/universal creature

These are the fundamental sound vibrations that connect us to different aspects of cosmic being through intonation practice.

• • •

Chthonic and Telluric Energy

C9 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Chthonic: Relating to or inhabiting the underworld; of the earth or soil; subterranean

Telluric: Of or relating to the earth; terrestrial; earth energy

Context from Teaching

"To give one's attention to it is to begin to notice the upwelling of chthonic energy, telluric life — which moves in the tailbone, in the channel that arises from the tailbone up through the spinal shaft, through the belly, up into the chest."

These terms describe the earth-based life force that rises through the spine during the Ha practice, connecting us to the planetary body and its core energy.

• • •

Ittisal - Mystical Conjunction

C9 · October 12, 2025 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan

Ittisal (Arabic: اتصال)

Meaning: junction, connection, conjunction

Sufi Definition: The mystical union between the individual soul and the cosmic being

Context from Teaching

"This is the first in a sequence of intonations, connecting us with the cosmic person by way of Ittisal conjunction."

Ha is the first link in this sequence of mystical connection through sound.

Salawat — The Complete Form

C16 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Three-prayer close marking the end of the November weekend. The Khatum is introduced here for the first time in Section II.

Salawat

O most gracious sovereign, messenger, Messiah, and Savior of humanity,

we greet thee with all humility.

Thou art the first cause and the last effect,

the divine light and the spirit of guidance,

Alpha and Omega.

Thy light is in all forms,

Thy love in all beings:

in a loving mother, in a kind father, in an innocent child,

in a helpful friend, in an inspiring teacher.

Allow us to recognize thee in all thy holy names and forms:

as Sita and Rama, as Radha and Krishna,

as Parvati, Shiva, Tara, and Buddha.

Let us know thee as Sarah, Hagar, and Abraham,

as Deborah and Solomon,

as Anahita and Zarathustra,

as a seer, Aaron, Miriam, and Moses,

as Mary and Jesus, as Khadijah and Muhammad,

and in the many other names and forms known and unknown to the world.

We adore Thy past.

Thy presence deeply enlightens our being,

and we look for Thy blessing in the future.

O Messenger, Christ, Nabi, the Rasul of God,

Thou whose heart constantly reaches upward,

Thou comest on earth with a message

as a dove from above, when Dharma decays,

and speakest the word that is put into Thy mouth

as the light filleth the crescent moon.

Let the star of the divine light shining in Thy heart

be reflected in the hearts of Thy devotees.

May the message of God reach far and wide,

illuminating and making the whole humanity

as one single family in the parenthood of God.

Amen.

Khatum

O Thou, who art the perfection of love, harmony, and beauty,

the sovereign of heaven and earth,

open our hearts that we may hear Thy voice

which constantly cometh from within.

Disclose to us Thy divine light which is hidden in our souls,

that we may know and understand life better.

Most merciful and compassionate God,

give us Thy great goodness,

teach us Thy loving forgiveness,

raise us above the distinctions and differences which divide us.

Send us the peace of that divine spirit

and unite us all in that perfect being.

Amen.

And letting go for a moment, for these two days, of everything that is hindering us to be in the space that we need. Just let go."

This gesture serves as a symbolic releasing of all that would impede spiritual presence and openness.
