Fifth Aspect of Prayer - Union and Communion

C19 · December 14, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The fifth and final aspect of Murshid's five aspects of prayer — the completion of the arc begun in C11 with gratitude:

"The fifth element of prayer is beyond thanksgiving, beyond repentance and healing, beyond supplication, and beyond invocation."

"There is the same aspect in prayer. We spent time with the aspect of invocation — the calling of the beloved. What is the next step? It's finding him, it's finding her. It's being in communion with the one."

Complete Review - Five Aspects of Prayer as Lived Life

The five aspects of prayer not as ritual moments but as qualities of lived experience encountered throughout each day:

1. GRATITUDE

A sudden outburst of thankfulness to the one; or a daily review in the evening. Not a fixed form, but a quality of cherishing what is given, usually hidden from attention.

2. REPENTANCE / HEALING

Moments of introspection: looking at deeds, how we managed situations, how it might have affected others. By putting it before the all-compassionate, being healed and strengthened to be more wakeful in the next situation.

3. SUPPLICATION / HAIYA

In moments of stillness, contact with the pure vision of one's path. The deep wish that one might get all the support needed. Desires closer and closer to one's true path within the one.

4. INVOCATION

In moments of intimacy, a heavy or uplifted heart: longing, love, sincere wishing for the presence of the one. Like the lover singing a song with no wish but to be with the ultimate.

5. UNION / COMMUNION

Moments of complete stillness. No name, no word. No me and thee. Just the one. No separation between the lover and the beloved. Love, lover, and beloved — just one.

"You're invited to be with these five aspects of prayer. Sometimes you might just be aware that you've suddenly, most naturally, been in the mode of one of these aspects — not even planned. It was a natural rising of this aspect. As this thankfulness or this longing — in the end it's nothing that's produced. It's something that's in you that comes forth."

"Live in the space of this thankfulness, the space of repentance and healing, the clarification of your desire, your path, the pursuit of the beloved, and the presence of the ineffable."

• • •

Salat — Prayer of Benediction

C20 · December 14, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The Two Forms

Half Prostration (previously taught):

  • Putting the hands before us and bowing down
  • Without going down towards the ground
  • Hands placed like on a stool in front of you

Full Prostration (new teaching):

  • Go down to the full prostration on the ground
  • Hands in front of you
  • Head touching the ground

The Significance of Full Prostration

"One of the wonderful things about this is that in this position, the heart is higher than the brain. And it is, as far as I know, the early way our body is formed in the early stages in the womb of the mother."

This physical positioning creates a specific energetic state where:

  • The heart takes precedence over the mind
  • We return to our most primal formation
  • The body remembers its original sacred geometry

Part II · Chapter 2

CHIVALRIC RULES & IRON RULES

The Ethical Foundation of the Path

Urs wove the Chivalric Rules into his elemental teachings, showing how ethical refinement connects to the practice of concentration and the purification of the elements.

5 Entries · Urs Qutbuddin Schellenberg

✿

Do Not Reproach Others Rule

C11 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The Rule

"My conscientious self, do not reproach others, making them firm in their faults."

Teaching Context

Urs offered this guidance on receiving the rules:

"The rules are an invitation. They are not set because these rules change with the ears and the tongues that hear them and speak them. They change with your biography, with where you're at."

"So it's an invitation to work with them. It's not a call to uphold each and every of these rules. And not at all is there any inclination to judge any of us in the way that we connect with the rules. They are like lenses that help us to explore ourselves, our connection with the world, and be aware of our moral compass."

Understanding "Making Them Firm in Their Faults"

"The part 'making them firm in their faults' — by addressing it harshly, you ask them in a way to put their concentration on this very specific aspect of their being. And as we will address today: when we focus on a certain part in us, it is strengthened. It will grow bigger."

"Maybe you've been in situations where your friend entered the mode of defending this very aspect of their being. So it strengthened it."

Positive Orientation

"An aspect of this rule invites us to take very good care of the feeling of others, and if ever possible, meet them in a loving, supportive way — in which you can still address your discomfort. But your aim is not to lash out at your friend, but to make way for some healing that needs be."

"God is love, and this love is also expressed through our own hearts."

• • •

Rule - Do Not Spare Yourself in the Work You Must Accomplish

C13 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The Rule

"My conscientious self, do not spare yourself in the work that you must accomplish."

Understanding Balance

"One of the core teachings of Murshid is balance. That is so important in his teaching that he could have never meant that we should grind ourselves in work and exhaust ourselves. He always points out that we should be as balanced as possible with action and repose, with work and rest."

"Work could not happen for long if we didn't have enough rest. So let's keep this in mind: the rule is not asking us only to be on the active side of our life."

What Is the Work We Must Accomplish?

"The second part says: 'in the work that you must accomplish.' Now, what is this work? Is it the work others ask us to? There's always someone around us who needs something from us. There's an immeasurable load of work that we could be doing for people that ask us."

"But what is the work we actually came here for? What is the work that can only be done by us — by you? No one else?"

"The universe would not be complete without you as an expression of the one — a unique expression of the one."

"So it's not so much the question of doing much work, but what work? Where do we give our time to? What do we give our attention to? Do we make enough space that this true self can be expressed in this world? Not in the sense of a show, or that everything must be seen by other human beings — but that this longing of the soul may be expressed in the way that it is meant to be."

Pledge Practice

"I'm reading the words of the rule again. And if you feel in resonance with this rule, you can join in, or decide to deepen it further. You can close your eyes — as it is not important to see who is speaking the rule and who is not. Rules are always an invitation."

"My conscientious self, do not spare yourself in the work that you must accomplish."

• • •

Rule: Render Your Services Faithfully

C15 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The Rule:

"My conscientious self, render your services faithfully to all who require them."

Reading the Rule Carefully

★ Urs drew attention to the precise wording — 'all who require them' is not 'everyone who asks':

"It's helpful to look at this rule closely and carefully. It doesn't say: render your services to each and every one that asks. But it is a rule that invites us to see where we lend our services when there is a true need — when there is a need only you can fulfill with your being."

Pir Zia — The Bodhisattva of Service

★ Pir Zia's framing of this rule — Bodhisattva service as the model:

"Pir Zia describes it as like the service of the Bodhisattva that supports others to move obstacles out of their way so they have a smooth path on their way to enlightenment."

"Where can you be of service for people around you in supporting them to be uplifted, to be safe on their journey to the one? What are these needs for the greater good where you can render your help faithfully?"

On Faithful Service

"What could it mean to render it faithfully? Full of trust and in contact with your true being."

"Maybe on a simple level, this rule asks us: if we are only preoccupied with our own sorrows and work that lies ahead, or if there is time and space we can make to be of service for others who truly need it."

Pledge

★ Opt-in pledge — same format as prior rules:

"If you are planning to take up this rule and take a pledge, we can say it together — or you can decide to contemplate it a bit further, which is wonderful. You can close your eyes."

"My conscientious self, render your services faithfully to all who require them."

• • •

Rule: Seek Not Profit by Putting Someone in Straits

C18 · December 13, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The Rule

"My conscientious self, seek not profit by putting someone in straits."

Two Dimensions

"There is a basic need for all of us to provide ourselves with everything that supports our wellbeing, from food to our home, warmth, shelter. So there's an invitation to contemplate this aspect of the rule for seeking profit."

"But it doesn't end there. It highlights the seeking profit by putting someone in straits. It doesn't say anything about the profit itself — but the way by which we seek profit. So others are carrying the costs for our own profit."

Pir Vilayat — The Food Supply Chain

"Pir Vilayat reminds us of a wonderful approach which we meet daily: when we're providing food for ourselves and others. While in some cases you can go to a market and meet the people who produced the food, put their work and time and care into growing vegetables — we nowadays mostly find food on shelves. And you need to really look closely to find out where this produce comes from. What were the circumstances in which it was grown?"

"Who was involved? How is their wellbeing? Can they make sure they have their basic needs covered as well? Or when animals are involved, how were they kept? Were they treated well?"

"So many things have happened before something is ready to be bought by us. And so many beings have given time and energy to make it possible. Was it in a way that is supportive for all — for each and every one's wellbeing? Or have other beings been put into straits?"

Pledge

"My conscientious self, seek not profit by putting someone in straits."

• • •

Final Iron Rule - Harm No One for Your Own Benefit

C20 · December 14, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The Rule:

"My conscientious self, harm no one for your own benefit."

This is the 10th and final Iron Rule, completing the first section of chivalric codes.

Teaching

Both this rule and Rule 9 (C18) ask us not to gain or benefit by harming others. For most this is common sense, but the highlight is more in the aspects where we are not aware of how our seeking for benefit or profit harms other beings.

Two Stages of the Nafs

Nafs al-Ammara (النفس الأمّارة) - The Commanding Nafs:

  • The nafs that separates oneself from every other being
  • Holds up a very strong self-identity where the strength lies in supporting oneself alone
  • Seeks benefit at the expense of others
  • This benefit cannot last long when it comes at others' expense

Nafs al-Lawwama (النفس اللوّامة) - The Self-Reproaching Nafs:

  • Connected with each and everyone
  • Seeks reasonable profit to support oneself AND all those one is responsible for
  • Seeks benefit that is beneficial for all that we can reach
  • Profit that benefits our generation and all generations to come
  • Benefits people, plants, animals, the whole ecosystem, the planet

The Rule's Wisdom

The rule doesn't forbid seeking benefit or profit - but it asks: what sort of benefit, and whom does it benefit?

With this 10th rule, all the Iron Rules are now complete. Students are invited to revisit them, perhaps choosing one to be with for a few days to deepen understanding and experience.

✿ ✿ ✿
Part II · Chapter 3

BREATH PRACTICES

The Bridge Between Worlds

Urs taught the Five Elemental Purification Breaths — Earth, Water, Fire, Air, and Ether — each with specific directions, colors, and qualities. His approach to breath is deeply embodied and experiential.

6 Entries · Urs Qutbuddin Schellenberg

✿

Five Element Breathing Practice - Foundation

C11 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

This is the core elemental breathing practice that serves as the foundation for all element work. This basic form will be returned to repeatedly with deepening layers added.

Preparation

  • Close the eyes
  • Find a comfortable position that allows the breath to flow freely
  • Be aware of the connection of your feet — or the tailbone — to the ground

The Five Elements and Their Breath

Each element has a specific breath mode. The practice moves through all five in sequence:

Earth

Breath: Inhale through nose, exhale through nose

Quality: Steadiness, Patience

Instructions: "Breathe in through the nose and breathe out through the nose. Just be aware of your breath for a few moments. Now be in the presence of the element Earth — whatever the initial thought or feeling, whatever Earth symbolizes for you, just be in this presence for a few more breaths."

Water

Breath: Inhale through nose, exhale through mouth

Quality: Flow, Adaptability

Instructions: "Breathe in through the nose and breathe out through the mouth. And be in the presence of the element water, in whatever form it might be present."

Fire

Breath: Inhale through mouth, exhale through nose

Quality: Transformation, Energy

Instructions: "Breathe in through the mouth and out through the nose. Be in the presence of the fire element."

Air

Breath: Inhale through mouth, exhale through mouth

Quality: Freedom, Movement

Instructions: "Breathe in through the mouth and out through the mouth."

Ether

Breath: Subtle (both mouth and nose)

Quality: Vastness, Spaciousness

Instructions: "The breath is very subtle — through mouth and nose, very subtle, in and out. Just be aware of all the elements in the space beyond."

• • •

Earth Element Extended Practice - Three Layers

C12 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Urs returned to the Earth element from C11 and introduced three additional layers of practice beyond the basic elemental breath. These layers are cumulative — each builds on the last.

Layer 1 — Purification / Grounding Breath

New layer: Earth as a purification element — letting go through the out-breath, drawing in magnetism on the in-breath:

  1. Close the eyes. Bring awareness to the feet, tailbone, and knees — everything touching the earth.
  2. Breathe in through the nose, out through the nose (Earth mode).
  3. On the out-breath: let go of bodily tensions. Then let go of impressions, feelings, memories not needed right now.

"You can feel how they're falling off you through your feet, through this touch of the earth. And with a feeling of kindness towards the things you let go, you hand them over trustfully to earth with a feeling of thankfulness."

Let earth take good care and transform what you let go.

  1. On the in-breath: imagine drawing in through deep roots — earth magnetism, all the gifts of the element earth — strengthening and holding you.

"Let go on your out-breath and be filled with earth qualities on your in-breath."

Layer 2 — Direction: The Horizontal

Each element is connected to a specific direction of movement. Earth's direction is horizontal:

"Earth is connected to the horizontal line. When breathing out, you can imagine how your breath is moving in every direction on the horizon — along the plains, over the mountains."

This directional awareness opens the practice beyond the individual body into the vast flat expanse of the Earth plane — the planetary horizon in all directions simultaneously.

Layer 3 — Color: Yellow / Ocher

Each element is attributed a color. Earth's color is yellow or ocher:

"Earth is the color yellow or ocher. It's the color of the earth you might see when it's freshly dug up. It's this rich color of the soil."

Just be a moment with this yellow, this ocher. Be with its quality, its atmosphere.

Closing Counsel on the Layers

"The work with the elements has so many layers. Stay with the elements that you're drawn to. Keep it a bit playful, explore, and be with this element like you would be with a friend you haven't met for a long time."

• • •

Water Elemental Breath Practice - Complete Instructions

C13 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Basic Form

  • Breathe in through the nose, out through the mouth
  • "Already in the setting of the breath, you see there is a downward stream. So the direction of water is downward."

The Waterfall of Water and Light

On the in-breath: Let yourself be lifted way above your head, up into the clouds and even beyond.

On the out-breath: Imagine a stream of water with its true origin in the one — becoming water, a waterfall — a waterfall of water and light washing down on you, cleaning you, refreshing you.

"Not only wash the outside of your body, but this waterfall goes through you — through your veins, through every part of your body. Feel how your heart is washed and refreshed, your abdomen, your arms and legs. And everything is washed away that is not needed anymore."

Go way up on the in-breath. Let yourself be emerged in this waterfall of water and light that runs through you and all around you.

Working with Blockages

"Sometimes you can feel how the water is stuck in a certain place in your body. With a subtle breath, just steer this water towards this part. And maybe you experience a subtle opening. Maybe this part allows itself to be washed by this water."

Color Layer: Green

"The color of water is green — green as you see it in the different shades in the ocean and the lakes. You can add this layer to your concentration: to be merged not only in this waterfall, but also in this color that runs through you."

As Communion

"The elemental breath is like a communion — the outer and the inner, of the world around us and within us, the aspects of our personality, our individuality, and the universal — all that belongs to the one."

Day Practice

"When you take your next shower or ablution, be aware of the transformative power of water — how it is used in so many traditions to help us to transform from one state into another."

• • •

Three Element Breath Sequence - Complete Practice

C15 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

★ First time all three elements practiced in sequence in a single opening. Represents the cumulative practice arc of C11–C15. Each element's full layer set now included.

EARTH BREATH

In through nose · Out through nose · Direction: Horizontal · Color: Yellow/Ocher

"You might have already been greeted by the earth today. Be aware again of this communion — that which seems to be separate, your body from your surrounding, is one. It shares the same origin. And you share in qualities."

"When you breathe out, be aware of the earth breath rolling in every direction through all the horizons, mapping the land. Be present with the color yellow, the ocher."

"Each element has a healing aspect, a cleansing that is offered. Let go of everything that is not needed anymore — everything for which it is time to be let go. Hand it over to earth, where it will be transformed into new soil, nutritious ground for new life to emerge."

"Let go with your out-breath. And take in new magnetism of the earth. Let the earth qualities in you be refreshed. And we can remember the eshk, the longing, the love expressed through this gentle pull by the earth that holds us."

WATER BREATH

In through nose · Out through mouth · Direction: Downward · Color: Green

"Let yourself be lifted up with your in-breath, and then connect to this downstream of the water element from far above. This waterfall full of light coming from the source, washing all over you, through you, through your veins, your limbs, your heart, the abdomen."

"Be aware of the water in you — how it is greeting the water that is flowing through you. How it is cleansed by it, renewed. And when you sense a blockage, let this water gently wash through it, and maybe you can feel how a gentle flow is emerging again."

At-onement: "Feel this atonement, this at-onement — being one with the element water that surrounds you. The streams beneath you, the clouds in the sky, the vapor we breathe. Be aware of this constant flow and exchange."

"Be aware of the color green — this shimmering green that is ever changing when you look out into the water. It's reflecting light. Sometimes you can see through."

FIRE BREATH

In through mouth · Out through nose · Direction: Ascending · Color: Red (belly) → Pure Light (above)

★ Fire element introduced for the first time in the breath sequence:

"While water is descending, the fire element is ascending. It's going up. Imagine fire burning in your belly with that red color. And with your in-breath, you supply it with the oxygen necessary."

"Everything that needs transformation through fire can be put in there. Fire consumes and transforms small things very quickly — lights them up, transforms them into heat and light. And there are things that take longer to be consumed by the fire, but this fire is ever burning."

"It rises up. When you follow this fire in your body rising up, you see it's getting more and more light. Warm light the further it gets upwards — transformed into pure light. And on your out-breath, you can be with this pure light shining from your inside out in every direction into your subtle body, your subtle body of light."

"Maybe you can feel how your body is heating up — feel the warmth produced in every cell. You can feel that fire is a part of your innate nature."

Slowly return to natural breath. Let go of this concentration.

ELEMENTAL PRACTICE SUMMARY — C11 THROUGH C15

EARTH · In/Out: Nose→Nose · Direction: Horizontal · Color: Yellow/Ocher · Quality: Patience, steadfastness, eshk as gentle holding · Healing: Release into soil; draw in magnetism

WATER · In/Out: Nose→Mouth · Direction: Downward · Color: Green · Quality: Flow, adaptability, cleansing, at-onement · Healing: Waterfall of light washing through; clearing blockages in Lataif

FIRE · In/Out: Mouth→Nose · Direction: Ascending · Color: Red (belly) → Pure Light (rising) · Quality: Transformation, will, eshk as consuming love · Healing: Burns what needs transforming; purifies to pure light

Two more elements — Air and Ether — to be introduced in the December weekend (C17–C20).

• • •

Complete Four-Element Breath Practice with Living Beings

C17 · December 13, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The full elemental sequence as practiced in Concentration 1 Part 2, with each element now enriched with awareness of living beings:

EARTH

Method: In/Out: Nose→Nose | Direction: Horizontal | Color: Yellow/Ocher

"While you're breathing out, be aware of your earthly element in your body. Be with this feeling of letting go of everything you don't need anymore — handing it over to earth. You can breathe it out through the soles of your feet. And be revivified on your in-breath, taking in this earthly magnetism that is given as a gift."

Living Beings of Earth: "Be aware of all the living beings that live in or very close to the earth: worms and insects, mammals that build their living spaces in the earth, seek that closeness to this element, or all the plants united through their web of roots, the fungi with their unseen web of communication — all hidden in the earth. Being aware of all these beings is being aware of the friendship we can hold in this reality that we share."

WATER

Method: In/Out: Nose→Mouth | Direction: Downward | Color: Green

"On your in-breath you can feel how you're lifted up, straightened, where your spine is lengthened — you follow it way up to the heavens. And on your out-breath through the mouth, imagine this stream of water, this waterfall immersed in light, running through every part of your body, renewing and washing every corner."

Living Beings of Water: "Reconnect with the waters around you. Be aware of all the beings living in the waters: fish and mammals, from the very large to the smallest insects that make the waters their home, or on the waters like the ducks. They hold a deep wisdom of this element by living in and on it so closely. There is much to share."

FIRE

Method: In/Out: Mouth→Nose | Direction: Ascending | Color: Red→Pure Light

"Breathing in, we can imagine drawing this air onto a fire in our belly — heating it up, flames rising. And from fire we see the light. On your out-breath you can imagine how you breathe out from your heart center pure light in every direction."

Living Being of Fire: "Fire spirits living in the heat. A salamander was believed to be able to live in the highest heat and quench a fire. Seen and unseen beings living in the elements."

AIR (New)

Method: In/Out: Mouth→Mouth | Direction: All Directions / Zigzag | Color: Blue

"It is the finest of the elements before ether. And it's very much connected to our breath. We breathe in through the mouth and we breathe out through the mouth. Maybe you can hear the sound of the air moving between your lips — it sounds like the wind."

"Air is moving in every possible direction. It's more of a zigzag — the wind that changes. And it's the element that we on the one hand hardly see or touch, and on the other hand, it is so close to us like the water is close to a fish. We are living in the air. We are in a constant exchange through our in-breath and out-breath."

Living Beings of Air: "There are those beings even more immersed in this element: birds, insects with wings, bats — moving through this element in their very own dance. From nervous, joyful zigzag to the majestic circles high above. There is so much wisdom in their lives of this element air."

Daily Practice Guidance

"It is most advisable to choose the elemental breath as the one daily practice — if you are overwhelmed by all the possible practices you could be doing, or life just doesn't give you enough space."

"It is advised to do this practice in the morning, and if you can, to do it outside in the fresh air. The contact with the elements is more immediate outside. Maybe you can step outside on a veranda, garden, or even an open window."

"In the daily practice, it is just five breaths — five breaths for each element. Of course you can always prolong it, but as a daily practice, it's a revisiting of your state how it woke up, and the reality with all its dimensions."

• • •

Complete Five-Element Breath Practice with Ether

C19 · December 14, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The first time the full five-element sequence is practiced in one sitting — the complete elemental breath as it will be done as a daily practice. Earth through Ether:

EARTH · Nose→Nose · Horizontal · Yellow/Ocher

"We let go of everything heavy that burdens us. We hand it over to earth. Let it be transformed, and we breathe in new magnetism. Earth lends you patience, endurance. There's a strength not easily shaken."

WATER · Nose→Mouth · Downward · Green

"Breathing out, be washed by this water, cleansed. This waterfall of pure refreshing water full of light, moving through every part in your body and your whole being, washing everything away that needs purification. Whatever the obstacle may be — like water, you will find a way through it."

FIRE · Mouth→Nose · Ascending · Red

"You can feel the warmth or even the heat rising. The flame going higher — become pure light. The fire that has the Ishq that burns everything except the beloved. The fire that lights us up to intensify our quest for the ideal."

AIR · Mouth→Mouth · All directions · Blue

"The air moving in every direction — the most subtle of the elements. Sometimes strong and powerful, but often very subtle. This constant stream of the breath is a communion with the element air. The air blowing through you, cleansing you."

ETHER · Subtle (mouth and nose both) · No direction · No color

"The quintessence of all the elements. Akash. Asman. A very fine breath through the mouth and the nose, on both the in and the out breath."

"It has no color. It has no direction, and it has no form. And as the quintessence of all the elements, it has all the colors, all the forms, and all the directions when expressed in the elements. The elements express what is hidden in ether. All emerges from it and all dissolves back into it. Ether is intimately present and yet ineffable."

Three Planes of Ether

"There is an ether of the body, ether of the mind, and ether of the spirit. In ether of the body, physical forms transpire. In ether of the mind, thoughts transpire. In ether of the spirit, souls transpire. It's like skies within skies within skies."

"After five breaths with every element, you enter the presence of ether. Just present with the dissolving of each and every element, present in silence. Aware of the union of all the elements in total balance. And when you do this practice in the morning, you can stay in ether as long as you wish and taste this essence of the elements."

Part II · Chapter 4

CONCENTRATION, VISUALIZATION & MEDITATION

Training the Sovereign Attention

Urs's approach to concentration emphasizes gentle attention over forceful will — the parent at a sick child's bedside rather than the warrior's focused determination. His practices include dot-on-wall gazing, color immersion, and elemental concentration.

20 Entries · Urs Qutbuddin Schellenberg

✿

Bridge from Concentration to Contemplation

C11 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Urs introduced a key arc for these two weekends — the transition from outer concentration to inner contemplation. This marks a significant shift from Section I.

The Progression

"In these two weekends, we already approach a bridge from concentration to contemplation."

"You might have already realized that there is no pure form of concentration that doesn't already lap into a meditative state — or that has very much in common with contemplation."

The progression described:

  • Section I: Concentration on outer objects (dot, colors, senses)
  • Now: Concentration on beings in imagination — beings one knows
  • Next: Moving toward abstract qualities of those beings
  • There: Already in the midst of contemplation

Two Modes of Concentration

"Concentration can come, for example, in a very strong focus — in a willful focus. But it can also come as a very gentle attention."

"A gentle attention which we might see in a parent sitting by the bed of a sick child, just being there, totally being there. Not being with his or her own sorrows, but being there fully attentive to this being."

"Sometimes it's in this mode that we concentrate on a certain aspect in our life, on a certain being, on the resonance, a quality — attentive to the one being."

Depth Over Multiplicity

"I would like to remind you of the story of the pupil who made a whole wall crumble just by mastering the Alif. And in this story, we already see that in a single practice, there can be the whole universe."

This teaching anchors the counsel: rather than being distracted by the multiplicity of practices, go deeply into one — as the pupil went deeply into the Alif.

• • •

Visualizing an Inspiring Being Practice

C12 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

This practice marks the transition from concentrating on objects toward concentrating on beings — thereby crossing the threshold from concentration into contemplation.

Practice Instructions

  1. Close the eyes.
  1. Imagine a person who is inspiring to you — someone you know personally, someone you have met, or someone whose qualities you know clearly from afar.

"It could also be a person you just know of, and you have a clear picture of that person and this person's uplifting atmosphere. It might be a person that you adore for what they stand for, what they did in their life. But eventually it's a person that has truly become herself — and reminds you of becoming yourself."

  1. Imagine this person sitting with you, in front of you.
  1. Be aware of the atmosphere, the resonance evoked through this being.
  1. If your mind wanders, just go back to this being. Keep it present.

"Use your imagination to have this being in your presence as palpable as possible, with these qualities that you admire."

  1. Feel the resonance in you. This focus can have an imprint on your thoughts, your feelings, the atmosphere you're in.

The Teaching Behind the Practice

"What we experience in the outer resonates in our minds. And that which our minds hold is reflected by our souls."

"The mind is the filter for the light of our soul — for what we show in the world of our true being, or what's not shown yet, maybe because the filter of the mind has another focus."

• • •

Feeling the Pulse - Water Element Inner Awareness

C13 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Practice Instructions

  1. Close the eyes
  2. Be aware of the water element within you — the element most of your body consists of
  3. Focus on the heart — It is most palpable in the heart, where the bloodstream is constantly pumped through every vessel in each part of the body
  4. Try to feel the pulse, the throbbing
  5. If it's not easy to feel, touch certain parts of the body: below the chest, the wrist, gently on the neck

"Just be aware for a moment of this constant movement within. Be aware of this watery existence you are."

Teaching Context

"On the inside of our bodies, it [water] is the predominant element. It's always hard to imagine because with our eyes open, we see a fixed set of body. But when we look inside us, we realize there is so much fluidity, so much water — always in constant movement, a movement that is necessary for us to be alive."

Movement as Life

"One aspect of water is its movement. If it doesn't move in our bodies, it has dire consequences. When water doesn't move on the street, it builds a puddle. When it stays there for a while, it gets murky and you can't see through it anymore."

"The moment it starts flowing again, it shows its revivifying and cleansing ability — the refreshing."

• • •

River Visualization Practice

C13 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Instructions

  1. Sit in the atmosphere of Astaghfirullah
  2. Imagine a river — a river you are sitting beside
  3. Imagine its color
  4. See the ground beneath it if visible
  5. See animals living in it
  6. See the lush vegetation and plants growing by its side
  7. Maybe you can hear it — this constant murmur
  8. See the reflected light
  9. Stay with this picture — Always return to the flow of this river

Returning to the Body

After the visualization:

  • "Now you can let go of this inner vision"
  • "Be aware of your body. What was the imprint of it?"
  • "How does your body feel? How is your breath? What is moving inside you?"
  • "You can feel your feet, come back and open your eyes again"

Context

This visualization followed the Astaghfirullah zikr practice, connecting the flow of water to the flow of divine forgiveness and the cleansing quality of repentance.

• • •

Color Concentration Practice - Brown to Green

C14 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

This practice develops concentration through a slow, intentional color shift — from brown (earth, density) to green (water, life, growth). It bridges the two elements worked with this weekend.

Practice Instructions

  1. Close the eyes.
  1. Imagine the color brown, just as it appears to you. Be surrounded by this color. Immersed. Just try to hold this presence of this color brown.
  1. Now slowly shift from brown to green — imagine how from brown there emerges the color green, step by step: a slow transformation.
  1. "When you've arrived with the color green, sit with this color. Be totally immersed in it. Always return to green again."
  1. Notice if there is a shift in experience between brown and green. Just stay in green for a moment.
  1. Slowly let the color fade away. Return to the breath. Feel the feet on the ground. Feel the body again. Open the eyes.

Teaching Context:

This practice reinforces the deeper pattern of the weekend: from Earth's steadiness and density into Water's life, flow, and greenness. The color shift is also a concentration technique — sustaining and guiding a subtle, willed transformation of the inner visual field.

• • •

Tailbone Concentration Practice

C14 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

A full body-awareness concentration practice, using the tailbone as the anchor point.

Opening Questions — Entering the Practice

Close the eyes. Return to the tailbone.

What happens when you're asked to be with your tailbone? What does it mean to shift your awareness to a certain place in your body? How does it feel?

"Is it a sensation of a mind sitting in your head, watching down to the tailbone? Or is it slowly shifting the whole awareness to that tailbone? How does the breath flow in and out?"

Deepening Inquiry

What comes to your awareness? How does it affect your posture?

Do you feel a warmth? Or is it cool? Is it still? Or can you feel a movement in the tailbone?

Concentrate on the tailbone and be aware of what is happening in it and around it.

"The legs, the abdomen, the upper body, the breath, the mind."

Breath into the Tailbone

Always return to the tailbone.

"It is possible to concentrate on a part in your body and still be aware of the surroundings."

Breathe in to the tailbone and breathe out through it.

The legs, the abdomen, the upper body, the breath, the mind.

Closing — Resonance Check

Notice: Do you still feel a shift? Does it still change? Has it come to rest? Is it constant?

Now, slowly return to natural breath. Let go of the concentration.

For a moment, feel what resonance is left — if any.

• • •

Three-Stage Being Visualization

C14 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

This is the culminating concentration practice of the November weekend — a direct enactment of the bridge from concentration (outer objects) toward contemplation (inner and non-physical beings).

Stage 1 — A Person You Know

Close the eyes. Take a few deep breaths. Feel the body.

Breathe in through the nose, out through the mouth.

Think of someone you know — a friend, a relative. Think of that person's name.

Let this person with that name appear before you. Use your creative imagination to really see this person in front of you, as clear as possible. Recollect your memory of their appearance.

Try to hold this image. Be aware of your resonance. How does it change your mood? What do you feel?

Let go of this image. Take a few breaths.

Stage 2 — A Person You Know Of (but not personally)

Think of a person you don't personally know, but have heard of — still living or from the past. An inspiring person, a teacher, a saint.

Be with their name. By their name, be with their appearance in front of you. You might not have a clear image — see what image is created before you.

Be in the presence of this being. Be aware of the atmosphere, of your breath, of your posture, your resonance.

Stage 3 — A Non-Physical Being

Imagine a being that has not existed on the physical plane — an angel, a jinn, a Bodhisattva in its pre-earthly stage.

Be with this image. Be in the presence of this being.

Be aware of the atmosphere of your breath, your posture, your resonance.

Finally, let this image also fade away. Return to your natural breath. Your feet. Slowly feel your body again. Open your eyes.

The Arc of the Practice

The three stages map onto an ascending interior arc:

  • Stage 1 — Personal memory; the being is known through direct experience; resonance is immediate and personal
  • Stage 2 — Transmitted image; the being is known through report; the imagination works with what has been received from others
  • Stage 3 — Pure imagination; no physical counterpart; the subtle senses reach beyond form entirely

"This is the threshold where concentration becomes contemplation."

• • •

Burning Torch Concentration Practice

C15 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

★ Fire as concentration object. The torch as purposeful fire: not burning for its own sake but to shed light.

After the fire teachings, Urs guided a concentration practice using the burning torch as object — the form of fire that is most deliberately directed toward a single purpose: illumination.

Practice Instructions

  1. Close the eyes.
  1. Imagine a burning torch in front of you. The torch uses fire for a specific purpose: to shed light.
  1. Imagine this fire of the torch as vivid as possible. See its colors. Its movements. Its ever-changing character. How the flames seem to dance. The emerging light.
  1. When you wander off, gently come back to this image of the burning torch.
  1. Keep your gaze a little bit longer on this torch.
  1. Slowly let this image go. Just be aware of your pure state, your breath, your body. Sit with it for a moment.

Teaching

"The torch uses the fire for a specific purpose: that is to shed light."

The torch is fire that has been given intention — it does not burn freely and wildly but is held, directed, purposeful. This practice is both a concentration exercise and a teaching image: the fire of the soul, when it has been contained by will and given a direction, becomes a torch. It illuminates rather than consumes.

Color Concentration - Green to Orange

C16 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

As the final concentration of the November weekend, this practice extends the brown→green transformation of earlier sessions and introduces orange for the first time.

Practice Instructions:

  1. Enter the color green. Let yourself be immersed in it.
  2. Now slowly let this green turn into orange — a slow fade from one color to the other.
  3. Until fully arrived with orange: be with this color for a moment.
  4. Let it go. Return to the body and feet.

Teaching Note:

Orange has not yet been formally assigned to an element in the curriculum as taught. It may anticipate the Air or Ether element teachings in December, or serve as a bridging color between fire's red and ether's more luminous palette.

Energy Ball Practice - Opening Session

C16 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Practice Instructions

  1. Slowly massage the left arm with the right hand — from the shoulder all the way down to the hands. Several times. Don't forget the hands. Not hard — just activating through touch.
  1. Change arms: massage the right arm with the left, all the way down from the shoulder to the hands. Gently stroke it down.
  1. Gently breathe on your palms.
  1. Rest the hands on the knees. On the in-breath, slowly lift both arms up in front of you. On the out-breath, let them sink back to the knees.
  1. Let them rest on the knees for a moment.
  1. Raise the hands again — palms now facing each other. Play with the distance between them.

Energy Ball Awareness

"There is a moment where there is this feeling of holding a ball between them. You can gently squeeze it and give way again — allow it. Stay with the gentle breath. With your out-breath, you can even make this ball a bit larger. Just be aware of this sensation."

  1. Place the left hand on the right chest and the right hand on the left chest. While breathing in, giving it a bit of space. When breathing out, return to the chest.
  1. Lower the hands. Rest them on the knees. Sit with it for a short moment.

Teaching Point

This exercise demonstrates that a shifted focus of awareness reveals phenomena already present in the body — subtle fields, warmth, the sensation of the etheric body between the palms. The practice is both grounding and a direct entry into energy perception.

• • •

Fana-fi-Sheikh - Three Stages Practice

C16 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Fana-fi-Sheikh is the practice where we are invited to be in the presence of Murshid, and through his presence, in the presence of all the murshids that have become him or her — the light that shines through this lineage and through this being.

Stage 1 — The Image

  • Build the inner image of Murshid, your chosen guide — as if you would sit before him or her.
  • Create a clear picture. Imagine being seen. You are not looking at an object — you are looking at a living subject looking back at you.
  • "It's a most intimate meeting. Your glance meets Murshid's glance. There's nothing to hide. You're just who you are, the way you're meant to be, and you're seen as this."
  • Be aware: you are in the presence not just of one murshid, but of the whole Silsila reaching back in time — the light of all those murshids before.
  • "You're in the presence of this very specific fragrance. Sometimes you can almost smell it. It's an atmosphere you're encompassed in."
  • There is an intimate connection through the breath: through your breathing out, Murshid breathes it in. Through your breathing in, he or she breathes it out.
  • "Try to keep the soft concentration, the awareness, the sympathy, as Murshid says. Be aware of this atmosphere."

Stage 2 — The Atmosphere

  • Let go of the image.
  • Let this atmosphere, this taste, this palpable presence of this being — let it reside in your heart. Be immersed in this light.
  • "You're not focusing on an image anymore. You are holding the atmosphere — pure presence. And it's no longer opposite you. Now it's in your heart, and it's around you."
  • Hold it alive. Hold it present. Settle in it. Be at rest.

Stage 3 — Merging

"Eventually the third stage of Fana-fi-Sheikh is when this being becomes a part of you. When Murshid's speech is expressed in yours. You hear with Murshid's ears. And when you walk, there is something of Murshid's walk in your way."

"And this is a much different way of transmission than just exchanging information."

Summary:

  • Stage 1 — Image: outer concentration on a living subject; glance meets glance; the Silsila as presence and fragrance
  • Stage 2 — Atmosphere: image released; pure presence held in the heart; the teacher is no longer opposite but within and around
  • Stage 3 — Merging: the teacher's qualities express through one's own speech, hearing, gait; transmission without exchange of content
• • •

Three Contemplation Practices

C16 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

These practices are described as being 'at the crossroad of concentration and contemplation' — each one asking the student to hold an intangible quality as an object of awareness, rather than an image, a sensation, or a being.

Practice 1 — A Character Trait

  • Think of a character trait you see in people you know, or in yourself — a habit, a mode of acting in life, a tendency. Perhaps highly focused, slightly distracted. Perhaps the habit of giving everything into a certain hobby.
  • Take one character trait and be with it. Explore it. Be in its resonance.
  • "How does it feel? What is its atmosphere, its taste? By focusing on it, by being with it, we explore something deeper that might otherwise be a neglected thing of daily life. But there is richness in it."
  • We approach an inner understanding of this mode of being.
  • Let it go.

Practice 2 — A Driving Motivation

  • Choose a driving motivation — a motivation for people to get out of bed in the morning, to thrive, to put in their effort. For some it's accumulating worldly richness or power. For some it's to be remembered, to leave an impression. For others it's care, or the longing for beauty.
  • Choose one — perhaps you see it in others, perhaps you see parts of it in yourself. Stay with it for a while and explore it.
  • "How does it feel to be motivated by this? What is the quality of it? We're not understanding it by analyzing it — but in this practice, we understand something by being in its presence, feeling its quality, and seeing what emerges when we're in contact with it."
  • Let it go.

Practice 3 — A Spiritual Aspiration

  • Think of yourself or people you know. Try to pick a spiritual aspiration — something that's keeping them on their path, something that brought them to the path, something that was a longing, maybe an ideal, maybe a concrete wish.
  • Explore it for a while. Be with it.
  • Slowly let go of this aspiration. Take a few breaths. Let the images and impressions go.
• • •

Breath Still-Point Concentration

C18 · December 13, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Practice Instructions

  1. Find a comfortable position — rooted, breath flowing easily
  2. Be aware of the breath for a few moments
  3. Let go of the out-breath a little further. Don't press it — relax and let it flow out
  4. At the end of the exhalation: hold briefly. Not uncomfortable — just hold and savor this moment
  5. Feel how your breath is, by itself, moving from the out-breath to the in-breath. There is no conscious will needed. The air flows in all by itself

Teaching on Magnetism

Murshid tells a story told in India about the cobras — that the cobras' magnetism is so strong that they don't need to hunt their prey. By magnetism and patience, he writes, the mouse will climb into the cobra's mouth by itself. And there is a quality of this magnetism in this still point after the out-breath.

This still-point — the moment between the exhale completing and the inhale beginning — is where the body's natural magnetism is most palpable. No will is needed; life moves by itself. A teaching on effortless attraction and the power of patient stillness.

• • •

Skull Light Concentration — The Luminous Glance

C18 · December 13, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

A practice on the light the being radiates outward through the eyes — exploring Murshid's teaching that the glance sheds light as much as it receives it.

Practice Instructions

  1. Sit straight, shoulders relaxed. Connect to the awareness of density in the body — feel the form given through density.
  1. Become aware of the space in this part of the body. Imagine it very subtly expanding — letting go of denseness, becoming aware of the permeability of your being. You are not truly separate from everything around you.
  1. Expand this feeling to the skull — the head. Be aware of this cask of bone. Let go and expand: be aware of the space where the brain is.
  1. "It can merge with a feeling of the heaven reaching into this part — as if there was no fixed boundary between the heaven and your upper part of your head. Merged with the luminosity of the heaven — this pure blue, luminous sphere."
  1. Through the front of your head above the eyes — as if your head were a crystal — feel the light entering on the in-breath. On the out-breath, from the center of your skull, this light is answered by your light shining back.
  1. "It is like a beam from the midst of your brain being cast through your forehead, above the eyes. You can imagine what is in front of you in your room — and without looking, cast with your out-breath out this light. On your in-breath, feel the resonance."
  1. Just be with it for a few breaths. Cast out the beam through your forehead. On the in-breath — feel the resonance. You might physically feel a shift around the eyes and forehead: expansion, a feeling of pouring something within you outward.

Opening the Eyes

As the next step — on the out-breath only — open the eyes with this feeling of the beams. Look slightly above the screen or turn a little to the side so the glance reaches something in the room.

"It will not be a focused glance — maybe you don't even see it clearly, but it's a glance that comes from within you and is shining out into the world. On your in-breath, close your eyes again, gather, be aware of the light. On the out-breath, open the eyes again — aware of these beams shedding light on a part of the room."

The Teaching Behind the Practice

"This concentration is a way to experience the light that we pour out into the world. Usually we are mostly thinking of the light that is entering us through our eyes. But Murshid says: through a luminous glance, there's also light which is shed by us, through us."

• • •

Star, Crescent Moon, and Heart Visualization

C18 · December 13, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

A layered inner construction practice, building three sacred forms in sequence — the three forms of the Inayatiyya symbol.

Practice Instructions

  1. Form the Star: Form before you in your inner vision a star — a five-pointed star. Geometric at first: peak on top, two spikes to the sides, two below.
  1. Make it Vivid: Now make it vivid. Be aware of its glance, its light, how it's shining. Keep this image. Return to it when drawn away.
  1. Add the Crescent Moon: Underneath the star: sculpt the image of a crescent moon, starting to grow, reflecting the light of the star. Its cool, silver light. Take joy in sculpting it and watching it take its form, shining in its beauty.
  1. Surround with Heart: Now draw around the star and the moon the shape of a heart — surrounding both. Keep this image for a moment.
  1. Dissolve in Reverse: Slowly let go of the heart and the moon — just the star remains.
  1. Complete Release: Now let go of the star and relax.

Star · Crescent Moon · Heart — the three forms of the Inayatiyya symbol, built and dissolved in sequence.

• • •

Elements Mapped to Stages of Concentration

C19 · December 14, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The five elements as five stages of the concentration arc, from outer object to union. The deepest philosophical integration of the elemental and concentration work — showing they are the same journey:

EARTH — Meeting the object

Awareness of the material reality of what is before you. The solid, the concrete, the given.

WATER — Flow between self and object

Through presence, a flow begins. The element water is present — this combining flow. One is no longer merely looking; one is in resonance.

FIRE — The object becomes a subject

One becomes aware that one is actually meeting a subject, a being. This being is lighted up, and we are aware of the spirit behind it, within it.

AIR — Increasing subtlety

The sitting with the subject becomes finer and finer. We become aware of the subtle qualities of this being in front of us.

ETHER — Union

The communion comes to a stage where there is no 'it and I,' subject and object anymore. Just the one presence of the one being held in ether. Beyond subtlety — it cannot even be described as subtle.

"Going through the elements and these stages of concentration, we have arrived at a state where we can't even describe it as subtle because it's beyond subtlety."

• • •

Geographical Orientation Practice

C19 · December 14, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Practice for spatial rooting before entering the elemental breath. Connects to C5's geographical orientation task:

Before the elemental breath, Urs guided a spatial orientation in the landscape:

Be aware of your location. Try to orient yourself in the landscape you're set in.

  • Where is the east — where the sun rises?
  • Where is the west?
  • North?
  • South?
  • Where is the nearest mountain?
  • Where is a strong expression of the element earth?
  • Where does the nearest river flow, or where is the nearest seashore?

"We're starting where we are at, where we are seated. We're aware of our bodies, of our physical being. Our feet are on the ground, tailbone, feeling the earth."

Fana Sequence - The Complete Arc

C20 · December 14, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

For the first time, the complete fana arc has been named explicitly as a sequential practice progression across the Suluk program:

The Three Stages

1. Fana-fi-Sheikh (فناء في الشيخ)
  • Annihilation in the teacher
  • Fully introduced in C16
  • Being in the presence of the murshid and the whole Silsila
  • The murshid's qualities expressing through you
2. Fana-fi-Rasul (فناء في الرسول)
  • Annihilation in the messenger / spirit of guidance
  • Focus of this final session
  • The great beings through whom the spirit of guidance shone
  • The cosmic beings whose presence inspires us across centuries
3. Fana-fi-Allah (فناء في الله)
  • Annihilation in God
  • The ultimate station
  • The arc's final destination
  • Complete dissolution into the Divine

The Process of Initiation

"Murshid calls the moment when we are so close to this being that this being becomes an expression of ourselves — an initiation."

Each stage represents a deeper level of spiritual initiation, moving from the personal teacher, through the archetypal guides, to ultimate union with the Source.

• • •

Final Color Concentration - Orange to Gold

C20 · December 14, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The Practice

The final concentration of the entire 20-session Concentration 1 program — a ceremony of completion moving through four colors in sequence:

1. Orange

Close the eyes. Be with the color orange — in you, around you, immersed.

2. Red

Orange slowly turns to red, brighter and brighter. From orange, slowly move to red. More and more red until it is a bright red. Keep it present. Experience the redness.

3. Purple

Red to magenta, then to purple as blue enters the red. From red, slowly move to purple — from red to magenta, more and more a shade of blue within the red, until you arrive at purple.

4. Gold

Purple turns to bright gold, reflecting the light. Finally, from purple, move to the color gold. See how the purple turns into bright gold, reflecting the light. Be immersed in this color gold, below and above you, around you, within.

Completion

Now slowly let this color dissolve and let it go. Return to your breath, to your body.

The Full Color Arc

The complete spectrum across Concentration 1:

Black → White → Yellow → Red → Blue → Brown → Green → Orange → Red → Purple → Gold

This traces the full spectrum from the densest (black) to the most luminous (gold) — a chromatic journey of the soul, ending in the golden light that reflects the divine radiance.

"Be immersed in this color gold — below and above you, around you, within."

• • •

Two Modes of Concentration - Hare vs Lion

C20 · December 14, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The Teaching from the Jataka Tale

"When you imagine to be amongst these hundreds and thousands of animals and you're sure the earth is coming to an end — there's no doubt. Everyone is sure. How focused you must be to try to run for your life. This is a very energetic and strong and willful focus and concentration. But it did lack the element of relaxation in it."

"The lion in his mode was not so easily lured in this powerful mood of the multitude. We may remember this one breath that we might take before we act."

"The concentration of the lion is a very different one. It's a concentration of awareness, of relaxation. It is a very broad concentration. It is the coming together of the ability of being aware of that which is in front of you and still be aware of everything that is around you, in you, and above you."

The Two Modes Crystallized

The Hare's Concentration
  • Willful, intense, single-pointed, energetic
  • Without relaxation
  • Without context
  • Without the breath
  • Power without wisdom
  • Driven by fear and urgency
The Lion's Concentration
  • Broad, aware, relaxed
  • Holds the immediate situation AND the larger field simultaneously
  • Takes the one breath before acting
  • Acts from knowing, not from fear
  • Power WITH wisdom
  • Rooted in awareness rather than reaction

This teaching synthesizes the entire Concentration 1 program: true concentration is not forcing the mind into a narrow tunnel, but expanding awareness to hold both the particular and the universal, the immediate and the eternal, with relaxed presence.

Ashukrillah - Zikr of Gratitude

C11 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Meaning: "Thanks be to the One"

Practice Instructions

  1. Repeat "Ashukrillah" many times in slow, continuous rounds
  2. Follow with a period of dwelling in the atmosphere of thankfulness
  3. "Be in this atmosphere of thankfulness for a moment. Be aware of the things around you that support you — that you can breathe in and be aware of something, and breathe out and disperse thankfulness."
  4. "Let this thankful attitude flow out to this aspect in your life you're thankful for. It can be the simple things, simple but necessary to do the things we wish to do — even the stool we're sitting on, the lights surrounding us."

Teaching

"By lifting something up in thankfulness, it is immortalized." (Bawa)

This zikr connects to the first aspect of prayer - gratitude (shukr) - as taught by Murshid in his work on the universality of religious ideals.

Astaghfirullah Zikr Practice (33x)

C13 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The Zikr

Astaghfirullah — "I seek forgiveness from God."

Practice Instructions

  • Repeated 33 times in tone
  • Followed by a period of silent sitting in the all-compassionate presence

Context

This zikr was practiced as part of the teaching on the second aspect of prayer (repentance/Istighfar), connecting to the water element and the teaching on tears of joy, sorrow, and regret together.

"One expression of water is tears. And we have tears of joy. Sometimes we have tears of laughter. We have tears of sorrow, and we have tears of regret."

• • •

Doing Zikr as Murshid

C16 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Pir Vilayat's Instruction:

"When you do the Zikr, don't do it as you. Do it as if Murshid would do the Zikr — and you will feel another power, another energy in it." (Pir Vilayat)

Teaching Commentary:

This is the third stage of Fana-fi-Sheikh made concrete in a daily practice. Rather than performing the Zikr from one's habitual self, the murid steps into the murshid's presence first — and the Zikr is done from within that merged state. The 'another power' is not added from outside but released from within as the small self steps back.

• • •

Sallallahu 'Alaika Ya Rasul Allah Zikr

C20 · December 14, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The Zikr

Sallallahu 'alaika ya Rasul Allah

"Divine benediction be upon you, O messenger of God"

Practice: Recited 11 times in tone

Teaching

"With fana-fi-rasul, we enter the presence of the great beings. Those who have been remembered for hundreds or thousands of years. The Rasul being the spirit of guidance — those beings through whom this spirit of guidance shone forth in a way that inspires us till today. The cosmic beings through whose presence we are close to the spirit of guidance. And in their presence, all doubts and fear might vanish."

"We humans have the tendency to understand it in an exclusive way. But even though our attention might not be with all the great beings in the same way, we still acknowledge the spirit of guidance manifesting in them. They are like the rays of a sun — light of the one true being."

The Universal Vision

This zikr acknowledges the spirit of guidance as it manifests through all the great archetypal teachers:

  • Buddha, Zoroaster, Christ, Krishna
  • Moses, Mohammed, and others known and unknown
  • They are rays of one sun
  • Light of the one true being

The practice connects us to this cosmic lineage of guidance that transcends any single tradition while honoring the particular forms through which divine guidance has appeared.

Earth Practice: Eshk — Communion with Earth

C11 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The Practice

"In the days coming, just be in communion with Earth in yourself, in your being, outside. If the weather allows, go outside barefoot — to really be in contact."

"This communion of the Earth and our bodies is also described as eshk — a form of love and longing."

"Be aware of this eshk when you take your next step. Your next step might be like a kiss — your body kissing the Earth."

"We might not understand everything they are communicating, but just be there, be aware in the next few days of this wonderful communion. So concentration as a form of awareness."

Understanding Eshk

Eshk (عشق) — in Sufi usage, a consuming, longing love. Here Urs applies it not to divine-human love but to the primal bond between embodied being and the Earth that holds it.

Context: We Are Earthlings

"Earth is not just outside of us. We are made of earth. We are the very same material as the whole universe. We have very dense material in our bodies — the bones. They allow us to stand upright. Incredibly strong. It takes usually hard blows to break them. It's like stone. Even stronger are our teeth — an element of Earth."

"So when we are in connection with Earth, it's not just on the outside. Be aware of your very own making. So we are siblings. It's not just 'us and the Earth' — it's we as earthlings. It's just such a wonderful word: earthlings. Made of earth."

• • •

Four Seating Positions for Practice

C18 · December 13, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Murshid's four traditional postures for practice, with Pir Vilayat's teaching on their inner significance:

Position 1 — For Kings and Queens (Cross-legged / Sukhasana)

"It is the cross-legged seating. You see it as a very natural way of sitting — around children who are very naturally moving on the grounds. It has different benefits: one is the broader contact with the earth element. It's not just the feet and tailbone, but the knees and thighs can touch the earth as well. And it can also be a healthy way of sitting as we need to move further to sit and stand up again."

Position 2 — The Cupid (Archer's Seat)

"The Cupid — like the god Cupid with his bow. This seat is very often taken when doing Zikr. Your right foot is at the back of the knee of your left leg. The big toe and the toe next to it could actually hold the tendon right behind the kneecap — which reminds us of the string of the bow of Cupid."

Position 3 — The Position of the Sages (Full Lotus / Padmasana)

"Also known as the full lotus — where the palms of your feet look upwards. Your right foot is placed on the left thigh and the left foot is placed on the right thigh. This can be a very powerful way of sitting, but not for every body easily to sit in."

Position 4 — Kneeling

"Kneeling is very close to the full prostration. When you are kneeling, it's the last position before you bend down and put your forehead on the ground — so your heart is lifted. There is a specific way of kneeling where the heel of the right foot is standing up while the heel of the left is bent down."

Pir Vilayat on the Inner Meaning

"Pir Vilayat said: in the posture of the king or queen — the cross-legged posture — we are at the center of the universe. And in the kneeling posture, we are before the beloved."

For Chair Sitting

Feet truly touching the floor, hips level, back straight for breath to flow, rootedness through tailbone and feet.

• • •

Itisal - The Junction Practice

C20 · December 14, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Definition

Itisal (اتصال) - Junction, connection. The practice of the junction between the small and the immeasurable.

The Practice

"Let us continue in this place where the limited self meets the vast — with the practice of itisal. Itisal meaning the junction between the small and the immeasurable. And over the months to come, the next teaching sessions, you will build up this practice."

Method
  1. Intone Ha (H-A)
  2. Trace the sound from the ground to tailbone, right up to chest
  3. Be aware of how the universe is connected with us from the ground, through the tailbone, right up to the chest
  4. Practice: Intone Ha 11 times
When to Practice

"You can intone Ha as a practice in the morning right after the elemental breath — while you've already established the connection to the universe around and within you."

The Sound

Ha (ه) - The aspirated A. With this sound, we are aware of the universe, being of beings, in deep communion with our limited self.

This is an introductory teaching that will be developed further in coming sessions. The practice establishes the living connection between individual consciousness and universal consciousness through sound and awareness.

TEACHINGS & WISDOM

The Living Transmission

Urs's teachings blend the wisdom of the Inayati lineage with his own 22 years of experience on the path. His stories of personal experience (like the fire element visiting him at breakfast) make the teachings immediately alive and relatable.
