✿

Earth Element Teaching - Outer and Inner Dimensions

C11 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Earth as Outer World

"Every step you take, this Earth is carrying you in the perfect way. There is a wonderful pull of the Earth. It is strong enough that we don't fly away and it is light enough that we are not crushed. It's the most gentle way to be held every day. And still we're most of the time not aware of it."

Two Forms of Outer Earth

Earth as Mountains — majestic, ancient, slow. Qualities: steadiness, strength, calm. "Even the massive mountains are moving, but in a pace that takes millions of years."

Earth as Soil — nourishing, patient, holding. "In spring, it will be this very Earth that nourishes every plant to grow again."

"It is all-patient. It doesn't ask. It gives when it can."

Earth as Inner Reality — We Are Earthlings

"Earth is not just outside of us. We are made of earth. We are the very same material as the whole universe. We have very dense material in our bodies — the bones. They allow us to stand upright. Incredibly strong. It takes usually hard blows to break them. It's like stone. Even stronger are our teeth — an element of Earth."

"So when we are in connection with Earth, it's not just on the outside. Be aware of your very own making. So we are siblings. It's not just 'us and the Earth' — it's we as earthlings. It's just such a wonderful word: earthlings. Made of earth."

The Work with Elements

"The work with the elements is a work that has a very, very long history. Very early recordings show us that throughout the world, people have been working with the elements in many different ways."

"It has actually been one of the first practices that I've been given. And throughout the years, it has always changed. It's never been the same. This is very exciting — how a single practice can evolve with you, with your life, your biography, your experiences."

• • •

Five Aspects of Prayer - Introduction and Gratitude

C11 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Introduction to the Five Aspects

"Murshid describes these five aspects in his work on the universality of religious ideals. He speaks about these aspects as a common way for human beings of addressing something beyond."

"You have been introduced to Murshid's prayers — the prayers he has been inspired to, that have been prayed by many Murids over many, many years."

"We will look into five aspects of prayer that Murshid introduces us to — that we find in these daily moments when we find ourselves praying outside the ritual prayers. It's these moments when we might try to finish a work and we're not sure if we can make it, and there's a prayer raising in us."

The First Aspect — Gratitude (Shukr)

"The first aspect is very close to Earth and what we've been experiencing — and that is gratitude. The aspect of gratitude."

Two Modes of Gratitude

Social gratitude — saying thank you, seeing the other, acknowledging what they've given

Cosmic gratitude — thankfulness for everything dispersed into existence: the air, the Earth, the warmth, the fruit

The Practice of Gratitude

"To connect with this form of prayer means to enter a mode of cherishing everything that has been given. I experience myself and people around me very easily focusing on things we don't have, on things that bother us. And often we find little time to be aware of everything that's there."

"So this aspect of prayer is an invitation to turn our attention, our focus, our concentration on the things that deserve our gratitude."

• • •

Murshid on Earth Personality Type

C11 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

From Murshid's teaching on elemental personality types — specifically the Earth personality:

"A person of the Earth character is calm and quiet, harmonious, serviceable, simple, and good. Also dependable to a great extent." (Murshid)

"Only the person of the Earth character must be told to do something. He will not do anything by himself or by herself. And it is better if you stand by him when he's doing a certain thing and look at him while he is doing it. Then you are sure of getting it done. He's willing to do all he can, but somebody must direct him." (Murshid)

Urs's Commentary

Urs offered this contextualization:

"There is a smiling face in that."

"It's a bit of a caricature of the earthly character, and I'm sure we've met people that we would attribute very strong earthly characters to. But we need to be aware that none of us is just an earthly character or just a fiery character or a watery character."

"We all have all of these aspects in us, but it might be in different strong expressions. And sometimes one aspect might be very dominant."

Shadow and Light of Earth

"If the Earth aspect is too dominant, it could make us sluggish. But when it's in balance and can produce its very strong side, then it's the element of patience, steadfastness, being there — just being there. What a wonderful quality."

• • •

Murshid on Fault-Finding and Law of Action and Reaction

C11 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

On the Nature of Fault-Finding

"When a person finds fault with another, insults another, he does it for two reasons. One is pride — because it satisfies his pride to know, or for it to be known, that he is better than the other. The other thing is that it comes out of cruelty in nature. There is a silent cruelty in the nature of man." (Murshid)

"Satisfaction of which is in causing hurt to someone in whatever form. That person gets a kind of satisfaction out of it. There are some in the world who, by causing hurt physically, by seeing a wound, get a satisfaction. So there are others who get a satisfaction out of hurting someone's feelings. And it is not a rare thing. It is so much to be found everywhere." (Murshid)

The Law of Action and Reaction

"And it must be known that there is action and reaction. Everything that one does has a reaction. It rebounds. Love brings grace. A person — however rich, powerful, highly placed, capable, efficient, supported by many in life, by armies — can be thrown down to the depths of the earth by the smallest hurt he may have caused, which then rebounds. No protection, no support can ward off the blow of the reaction of any hurt a person causes to anybody." (Murshid)

"But one may say there are many people in the world who are quite happy in spite of all the cruelty they have inflicted. But it must be remembered that their time comes. It is nothing but a matter of time." (Murshid)

Context

This teaching was given in connection with the chivalric rule: "My conscientious self, do not reproach others, making them firm in their faults."

• • •

Body as Vessel - Not Something to Overcome

C12 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Foundational teaching from Urs addressing a common misunderstanding about the body's role in spiritual life:

"Our body is always the first and the last thing we are aware of when we are turning inside. This body is the very vessel that moves us through time and space."

"Our body is not something to overcome to be in touch with other realms. It is that which is given to us to actually host this intelligence and spirit. It is pure expression of it."

"So it's wonderful to be activated and feel this body — and at a certain age, also the limits of this body."

Core Teaching

Concentration is not an escape from the body into spirit, but a deepening into what the body already hosts and expresses.

Practice Instruction

"Every time when you sit down for your practices or stand for your prayer — first be aware of your bodily reality. Be aware of your feet, of your tailbone."

• • •

Concentration as Guardian of the Door

C12 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Teaching following the Buddhist monks story:

"Through concentration, we can build a threshold. Concentration through the mind can be like a guardian of a door that decides who is entering that door and who isn't."

"When a person is bothering you, it is in that moment. But if that person keeps on bothering us in our minds and in our memory — it can be through concentration that we let it go for that moment."

The Positive Reframe

Concentration is not passive acceptance but an active, sovereign choosing of what is held in the mind and what is released. The abbot concentrated on the act of service, fulfilled it, and set it down. The young monk concentrated on the transgression — and carried it for an hour through silence.

• • •

Life Force and Concentration - Steering Awareness

C12 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Teaching on how attention directs life force, developed through contrasting examples from ordinary life.

Outer Influence: The Company We Keep

"We might experience it with the people around us. Sometimes we are around inspiring people. They help us to change our mood. Maybe we entered a company in an unhappy mood — maybe we have our attention with our sorrows. So the sap flows to these branches that are sorrow."

"Through the company of uplifting friends, one might forget about these branches, and the other branches are filled with energy. And suddenly there is an almost contagious atmosphere and our mood changes."

The Shadow Direction

"I'm sure you've been in situations where everyone was nagging — the mood of complaining about what's happening, what's not good, what's difficult. And it's really hard to withstand it. And one gives energy towards that."

The Inner Direction of Life Force

"There might be a tendency where our life force goes to when we go through our daily life. We might find ourselves giving energy to sorrowful thoughts. And sometimes we might steer it through concentration to more uplifting aspects — like thankfulness, as we discussed before."

"Through concentration, we can actually steer where this life energy goes — what is alive and what we can let go."

Bawa's Tree Analogy - Commentary on Murshid

Bawa offered a complementary image to Murshid's bloodstream metaphor — the tree and its sap:

"Murshid compares our minds connected to the bloodstream. Bawa translated it to the picture of a tree with its branches. In a tree, you have thick branches, smaller ones, and each of them is living through the sap that is running through the tree — giving life to each and every branch, leaf, flower, and fruit. But when one of the branches is not supplied by sap, it withers. It loses its life." — Bawa

"That can be compared to how our mind works. Depending where we steer our awareness, where we steer the life — there something comes to fruition."

• • •

Mind as Bloodstream and Lines - Psychology of Mind

C12 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Central teaching from Murshid on the concentration of the mind:

"Every line which is deeply engraved on the surface of the mind may be linked to a vein where the blood runs keeping it life. And while the blood is running, it is productive of offshoots of the deep-set line. There are moments when there comes a kind of congestion in a certain line where the blood is not running. There are no offshoots. But this congestion can be broken by some outer influence." — Murshid

"And when that congested line is touched by an outer influence, which is related to that particular line, then again it sets the blood running through and offshoots arising, expressing themselves in thoughts. It is just like a waking or sleeping state of these lines." — Murshid

"As a note of music can be fully audible at one time, so one line of offshoots can be comprehensible at a time. And it is the warmth of interest that keeps the blood running in that particular line. There may be other lines where the blood is alive also. Still, if they are not kept warm by one's interest, they become congested and thus paralyzed." — Murshid

"And yet the blood is there, the life is there. It awaits a moment to awaken it. The sorrows of the past, the fears of the past, the joy of the past, can be brought to life after ages and could give the same sensation exactly as one had experienced before." — Murshid

"The more one knows the mystery of this phenomenon, the more one learns to understand that there is a world in oneself. And that in one's mind there is the source of happiness and unhappiness, the source of light and darkness. And that it can be awakened either mechanically or voluntarily, if only one knew how one must do it." — Murshid

"And then one would not blame one's misfortune, nor would one complain of one's fellow man. One could become more tolerant, more joyous, more loving. Because one knows then the cause of every thought and action, and one sees it all in the effect of a certain cause." — Murshid

"The physician would not take revenge on a patient in the asylum even if the patient hit him, for he knows where it comes from. The psychology of mind is the higher alchemy, and one cannot only study it and not practice it. It is practice and study both that must go together, and this opens the door for every soul to happiness." — Murshid

• • •

Mind as Filter · Soul as Light Source

C12 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The definitive framework for understanding the mind's role in concentration teaching:

"The mind is the filter for the light of our soul — for what we show in the world of our true being, or what's not shown yet, maybe because the filter of the mind has another focus."

Integration with Breath and Light

On the in-breath: imagine how all these imprints through your awareness — led by the mind — stand mirrored by the soul.

On the out-breath: a pure light, the pure light of your soul, shines into this world through this filter.

"The mind is like a filter through which the impressions of the physical world — our bodily, emotional experiences — are given a focus, reflected by the soul."

The Soul-Mind-Body Triad

This is the soul-mind-body triad in dynamic form:

  • The soul is the source of light
  • The mind is the filter (lens) through which that light passes
  • The world receives whatever the filter allows through

Concentration is the act of adjusting the filter — clearing, directing, refining it — so that more of the soul's light reaches the world.

• • •

Uruj and Nuzul - Two Directions of Breath

C12 · November 21, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Teaching from Murshid on the metaphysics of breath:

"Inhaling is called 'uruj,' which means rising. Exhaling is called 'nuzul,' which means descending. And each has its particular part in the life of an individual." — Murshid

"Breath is life, and its work is to take the condition from within to the external plane and to take the conditions of the external plane into one's being." — Murshid

"When one exhales, the conditions of the inner plane are brought out. Their influence first working on one's mind, then on the body, then on surroundings. When inhaling, the conditions of the external plane — harmony or inharmony — are drawn into the body, then into the mind, and then into the soul, which sets the soul either in calmness or in disturbance." — Murshid

"When exhaling, one's feelings and thoughts first work on one's body, then on surroundings. The same is the case with the physical body: it sends out gases with exhaling and inhaling takes in all the fine properties from one's surroundings." — Murshid

Practice Integration

Urs guided a few breaths with this picture held: breathing in the surrounding — from body to breath to mind to soul — and from soul outward through mind to body to surroundings.

• • •

Murshid on Conscience and Regret

C13 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

"If there is no regret, our conscience is numbed. It loses its sharpness. And with regret, our conscience becomes sharper and clearer, and it refines our moral compass." — Murshid

Urs's Commentary

"Every mistake we make is an invitation to make another step forward in our life's journey. One could even go so far as to say it's only through mistakes that we learn."

"When there is a moment of regret, we are actually pointed towards our own true moral compass. And it's like a sign that's steering us to where we're pulled."

Context

This teaching was given in connection with the second aspect of prayer (repentance/Istighfar) and the water element teaching on tears that encompass joy, sorrow, and regret together.

Murshid on Water Personality

C13 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Characteristics of Water Nature

"The person of water character is sociable, imaginative, affectionate, and lovable. Only he will respond quickly to all influences, as the sea responds to the storm. By nature, this person will always be desirable. He or she will show adaptivity, response, and fineness of character." — Murshid

"The person of the water nature is emotional, devotional, generous, but sensitive. There are moments when this person is calm and quiet, and there are moments when this person is quite upset. This person is subject to be misled and yet, if rightly guided, will prove to be most desirable. Creative, expressive, brimming with emotions." — Murshid

Reflective Questions

Urs offered this reflection to accompany Murshid's teaching:

"Where does your water personality express itself? Where is it withheld — because the water can't flow? When the water is stuck in the heart, what can become hard and insensitive. When it's washed by the water of love, it brings up tears."

Pir Vilayat on Tracing Manifestations to Pure Love

C13 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

"Even those manifestations of feelings that we would describe as hateful have their root and source in pure love. Hate is a manifestation of love — a manifestation of love that has become skewed, imbalanced, distorted. But if we track every intention back to its source, we get to something vast, something pure, something divine." — Pir Vilayat

"So the process is to discover: how did such and such a crude manifestation emerge, when what my soul wanted all along was a beautiful expression of its knowledge of the infinite? And by looking back in this way, one can balance a sense of responsibility and vigilance with compassion towards oneself and everyone involved." — Pir Vilayat

Context

This teaching was shared in connection with the practice of repentance and tracing our actions back to their divine impulse, showing how even difficult emotions and actions can be understood as distorted expressions of something originally pure.

• • •

Teaching on Repentance and Divine Impulse

C13 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

On Accountability

"Pir-o-Murshid reminds us that if we look back in our past, there are many situations where others have been unfair to us, have hurt us, overstepped. But he reminds us that the accountability in these situations lies with them. We are not accountable for their mistakes."

"But what might it mean to be accountable for the things we did, where we overstepped? Maybe not always, but there are so many moments where it feels so much easier to forgive someone else than to forgive oneself."

The Stuck Place of Regret

"Sometimes this regret is so deep that we feel ashamed. We don't dare to look in the other's eyes anymore. And if we remember the one, remember the fact that we're here for a reason — this is probably not the place we are meant to be stuck in, in this moment of regret and beating oneself up for what we did."

Tracing Back to Divine Impulse

"One aspect is to remember that nothing that happens happens outside the one. Every deed, everything we do, is based on a divine impulse. There's nothing that happens which is not based on a divine impulse."

"One step you can take when you have acknowledged that you did wrong to someone — trace your action back to this divine impulse. What of your true being was trying to show itself? It might not have succeeded the way you would wish, and it was hindered by the difficulties of our physical being. Still, the impulse was a divine one. What wanted to be shown? What was it behind?"

Practice for Working with Regret

  1. Acknowledge the situation: 'It is how it is.'
  2. When you've been fully present with it, trace it back to the divine impulse. What of your true being was trying to show itself?
  3. Are there ways to give this impulse a clearer expression in the love that it was meant to be?
  4. Bring what cannot yet be resolved before the one, the all-compassionate: 'Let it be held in his loving compassion.'
• • •

Teaching on Tears - Joy, Sorrow, and Regret Together

C13 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The Convergence of Tears

"One expression of water is tears. And we have tears of joy. Sometimes we have tears of laughter. We have tears of sorrow, and we have tears of regret."

"I find there is a very magical moment where all these aspects come together in our tears. And those are moments of ecstasy — when we are truly uplifted in a moment that encompasses every aspect of our human being and our human experience in the light of the one."

The Moment of Recognition

"Sometimes when you walk and you're just looking at some birds, but you don't see the birds — you see something beyond them. You see an expression of the one, and tears are filling your eyes. And these are tears of joy, sorrow, and regret all together. The joy of the meeting with the one in this seemingly daily situation — but there's also this sweet aspect of regret: why haven't I been there? Why have I been so much away from you?"

Elevation Through Convergence

The convergence is uplifting: when regret stands alone it is heavy. When it meets joy in the presence of the one, all aspects are elevated.

Context

This teaching was given in connection with the second aspect of prayer (repentance) and the water element, showing how tears become a bridge between the outer water element and inner spiritual states.

Water Element Teaching - Outer and Inner Dimensions

C13 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Water as Constant Flux

"With water, we are in contact with a constant flux, a constant movement. And even though we're also taking in the element of earth every day, it's more palpable with water."

Meditation on Water's Journey

"Where has all this water already been that we've been drinking today? How many rivers has this water seen? In how many oceans it has already been? How many bodies it has flown through? How many plants it has nourished? Ever and ever refreshing — again and again."

Water's Forms - Urs's Teaching from Nature

Urs, walking in snow in the Valais mountains that morning:

"I've been for a short walk today through the snow — in its crystalline form. And slowly the heat of the sun made it melt, and it built small rivers. And it was trickling down, and when I follow it in my imagination, it will end up in little streams, go down to the river, and eventually end up in one of the big lakes."

"Part of this water will be evaporated and will shift in the form of clouds. And other parts will move on to the even bigger vessels — the sea, the ocean. It comes in little streams, seen, streams unseen in the earth. And it also comes with much power, hardly possible to stop."

Increasing Subtlety

"Moving from earth to water, we see an increasing subtlety. It's already much liberated. It chooses its way more quickly, more freely."

Inner Water Element

"On the inside of our bodies, it is the predominant element. It's always hard to imagine because with our eyes open, we see a fixed set of body. But when we look inside us, we realize there is so much fluidity, so much water — always in constant movement, a movement that is necessary for us to be alive."

Movement as Life - Stagnation as Murkiness

"One aspect of water is its movement. If it doesn't move in our bodies, it has dire consequences. When water doesn't move on the street, it builds a puddle. When it stays there for a while, it gets murky and you can't see through it anymore."

"The moment it starts flowing again, it shows its revivifying and cleansing ability — the refreshing."

• • •

Repentance - Outer Expectations vs Soul's Calling

C14 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

"I'm aware that the aspect of repentance in the five aspects of prayer is not the easiest one. Many of us have had the experience that throughout our lives, other people have told us what we did right and what we did wrong. And it's sometimes not easy to find a fresh approach to this aspect in life."

"Murshid invites us to differentiate between expectations from the outer and true callings from our soul. It's not so much about moments when we might have let down others due to their expectations of us. Maybe your parents had a specific wish for what you should become, and you became something much different — but it was their expectation, and it had maybe nothing to do with your true calling."

"But when it's about the soul's journey, and when we feel that in our conscience something is touched — then it can be a guidance. And this calling for healing of regret and sorrow is something truly different."

On Retreats and Repentance:

"Many retreats start with healing practices. One reason is that regrets — especially in these moments when we enter silence — can be very powerful and very present in our minds. And healing is much necessary to let go and be free of things that hold us back."

"Just take your liberty and explore it in all freedom without putting any pressure on yourself, but with curiosity."

• • •

Stay in Conversation with Your Soul — A Gentle Invitation

C14 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Context

After sharing the Jataka Tale of "Myself is Watching" and the story of Murshid's murid who stopped drinking by realizing he was always in Murshid's presence, Urs offers a deeply compassionate counsel about how to receive these teachings.

The Teaching

"Sometimes these stories might be uplifting and sometimes they might put pressure on us because this is not how we experience our life."

"And I think as many of these teachings, they are a very true and sincere invitation to stay in conversation with our soul. Be as much in conversation with this hidden mystery, with your life's purpose, in a gentle and loving way."

"Not with the pressure of, 'Oh, I should be like these beings in these stories.' But with a loving and curious conversation with your soul."

Key Principle

The stories and teachings of the saints are not standards to measure ourselves against — they are invitations to deepen our relationship with our own soul. The approach is:

  • Gentle, not pressured
  • Loving, not judgmental
  • Curious, not demanding
  • A conversation, not a test

This teaching reflects a core principle of Urs's approach: spiritual practice is not about achieving perfection but about cultivating an intimate, compassionate dialogue with the mystery at the center of one's being.

• • •

Three Stages - Receiving, Assimilating, Representing

C14 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Teaching from Hazrat Inayat Khan

"There are three stages of action which the sincere follower of the message have to pass through, and the difficulty is that each stage has the tendency to keep back the followers from going to the next stage. The reason is that every stage has no end of interest and happiness in it."

"Another thing is that one stage is quite different from another stage, and therefore each stage is a kind of counter-reaction to the stage which was previous. Now, these stages may be called receiving the message, assimilating of the message, and representing the message."

Stage 1 — Receiving

"For a sincere murid, the first stage can be so interesting that one may think it is never enough. That endless knowledge and the heart of the seeker after truth which is never full. Fill it, and there is still a place to fill. May receive for ages, and it's yet never enough. When the receiver of the message is in that stage, then the activity of the further stages remains unaccomplished."

Stage 2 — Assimilating

"For the next stage, which is the stage of assimilation, patience is most necessary. Very few can imagine how long it takes for the spirit to assimilate knowledge of truth. One assimilates it by the power of contemplation, by pondering over the subjects that one hears, by practicing the teaching in one's life, by looking at the world from the point of view which has been told, by observing one thing in its thousand different positions — one assimilates."

"Many before assimilating the knowledge wish to reason it, wish to discuss it, wish to justify it, and see how it fits in with one's own preconceived ideas. In this way, they disturb the digestive fire of the spirit. For as the mechanism of the body is always working to help assimilate the food, so the spirit is constantly working to assimilate all that one learns through life."

"Therefore, it is a matter of patience and is taking life easily without troubling the mind too much over things, and allowing the knowledge which one has received as a food of the spirit to have time to assimilate. By trying to assimilate knowledge before the time, one loses one's normal health — just like taking a drug to help digest food, which is not beneficial in the end."

Stage 3 — Representing

"But the third process is also necessary, and those who care little for the third stage of representing miss a great deal in life. A person who has seen something beautiful, who has heard something harmonious, has tasted something delicious, who has smelled something fragrant — alone has enjoyed it and yet not completely. The complete joy is in sharing one's joy with another."

"The selfish one who enjoys oneself and does not care for others — wherever one enjoys things of the earth or things of heaven — one's enjoyment is not complete. So it is in the third stage that the following of the message is fulfilled, when a soul has heard and has pondered upon it and has passed the same blessing to others."

• • •

Two Modes of Concentration

C14 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

"As you will experience deeper and deeper in the coming months — concentration changes and shows itself in different forms. And sometimes concentration can actually be a mode of letting go. Not being set on a specific point with will, but quite the opposite: with a broadness and openness, with an open awareness."

Musical Metaphor

"Those of you that have taken up learning an instrument know that there are parts in your study when high concentration is needed — sometimes restless repetition of the same chords. But this kind of concentration wouldn't lead to music."

"So after this kind of concentration, it's the concentration of letting go — being in the music, being very close in this moment where music creates itself and you create the music, and it's not clear anymore where it's coming from."

"This staying in this space between — this is as well a form of concentration, but a different form. And both are needed for music to arise."

The Two Modes:

Mode 1 — Willful Focus: Deliberate, repetitive, technical practice. Necessary but insufficient alone.

Mode 2 — Open Presence: Letting go into the music; the threshold where self and sound merge. The fruit of Mode 1.

Both modes apply directly to Sufi practice: the deliberate work of concentration practices (Mode 1) opens into states of expanded awareness and contemplation (Mode 2). Neither replaces the other.

• • •

Urs on the Three Stages in Practice

C14 · November 22, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Two Modes of Receiving

"When you read in a moment where your mind is activated, it is processed very much by the mind — which in some stages of learning is most necessary. But when you do the same reading in a receptive state — maybe you've done some breathing exercise before, or it's in the middle of a retreat — you will experience a different reading. Because it doesn't only resonate with your mind, but with your whole being. And you might understand things that your mind didn't notice."

"When you're sitting in teaching classes like these, the mind is calmer — ideally there's a receptive openness. The mind still has its duties and protects you from being naive. But the mind also knows when it can relax and make way for a deeper truth that is within you and that is in resonance with a message given to you."

On Nodding Off in Teaching Sessions

"Don't worry if you feel tired in these teaching sessions and you might sometimes even nod off. Part of it is because this receptive state is very similar to the state the body is in when it's preparing itself for sleep. So it's not the activated state we're in when we decide to take up tasks. It's a state of resonance, and it uses a lot of concentration and focus not to nod off."

Assimilation as Living Practice

"The assimilation part is already much more active. This is when you go into your practice. This is when you make it your own. All of these teachings are alive in their very own way in the different teachers, and they are alive in their very own way in you. But that needs assimilation — living it, working with it, exploring it. That's what you do when you leave the sessions, when you go back to your lives, or when you're in your mentor groups. Make it your own. Bring it to life."

Suluk as All Three Stages

"Suluk is built up this way. It has its receiving parts, its assimilating parts, and its representing parts. As you might have realized, these are not exclusive — they always overlap, and they are never finished. We will always stay students. And it's easier to be a teacher than it is to be a student."

• • •

Fire Element Teaching - Complete

C15 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

History: The Hearth

Urs opened the Fire teaching with a meditation on how fire has accompanied humanity from the beginning:

"Fire has accompanied us as human beings all our lives — from the beginning of the first tribes. And not too long ago, people were not gathering around the light of a TV or a computer, but they were gathering around the hearth, the fire."

"When the work was done, the sun wasn't to be seen anymore. People gathered around the fire in the midst of their homes. The fire was a support for warmth, for light. It was the place where the food was processed. And maybe people looked into these flames in the evenings when the stories were told — some might have already been asleep, and others were still looking into this mystery of the fire."

Vigilance and Containment

"Fire needs to be attended, needs to be held. We need the earth element to contain the fire so it emerges its energy where it's nourishing, supportive, and brings things to light. And when we're not vigilant, fire will spread its power in a way that can be most destructive and life-threatening."

Earth and Fire in relationship: Earth is the container that gives Fire its direction and safety. Without Earth's containment, Fire becomes chaos. The elemental sequence is not just parallel — the elements are in dynamic relationship with each other.

Inner Forms of Fire

★ Three inner expressions of fire:

  1. Holy fire in purposeful work — "an upright person taking up her work with a holy fire. Without this fire, she might have stayed and watched the scene to unfold."
  1. Humor and laughter — "fire as expressed in laughter; the body heats up; laughter is a combustion of delight."
  1. Precise intellect — "a beam of fire; the focused, penetrating quality of sharp thought."

"Or it can be experienced in moments of very precise intellect. There is like a beam of fire."

Fire as Cosmic Phenomenon

★ Extended cosmic teaching on fire — three scales: planetary, solar, cellular:

The Fire Beneath Us — Earth's Core

"When we look at the communion of our fire and the fire around us — imagine the earth underneath it, the layers of magma, the core of the planet we live on that is as hot as the surface of the sun."

The Fire Above Us — Sunlight as Vision

"The sun blessing us every day with its warmth and its light — the product of this fire. Remember: when we look around us, we actually don't see the objects. We see the reflected sunlight. So in everything we see, we see the element fire."

The Fire Within Us — Digestion as Combustion

"When we eat, we digest fire that is contained by the plants that have transformed the sunlight to nutritious elements like sugar. And when we eat it and it's burned in the cells, it provides us with energy for every movement."

The fire element thus operates simultaneously at every scale: the planetary core, the stellar light, the cellular metabolism. We are fire-beings at every level of our existence — not metaphorically but physically.

Fire in Alchemy

"The alchemists know that fire is an important servant for transformation, and she knows the amount of fire that is used to transform one thing into another without burning it."

"And it's the same when we're preparing a meal — the alchemist of the kitchen. This ability to befriend this fire and create something wonderful that nurtures."

The alchemist of the kitchen is a beautiful grounding image: every cook is working with fire daily, calibrating heat, knowing when to increase and when to withdraw, transforming raw matter into something nourishing. Alchemy and cooking are the same art at different scales.

• • •

Fire as Eshk - Love as Consuming Flame

C15 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Arabic Saying on Love as Flame

★ Full text recovered from transcript:

"Love is a flame. When it befalls the heart, nothing but the face of the beloved remains. Love is a flame. When it befalls the heart, nothing but the face of the beloved remains. It burns up all but the face of the beloved." — Arabic saying

The saying was offered twice — once as a single pass, once as a deliberate repetition to let it settle.

The Moth and the Flame

"So in dhikr, in remembrance, there is this fire element that's burning up everything except the one. It's like the moth approaching the flame — becoming the flame."

This is one of the most ancient images in Sufi poetry — the moth (parvaneh) drawn irresistibly to the candle, its annihilation in the flame being the very consummation of its love. In Rumi, Attar, and Hafiz, the image marks fana — the dissolving of the self in the divine. Here Urs connects it directly to dhikr practice: the repetition of divine names as a controlled fire that burns away everything except the one being named.

Connection to Eshk

"I spoke of the transformative power of fire, and this is also an aspect of the eshk, of the transformative love."

Eshk (عشق), first introduced in C11 as the longing-love of the Earth communion, here expands into the consuming fire of divine love — the eshk that does not hold but burns, does not possess but transforms. The same Arabic word carries both the gentle longing of the Earth breath and the consuming passion of fire.

• • •

Murshid on the Fire Personality

C15 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

"The person of fire nature is useful but dangerous. You do not know what he will do from one moment to another. This character is just like a cracker, a firecracker. The silent cracker only needs the touch of a lighted match, and at once will declare that it is a cracker." (Murshid)

"A fire person cannot hide her character. It takes but a moment to bring it out. A least a little excuse will bring him up in a moment. This person is destructive by nature, and the trouble he causes to all others is much less than the harm he does to himself. Her life is as destructive as fire — fire which burns all things and burns itself at the same time." (Murshid)

Urs's Reframe

Urs offered a careful reframe, consistent with the approach to Earth and Water personalities:

"Murshid touches on the destructive side of fire in people. But again, if we trace it back to the divine origin, it is an expression of the eshk, of the love."

• • •

When the Elements Come to Visit

C15 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Urs's Personal Experience

During the fire element teaching, Urs shares a personal story of how the fire element "visited" him that very morning:

"I had the good fortune today to be visited by this fire. I, by accident opened a message from my work, and immediately I could feel the fire rising in me. Fire that makes you alert, makes your mind very present, but also sets the stage to be destructive, to be in this fire as a form of anger."

"And when it happened, I wasn't so thankful yet, but I could really feel how my body was heated up, and that was so amazing that simple words can spark the fire in you."

The Teaching

"Maybe you have experienced similar things during these days that when we immerse in one of these elements, they come to visit. And when they visit, I hope we can acknowledge it and be with it and when we've settled again, be with this atmosphere of this element."

Key Insight

When we practice with the elements — earth, water, fire, air, ether — we develop a sensitivity to their presence. The elements then begin to "come to visit" us in daily life:

  • Earth may visit as a feeling of heaviness, groundedness, or stubbornness
  • Water may visit as tears, flowing emotions, or adaptability
  • Fire may visit as anger, passion, alertness, or transformation
  • Air may visit as lightness, freedom, or scattered thoughts
  • Ether may visit as spaciousness or transcendence

The practice is not to resist or suppress these visitations, but to acknowledge them, be with them, and when settled, remain in the atmosphere of that element. This transforms everyday emotional experiences into opportunities for elemental awareness.

• • •

Be Mindful of the Transit — Returning to Daily Life

C16 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The Teaching

At the close of Weekend 3 (the first Urs Qutbuddin weekend), Urs offers this counsel on the transition from retreat back to everyday life:

"We have come to the end of this session. And for some there lies a night ahead, for others the day, but soon you will move out of these three days, and I would like you to be mindful of this transit."

"When you adapt the rhythms again of your daily lives, and go back to all those who have given you this time, be mindful of them as well."

"And I wish you a wonderful time with your practice. Be gentle, but focused, and explore with joy. Take everything like nectar that's given to you, everything you find."

Key Principles for the Transition

  1. Be mindful of the transit — The shift from sacred retreat to daily life is itself a practice. Don't rush through it unconsciously.
  2. Acknowledge those who gave you this time — Family, friends, colleagues who held space for your absence deserve mindful gratitude.
  3. Be gentle but focused — The balance between softness and intention carries the retreat energy forward.
  4. Explore with joy — Practice is not grim duty but joyful exploration.
  5. Take everything like nectar — Every experience, whether from practice or from life, can be received as nourishment.
• • •

Concentration and Contact with the Murshid

C16 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

"By concentration, by single-mindedness, by sympathy, one can establish a contact with their murshid in which distance would make no difference. And it is for that reason that to some capable of concentration, concentrations are given to contact the murshid in their thought. The qualities of the teacher manifest after that in the murid." (Murshid)

"And as the murid goes onward, the murid feels in himself or herself the heritage of the teacher — as if one had inherited from the teacher the power and inspiration which would help one in the path of truth." (Murshid)

"Many ask: can one not take the direct road to God without the help of a teacher? I say, there is nothing impossible. A ladder is only a means to go from the ground floor to the upper floor, but if one can climb without a ladder, it is not impossible. As the ladder is a convenience, so the teacher takes the same place in the spiritual path." (Murshid)

"It is therefore that in the East, great importance has been given to the guidance under the teacher. And that guidance is considered so sacred — as sacred as one could consider one's own faith. Because faith in the form of religion is a conception, but when the faith is given in the form of allegiance to a murshid, that is living faith." (Murshid)

"Therefore in the East, it becomes easy for a murid, since those who come under the murshid's guidance know beforehand what a murshid means. They do not need anymore for their objects of concentration the idols of the temple. Once they have come to the murshid, they have found the living example which they wish to follow." (Murshid)

Context:

These teachings from Hazrat Inayat Khan form the foundation for understanding the practice of Fana-fi-Sheikh and the metaphysical basis of the murshid-murid relationship across distance.

• • •

Four Planes of Magnetism

C16 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Each plane represents a distinct form of drawing power that can be perceived and cultivated:

Magnetism of the Body

"When someone takes good care of his physique, does a lot of sports, is in good shape — he or she can build a physical magnetism."

Magnetism of the Mind

"When someone has really put herself, himself to the deep study of a certain matter — when she is most knowledgeable and can quickly combine most complex matters — this can produce a magnetism of the mind."

Magnetism of the Heart

"When you meet someone whose heart is so open, so responsive — you realize you're seen, your current state is felt, there is a deep resonance and the heart is open. This is a magnetism of the heart."

Magnetism of the Soul

"It might be encountered in someone who seems simple, almost naive, but there is something in her glance, in his glance that calls you right away to your source — beyond everything. Immediately your soul is touched by this magnetism of this being."

Reflective Teaching

"These are all wonderful magnetisms, and we all have them in us. Maybe we put our concentration on some more than on others. But when we focus on one aspect of our being, we build up its magnetism. It doesn't need to be exclusive — if one is built, the other doesn't crumble."

"If you explore yourself: where did you put your focus in your life so far? What magnetism did you build? And is there another part inviting your attention?"

"Where was your focus so far? And where shall it be?"

Practice in Daily Life

"When you go about your lives and you realize suddenly a magnetism of another being is catching you — be curious. What was it? What element of magnetism was it?"

• • •

Inter Esse - Being in the Middle of It

C16 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Etymological Teaching:

"By means of concentration and sympathy — and there's also the aspect of interest — inter esse: to be in the middle of it, so immersed that you become the thing that you're interested in."

Definition:

Inter esse (Latin) — literally 'to be between' or 'to be in the midst of.' The word 'interest' comes from this root.

Teaching Point:

Genuine interest is not a casual preference but a state of immersion — the self entering so fully into the object of attention that the boundary dissolves. Baba Farid's interest in his cow was so total that he literally became it.

Connection to Practice:

This teaching connects directly to the three stages of Fana-fi-Sheikh: each stage is a deepening of inter esse — from looking at the murshid, to being surrounded by the murshid's atmosphere, to being in the midst of the murshid so thoroughly that his qualities express through you.

• • •

Pir Vilayat on Zikr as Murshid

C16 · November 23, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

"When you do the Zikr, don't do it as you. Do it as if Murshid would do the Zikr — and you will feel another power, another energy in it." (Pir Vilayat)

Teaching Context:

This instruction represents the third stage of Fana-fi-Sheikh applied to daily practice. Instead of performing Zikr from one's ordinary consciousness, the practitioner first enters the merged state with the murshid's presence, allowing the Zikr to emerge from that unified awareness. The "another power" is not external addition but the natural result of the ego stepping aside.

• • •

Four Aspects of Prayer Mapped to Four Elements

C17 · December 13, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Urs provided the complete mapping of all four aspects of prayer to the four elements — the first time this full correspondence has been explicitly stated:

EARTH ↔ Gratitude (Shukr)

The first and most grounded prayer; cherishing what is given; earth's gift of carrying

WATER ↔ Forgiveness / Healing (Istighfar / Tawba)

The cleansing quality of water; the tear; repentance as a waterfall washing through the heart

FIRE ↔ Supplication / Haiya

The prayer of the driven wish; the fire of longing for specific aims and support

AIR ↔ Invocation

The subtlest of the four; the longing to be close to the one; reaching out like air in all directions

"We had gratitude with the element earth, forgiveness and healing with water, supplication and the wish for one's aims with fire — and with air, we are with invocation."

This mapping shows how the elemental breath practice corresponds to the complete spectrum of prayer, from the most grounded (gratitude) to the most subtle (invocation).

• • •

Music as Munajat and Teaching

C17 · December 13, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Music at the Core of Teaching

Urs explicitly framed the session music as integral to the teaching itself:

"Thank you especially Hamad for your wonderful musical inspiration. It's a real blessing that we have with us all these wonderful musicians. I just would like to point out that the music which might seem like an introduction to the teaching is actually very much at the core of the teaching itself."

"While continuing going through the elements and the aspects of prayer, and especially this weekend with the stories of Murshid's life, we might get back to this wonderful aspect of music as a form of teaching."

Music as Munajat

"This subtlety of longing to be close to the one often reaches us through music — which is also very close to the air element, as it is transported through this element to our ears."

"In the Gayan Vadan Nirtan, there are ragas that contain something called munajat — it's the calling of the beloved, of the lover, in the middle of the night or in the wilderness, when the lover is calling out for the beloved."

The Connection to Air Element

Music's connection to the air element and invocation creates a natural bridge between the elemental breath practice and the devotional poetry of Murshid. The subtle quality of air corresponds to the subtlety of invocation, both carried through the medium of sound and breath.

• • •

Teaching on Invocation and the God-Ideal as North Star

C17 · December 13, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

The Quality of Invocation

"Like air, invocation can be seen as a little bit subtler than the other aspects. Invocation is the reaching out for the beloved — the asking, the longing, the singing for the closeness of the one."

"While in Haiya we are asking for support so that our deepest wishes might be fulfilled, in invocation there is only the wish to be with the one. It's the expression of those sacred moments when the greatest boon is to be in the presence of the one."

"As the saying goes: when you take one step towards the one, he will make a thousand steps towards you."

The God-Ideal as North Star

"This longing is the longing for the God-ideal — which is not the one, but it's like a rung in the ladder, a step which leads us in the direction of the one. It's like the north star. It's our picture of perfection — one that we hold now, and that we let go when this rung of the ladder has helped us to rise further."

"It is like in the Zikr when we say: there is no God but God. We let go of an ideal knowing it's not the one itself — but the north star that leads us."

What God Looks For — Burning

The core teaching from the story of Moses and the shepherd:

"I don't look at the words. I look at what is in the heart. I want to see burning. Burning is what I hear."

This reveals that the divine response is not to the form of prayer but to the sincerity and intensity of longing in the heart.

• • •

Air Element Character Traits and Balancing

C18 · December 13, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Air Element Qualities

"With air, it's a freedom of thought, being inspired, epiphanies, visionary ideas, and free movement from one thought to the next. There is a liberty and creativity in this."

"And sometimes we experience that it's easy to have a thought, but sometimes not as simple to put these thoughts into practice. So the air element is not so strong in realizing what it creates in the thought. For that, it needs a good balance with the other elements."

The Elements in Combination

When a thought is formed, it needs all four elements to manifest:

  • Air: The idea itself
  • Fire: The passion and will that moves it into existence. Otherwise it will just stay a wonderful idea
  • Water: Takes shape, the down-pouring element that gives form
  • Earth: Holds this water and gives it clear, concrete direction

"We have been given the gift of all these elements, and sometimes we see one element being predominant in another being, in a friend, and in ourselves. Eventually it's the balancing of the elements that helps each element bring forth its true magnitude, its capability."

The elemental interplay for bringing a vision into reality: Air (the idea) → Fire (the will and passion) → Water (takes form and flows) → Earth (grounds it, gives it concrete direction). All four are necessary; none is complete without the others.

• • •

Murshid on Concentration and Self-Consciousness

C18 · December 13, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

"Real concentration is the forming of the concrete picture of the object of concentration in the mind. Lack of concentration comes from the wavering nature of the mind, and the mind wavers by lack of proper exercise. As the body develops with physical exercise, so the mind develops by concentration." (Murshid)

"The great hindrance that stands against concentration is the thought of one's own being. When one thinks of one's own presence, and at the same time thinks 'I am concentrating on a certain object,' at that time it is impossible to have full concentration. The more one loses the thought of one's own being from one's consciousness, the more one becomes capable of concentration." (Murshid)

"As self-consciousness is the enemy of a speaker, singer, doctor, or lawyer, so it is the great enemy of the one who concentrates. Concentration is to avoid self-consciousness. And at the same time, self-consciousness is the only thing that keeps one from progress. The Sufi, while concentrating, uses abstinence against the constant and uncontrollable activity of the mind." (Murshid)

Urs's Commentary

"As we've already experienced, concentration has different modes or steps. And while in the beginning, concentration seems to be with a focused will, there is another concentration where we are just immersed in the object that we are looking at — so immersed that there is no object and no subject anymore. There's just pure awareness."

• • •

Murshid on the Air Personality

C18 · December 13, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

"The person of air character is moody and imaginative and visionary. At one moment he is your great friend, at the other moment he is your enemy. As the air at the moment before was blowing to the east, and the moment after went towards the west — this person will have material fits and spiritual fits, and spells of virtue and obsession by evil." (Murshid)

"This person will change from time to time. When you think today he is good, tomorrow he will show himself different. When you see this morning he was calm, in the evening you will find him upset. It is the greatest difficulty to keep that person in control. It is like controlling the air, which is always difficult." (Murshid)

"Yes, this person will show wit, quickness in grasping things, capability, efficiency in work. She will act on impulse, she will be adventurous, and if powerful, will be influential in life." (Murshid)

Urs's Commentary

"I wouldn't take it as an invitation to put people into boxes of the different elements, but maybe it can be like a lens through which we sometimes perceive what is in and around us. And when we sometimes realize that a situation contains a lot of fire that has no container — the fire without the container will spread — then the earth element might be helpful to balance the situation."

• • •

Gayan Vadan Nirtan as Companion

C19 · December 14, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

Gayan Vadan Nirtan described as a companion to be opened, not read:

"As Murshid does in his writings of the Gayan Vadan Nirtan — a collection of his pearls of wisdom. It's not a book which you read from the beginning to the end. It's rather a steady companion which you open and see what awaits you. Gayan meaning singing, Vadan playing music, and Nirtan dancing."

"Murshid describes the yearning for the one, the seeking for the friend — writes about longing and absence, separation and remembrance, the pursuit, the trace, the fragrance of the one. The disappearance of the self into the infinitude of the one being — describes the loss of the self and the emergence of the true self."

• • •

Murshid on the Ether Personality

C19 · December 14, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

"The character of the ether person shows all the above-set qualities — the qualities of all the elements — and yet every quality in a subdued form. This person will be serious, calm, quiet, peaceful, subject to sadness and melancholy at times, yet responding to humor and mirth, rhythmic in action, balanced in life, deep in understanding, brave bearing at the same time, thoughtful and considerate." (Murshid)

"Ether is the essence of all the elements, and a person that shows ether in one's character shows wisdom. Where there is wisdom, there is beauty. Wisdom is adorned by beauty. This person will have the power of attraction and expression, together with magnetism expressed through one's whole personality." (Murshid)

• • •

Bawa - Concentration Is a Sign of Love

C20 · December 14, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

"Concentration is a sign of love." — Bawa

Urs's Teaching

"We've experienced it in a moment when you see a friend. And when this friend is really there — and you feel that he or she is not preoccupied with a thousand other things, but is there in this moment with you — you're seen. How precious is this? This is also a form of concentration, and with it, an expression of sincere feeling and love."

The Final Synthesis

This is the final teaching of Concentration 1: the practice returns to where it began — to presence, to being truly with another, to the act of seeing and being seen.

All the techniques have been in service of this:

  • The dot
  • The colors
  • The elemental breath
  • Fana-fi-sheikh
  • The star
  • All visualization practices

They have all been developing the capacity to be fully present with what is in front of you, and to offer the gift of that presence to another.

The Circle Complete

Concentration is not ultimately about mental control or psychic powers. It is about love — the ability to give someone or something your complete, undivided attention. To be so present that the other feels truly seen, truly met, truly received.

This is perhaps the most profound spiritual accomplishment: to love so purely that your very attention becomes a blessing.

• • •

Murshid on Fana-fi-Rasul - The Self-Made Ideal

C20 · December 14, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

"There is an initiation the seeker gets from one's ideal. And who is this ideal? No living creature on earth, however great, can prove to be the ideal of anyone else. He or she may for a certain time, but not forever." — Murshid
"The great ones like Buddha, Zoroaster, Christ, and Krishna, who have been the ideal of humanity for thousands of years — during their lifetime, they gave a sense of being the ideal. They left impressions which afterwards proved them to be the ideal. But during their lifetime, they could not prove it. Why? Because even the perfect human being is limited in the imperfect garb of humanity. Human limitation covers perfection." — Murshid
"However great, however deep, however spiritual a person is — that person remains limited. One cannot make oneself as one's pupil imagines one. Imagination goes further than the progress of the human being. Imagination is every person his own." — Murshid
"And therefore, one can only make one's ideal oneself. No one has the power to make the ideal of another person. It is the impressions of the great saviors of humanity, it is their goodness — whatever little grain of an ideal they have left behind — that becomes just like a seed. And that seed put into the soil of the devotee's heart develops into a plant that can bear fruits and flowers as it's reared." — Murshid
"So in this initiation, there is the ideal of the human imagination. One may call it Christ, or Buddha, or Mohammed, or Moses, or Zoroaster. It is one's ideal. It is one who has made it. It is one's savior. Certainly it will save one, if one considers it to be one's savior." — Murshid
"One has to make it. If one does not make it, the savior will not save one. Once one has made one's savior, then one is face to face with that perfection which one's heart has created. Then this impression flowers and grows into a tree and bears flowers and fruit which one has desired. Once this initiation is received, one begins to radiate one's initiator who is within one as one's ideal." — Murshid

Urs's Commentary

"We are fortunate that many of what Murshid says here are encompassed in the prayer Saum. So practicing Saum will give us the opportunity to go deeper and deeper into this wisdom that Murshid is bringing forth."

This dense and rich passage was recommended for repeated study and contemplation. It reveals the profound psychology of spiritual idealization and the creative power of the devotee's imagination in manifesting their own salvation through communion with the great archetypal guides.

• • •

Murshid on Single-Mindedness

C20 · December 14, 2025 · Urs Qutbuddin

"Single-mindedness as a nature becomes a great help to concentration. People with a great many responsibilities and a great many interests in life cannot keep up single-mindedness, which indeed is a great power. This nature can be developed by concentration." — Murshid
"It is at first essential for one who practices concentration to allow one thought at a time or one action at a time, and to keep mind and body busy together. When a person does something, one should not be thinking of another thing while doing it. And if one wishes to think out something, one must not be doing something at the same time." — Murshid
"Single-mindedness is a complete absorption of one's whole being in a single thought, speech, or action. Also, single-mindedness can be developed by dwelling on a subject until the thought is finished — and while thinking on the subject, not allowing the mind to take up another subject. The same law should be observed in speech and in action." — Murshid
"In this way, one can develop concentration at every moment of the day and night. And by acquiring this one, acquires mastery over one's life as well as over life in general." — Murshid

Urs's Practical Guidance

"Maybe you feel invited to just be aware of this invitation from time to time and develop a habit. Maybe you already have that one time a day where you pour a cup of tea. Then for a moment — just be with drinking this cup of tea. Even if it's a minute where you restrain yourself from scrolling through your mobile. Just for this moment, be with you drinking that tea. And what first might sound like a challenge might be a moment of relaxation, where not everything has to be at once, but only this."

The Practice

  • One thought at a time OR one action at a time
  • Keep mind and body busy together
  • Complete absorption of whole being in single focus
  • Develop through simple daily moments like drinking tea
  • A moment of relaxation rather than strain
