Fazl Mullah Rahim Allah — Blessing Invocation
Sung or recited invocation: Fazl (blessing) + Mullah (great) + Rahim Allah (Allah's compassion); use in worldly/noisy situations.
Part III, Chapter 4 · Guide Mansur
Saum Prayer — Movement Instructions
Nine-movement sequence for Saum: palms forward, hands converge, bend forward, rise, lean with palms to ground, open Qalb, final surrender.
Part I, Chapter 5 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Breath Practices
Rightful Breathing Practice
Upright seated breath: enter without forcing, do not rush exhale, let muscles yield to maximize refreshment.
Part I, Chapter 3 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
The Invisible Rain — Full Body Breath
Visualize subtle rain entering every pore; breath cascades from crown to toes quenching each cell; exhalation as communion with plant life.
Parts I · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Purification Breathing — Emotional Stages
Watch murkiness on the out-breath dissolving like squeezing a dirty sponge; stages: murkiness → less murkiness → clear channel → radiance.
Part I, Chapter 3 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Elemental Purification Ritual
Identify the element of a burden (earth/water/fire/air), take it to nature, release it through burial, pouring, burning, or wind; post-ritual prayer.
Part I, Chapter 3 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Five Aspects of Breath — Review
Pir Zia's five-aspect model: exhalation, depth/breadth, belly-centering, rhythm, and scope (physical breath → soul breathing).
Part I, Chapter 3 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Breath Visualization Through Soles of Feet
Lie on the ground; inhale through soles as a wave, let it fill the whole body; exhale back out through the feet into earth (10 minutes).
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Light & Breath Practice — The Orb / Auric Body
Visualize breath as a sphere of light that expands on exhale and congeals on inhale; reveals the auric/etheric body.
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
The Swing of Breath — Ha × 11
Feel the breath as a pendulum swing between inner and outer; intone Ha eleven times connecting little body to great body of the universe.
Part I, Chapter 5 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Five Element Breathing — Foundation
Core elemental breath cycle: Earth (nose-nose), Water (nose-mouth), Fire (mouth-nose), Air (mouth-mouth), Ether (subtle both); each 5 breaths.
Part II, Chapter 3 · Urs Qutbuddin
Water Elemental Breath
Inhale nose, exhale mouth; visualize waterfall of water and light from above washing through the body; color green; direction downward.
Part II, Chapter 3 · Urs Qutbuddin
Three Element Breath Sequence
Earth + Water + Fire practiced in one sitting with full layer sets (direction, color, quality, healing aspect) for the first time.
Part II, Chapter 3 · Urs Qutbuddin
Complete Five-Element Breath with Ether
First time all five elements practiced in sequence; Ether = quintessence, no direction, no color, three planes (body/mind/spirit).
Part II, Chapter 3 · Urs Qutbuddin
Hosh dar Dam — Breath Awareness
Life-practice: make the breath your home base throughout the day; go there whenever thinking has no meaningful occupation.
Part III, Chapter 2 · Guide Mansur
Qasab — The Reed Breath (Alternate Nostril)
9-step alternating nostril sequence; at retention: close nostrils, expand chest, curl tongue, turn eyes up, hold 2× inhale count, think HU.
Part III, Chapter 2 · Guide Mansur
Five Elemental Purification Breaths (Mansur Version)
Complete elemental sequence with Mansur's specific visualizations, directions, colors, and qualities; 7 rounds per element (max 10).
Part III, Chapter 2 · Guide Mansur
Breath Still-Point Concentration
At end of exhale, hold briefly and savor the still-point; feel the body's magnetism draw the in-breath without will — Murshid's cobra metaphor.
Part II, Chapter 4 · Urs Qutbuddin
Ablutions — Ritual Purification
7-step washing sequence (hands, mouth, nostrils, face, arms, hair/neck, feet), 3 times each; body as five-pointed star; practiced upon waking.
Part I, Chapter 5 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Elemental Practices
Earth Element Extended Practice — Three Layers
Layer 1: purification/grounding (let go on exhale, draw magnetism on inhale); Layer 2: horizontal direction; Layer 3: yellow/ocher color.
Part II, Chapter 3 · Urs Qutbuddin
Earth Practice: Eshk — Communion with Earth
Go barefoot; each step is a kiss; be aware of eshk (longing-love) between body and earth; we are earthlings — made of the same material.
Part II, Chapter 6 · Urs Qutbuddin
Concentration & Visualization
Color Black Concentration
Fill the mind completely with black — ebony, obsidian; no black things, just blackness; first in the alchemical sequence.
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Color White Concentration
Replace or amplify white from behind closed eyelids; two approaches (replace or amplify); self-observation of returning attention.
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Color Yellow Concentration — Alchemical
Third in black→white→yellow alchemical sequence (Khem); become saturated by yellow like cloth in dye; symbolizes illumination.
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Color Red Concentration
See redness as living atmosphere, not a thing; two phases: hold redness, then let fade and notice resonance; extend throughout day.
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Color Blue Concentration
Let blue fill and saturate; be dyed blue in every fiber; Murshid's nature meditations on blue (heaven, purity, uplifting).
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Color Concentration: Brown to Green
Slow intentional color shift from earth-brown to life-green; bridges Earth and Water elements; bridging density to flow.
Part II, Chapter 4 · Urs Qutbuddin
Final Color Concentration — Orange to Gold
Ceremonial four-color closing sequence of Concentration 1: orange → red → purple → gold; immersed in golden light.
Part II, Chapter 4 · Urs Qutbuddin
Gemstone Concentration
Visualize a translucent crystalline gemstone; see facets, glow, revolve it; avoid associations; rest in resonance afterward.
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Sandpaper Touch Concentration
Close eyes; give whole attention to fingertips on sandpaper; feel every grain; stop; notice state. 'That which your heart meets is introduced into eternity.'
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Flower Concentration Practice
Jamali concentration object: Jalali phase (active observation of petals/stamen/color) followed by Jamali phase (easeful gentle embrace).
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Gazing & Visualization — Crescent Moon + Star
Two phases: open-eyed fixed gaze on wall point; inner visualization of both crescent moon and star held together; crystallizes retreat arc.
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Green Dot Practice
Stand and gaze at a green dot on the wall without rigidity for one minute; point reduces each session; eventually no dot needed.
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Visualization — Calling a Loved One
Let a beloved person's name resound in the mind; allow face/form to emerge from the name; let it dissolve back; rest with residue.
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Tailbone Concentration Practice
Shift whole awareness to the tailbone; notice sensations (warmth, movement, stillness); breathe into and out of the tailbone; check resonance.
Part II, Chapter 4 · Urs Qutbuddin
Three-Stage Being Visualization
Stage 1: known person; Stage 2: known-of person (saint/teacher); Stage 3: non-physical being (angel/jinn/Bodhisattva); concentration→contemplation arc.
Part II, Chapter 4 · Urs Qutbuddin
Burning Torch Concentration
Visualize a burning torch: see colors, movement, dancing flames; fire given direction = illumination; when wandering, return to image.
Part II, Chapter 4 · Urs Qutbuddin
Skull Light Concentration — The Luminous Glance
Feel skull expanding; light enters through forehead on inhale; cast beam outward on exhale; open eyes with beams shedding light on the room.
Part II, Chapter 4 · Urs Qutbuddin
Star, Crescent Moon, and Heart Visualization
Build the three Inayatiyya symbol forms in sequence: five-pointed star → crescent moon below → heart surrounding both; then dissolve in reverse.
Part II, Chapter 4 · Urs Qutbuddin
River Visualization Practice
Sit in Astaghfirullah atmosphere; imagine a river — its color, animals, plants, sound, reflected light; stay with the flow; notice body resonance afterward.
Part II, Chapter 4 · Urs Qutbuddin
Fikr, Zikr & Wazifa
Ashukrillah — Zikr of Gratitude
Repeat 'Ashukrillah' (Thanks be to the One) many times; dwell in thankfulness atmosphere; let it flow to what you are grateful for.
Part II, Chapter 5 · Urs Qutbuddin
Astaghfirullah Zikr — 33x
Repeat 'Astaghfirullah' (I seek forgiveness from God) 33 times in tone; sit in silent all-compassionate presence; connects to water element / tears.
Part II, Chapter 5 · Urs Qutbuddin
Doing Zikr as Murshid
Pir Vilayat's instruction: don't do Zikr as yourself — do it as if Murshid does it; 'another power' is released from within.
Part II, Chapter 5 · Urs Qutbuddin
Sallallahu 'Alaika Ya Rasul Allah Zikr
Recite 11 times in tone: 'Divine benediction be upon you, O messenger of God'; enters presence of the Rasul through Fana-fi-Rasul.
Part II, Chapter 5 · Urs Qutbuddin
Fikr — Ya Sabur-o / Ya Wahhab-o
First/foundation fikr: inhale Sabur (patient meeting of life), exhale Wahhab (freely abundant flow of blessings); 11 or 33 times daily.
Part III, Chapter 4 · Guide Mansur
Fikr — Subuhun / Quddusun
Preparatory fikr before advanced practice: inhale Subuhun (Glorified One), exhale Quddusun (Holy One); purification of consciousness; 33x.
Part III, Chapter 4 · Guide Mansur
Fikr — Ya Fazl / Ya Fattah
Current leading practice: inhale Fazl (blessing/illumination), exhale Fattah (opener/revealer of paths); when thinking stops, fikr continues on its own.
Part III, Chapter 4 · Guide Mansur
Ayat al-Qutb — Advanced Fikr
Advanced fikr practice; preceded by Subuhun-Quddusun as preparatory; reference Gatha II Pasi Anfas.
Part III, Chapter 4 · Guide Mansur
Body Awareness
Energy Ball Practice
Massage arms; breathe on palms; raise hands palm-facing; play with distance to feel the energy ball between them; awareness of etheric field.
Part II, Chapter 4 · Urs Qutbuddin
Other Practices
The Amen Gesture — Physical Cascade
After prayers: gather accumulated resonance in cupped hands, lift overhead, pour down over face-neck-shoulders-chest.
Part I, Chapter 1 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Sleep & Waking — Nostril Practice
Sleep on right side (lunar nostril); before waking shift to left side to activate solar nostril; step out of bed right foot first; say Invocation first.
Part I, Chapter 5 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Jalali — The Star Practice
Visualize a single blazing star; face its fierce Jalali radiance; breathe in starlight; dissolve into the star; rest in afterglow.
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Jamali — The Crescent Moon Practice
Visualize crescent moon with cool silver light; embody its receptive, reflective quality; become lunar; release opinions.
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Cardamom Tasting Practice
Place cardamom on tongue; bite once; give whole attention to taste — no taster, no tasted, only the tasting; cultivate interest + indifference.
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Rose Essence Smell Practice
Lift rose-essence paper to nostrils; lose yourself in fragrance until there is only the fragrance making itself known; location remains accessible.
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Journey Through the Mind: Three Faculties
Sequential guided exploration of Sensation (Nasut), Memory (Malakut), and Imagination (Malakut); think of an unmet person, form their presence, dissolve.
Part I, Chapter 4 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Visualizing an Inspiring Being
Imagine an inspiring person in front of you; hold their presence and atmosphere; transition from outer objects to inner beings in concentration.
Part II, Chapter 4 · Urs Qutbuddin
Three Contemplation Practices
Hold three intangibles in sequence: (1) a character trait, (2) a driving motivation, (3) a spiritual aspiration; explore resonance without analysis.
Part II, Chapter 4 · Urs Qutbuddin
Fana-fi-Sheikh — Three Stages
Stage 1: build image of Murshid, glance meets glance, Silsila present; Stage 2: release image, hold pure atmosphere in heart; Stage 3: Murshid's qualities express through you.
Part II, Chapter 4 · Urs Qutbuddin
Sky of Mind — Five-Stage Practice
Stage 1: witness thoughts as clouds; Stage 2: dense dark clouds; Stage 3: remember soul as inner sun; Stage 4: luminous ice-crystal clouds; Stage 5: radiate through open eyes.
Part III, Chapter 3 · Guide Mansur
Muraqabah — Watchfulness of Thought
When negative thought arises: pause, ask where it comes from, release, then REJOICE — the noticing is itself waking up.
Part III, Chapter 3 · Guide Mansur
Ideal Guru Contemplation
Hold archetype of the Ideal Guru (Pir Zia, inspiring yogi); absorption into the quality of presence — 'it can be caught, not just taught.'
Part III, Chapter 3 · Guide Mansur
Subuhun Quddusun Rabbanu — Evening Practice
Recite 33 times before sleep; Subuhun (utterly pure), Quddusun (Holy One), Rabbana (our Lord); takes energy into sleep — 'winding the clock.'
Part III, Chapter 4 · Guide Mansur
Daily Task — Stepping Through Doors (Right Foot First)
Step through every threshold right foot first; cultivates concentrated, mindful awareness in everyday movement; practice for one day.
Part I, Chapter 5 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Daily Task — Avoid the Word 'I'
Abstain from using the word 'I' for 24 hours; substitute 'we', 'one', or avoid self-reference; ego-observation practice.
Part I, Chapter 5 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Geographical Orientation — Daily Task
Determine and maintain awareness of north/south/east/west plus nearest sea, mountains, and river throughout 24 hours without technology.
Parts I / II · Pir Zia Inayat Khan / Urs Qutbuddin
Think of God After Every Statement
After everything you say, pause and remember God for just a moment — transforms ordinary conversation into continuous remembrance.
Part I, Chapter 5 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Walking Practice — Two-Year Prescription
Walk daily; feel gravity holding you, feel every footstep's contact with earth; 'Let your soul be where your soles are.'
Part I, Chapter 5 · Pir Zia Inayat Khan
Four Seating Positions for Practice
Murshid's four postures: cross-legged (king/queen, center of universe), Cupid (archer seat for Zikr), lotus (sages), kneeling (before the beloved).
Part II, Chapter 6 · Urs Qutbuddin
Itisal — The Junction Practice (Ha × 11)
Intone Ha eleven times; trace sound from ground through tailbone to chest; junction between individual and cosmic being; daily after elemental breath.
Part II, Chapter 6 · Urs Qutbuddin
Chivalric Rules — 40 Rules (Iron / Copper / Silver / Gold)
40 ethical contemplations as personal pledges over 40 days; each rule a prism for self-refinement; Rules 1–10 Iron covered across Parts I and II.
Parts I / II · Pir Zia Inayat Khan / Urs Qutbuddin
Daily Practice Sequence (Mansur)
Complete ordered sequence: elemental breaths, invocation, Sabur/Wahhab, Subuhun/Quddusun, Fazl/Fattah, watchfulness/hosh dar dam, Qasab, Sky of Mind.

PRAYER MOVEMENTS

The prayers of the Inayatiyya — Saum, Salat, and Salawat — are accompanied by sacred body movements that embody the meaning of each phrase. These diagrams, from The Prayers of the Inayatiyya, illustrate the postures for Saum and Salat as practiced in the Suluk Global program.
